**v8.31.0** (Jun 19, 2026) — **New Critical Constraint: never add AI-authored comments inline in `recipe.yaml`; park new rationale in a bottom `# CFE comments` block for human triage.** **MINOR bump** — additive: 1 new authoring constraint; no code/test/schema/CLI change. User-established convention (the `recipes/ironcalc/recipe.yaml` body is the reference exemplar). **Goal**: keep recipe bodies free of AI comment clutter so the local recipe is a clean copy-paste source into a feedstock / staged-recipes PR, and submitted conda-forge recipes never inherit a pile of AI-generated inline comments. **Rule (two comment classes)**: (1) existing human / upstream-feedstock comments already in the body (e.g. podman-desktop's `# Node.js build environment`) STAY verbatim — removing them is a defect; (2) NEW comments an agent would add (rationale, gotcha tags `# G25 flatten` / `# load-bearing under pip_check`, license-pattern notes, python_min reasoning, BFP-fix notes) must NOT be inline — they go only in the bottom `# CFE comments` block, organized by recipe location (build / context / host / run / requirements / about / tests), where a human curates which to promote up into the submitted recipe. The functional schema-header comment stays at the top. Both the `# CFE metadata` and `# CFE comments` sections are CFE-local-only and stripped before any push. **Files touched**: `SKILL.md` (new "Never Add AI Comments Inline" Critical Constraint, after the schema-header one); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.30.1 → 8.31.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry); auto-memory `feedback_cfe_comments_at_bottom.md` + `MEMORY.md` index (cross-skill — affects how every recipe-authoring agent emits comments). **Pending**: `recipe-generator.py` to emit new rationale into the bottom block (flagged in SKILL.md); retroactive application to all recipes edited/created in the 2026-06-19 session (in progress, ironcalc first — already compliant). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.31.0.

**v8.30.1** (Jun 19, 2026) — **G2 correction + reference-doc About-section fix: `license_family` is deprecated-but-valid in v1, not "removed".** **PATCH bump** — doc correction; no code/schema/CLI change. Verified against the live `prefix-dev/recipe-format` schema (the `About` object has exactly 9 properties with `additionalProperties: false`: `homepage`, `repository`, `documentation`, `license`, `license_file`, **`license_family`**, `summary`, `description`, `prelink_message`) plus `conda_build.license_family.ensure_valid_license_family` and `conda_smithy.linter.lints.lint_license_family_should_be_valid`. (1) **G2 was wrong** — it listed `license_family` in the v0→v1 rename table as "*(removed; no replacement)*". It is neither removed nor a rename: it keeps its name and is a valid (deprecated) v1 `about:` field. It passes rattler-build schema validation AND conda-smithy lint provided its value is a recognized family (`ensure_valid_license_family` raises only on an unrecognized value; `lint_license_family_should_be_valid` fires only when `license_file` is absent, never on the field's presence). For modernization it should be omitted (deprecated; neither the CFE generator nor current grayskull emits it). Fixed the G2 symptom line, dropped the bogus rename row + added a clarifying note, and corrected the G20 cross-reference. (2) **`reference/recipe-yaml-reference.md` About section corrected** — annotated `license_family` as deprecated, **added the missing `prelink_message` field**, **removed `identifiers`** (not in the schema at all → `about.identifiers` is schema-invalid in v1), and added an authoritative note enumerating the complete 9-field set with `additionalProperties: false`. (3) **`extra:` analysis + reference-doc Extra section enhanced** — verified `extra:` is a free-form object (schema: *"a set of arbitrary values included in the package manifest"*, no `additionalProperties: false`); the only lint-enforced rules are `recipe-maintainers` (required, must be a non-empty list — `NoMaintainers`/`MaintainersMustBeList`, v0+v1) and `feedstock-name` (must not end with `-feedstock`). The unexpected-subsection lint (`lint_subheaders`) is gated `if recipe_version == 0`, so arbitrary `extra:` keys are **un-linted on v1** but draw an `UnexpectedSubsection` warning on v0 (conda-smithy's `FIELDS["extra"]` knows only `recipe-maintainers` + `feedstock-name`; conda_build's base is `{}`). Added `recipe-maintainers-emeritus` + the v0-vs-v1 lint nuance + a free-form note to the reference doc's Extra section. Surfaced mid-effort during the sole-maintainer feedstock-refresh (Wave 1) when the user asked for the complete `about:` and `extra:` field lists. **Files touched**: `SKILL.md` (G2 symptom + table + G20 cross-ref); `reference/recipe-yaml-reference.md` (About section); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.30.0 → 8.30.1); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.30.1.

**v8.30.0** (Jun 18, 2026) — **Batch autotick-PR-fix retro: 4 new gotchas (G31–G34) on existing-feedstock CI triage + fix mechanics.** **MINOR bump** — additive: 4 gotchas; no code/test/schema/CLI changes. From a 12-PR batch of failing `[bot-automerge]` autotick version-bump PRs (2026-06-17/18), each diagnosed, fixed locally-first, then maintainer-edit-pushed. **G31** — overriding `python_min` *upward on an existing feedstock* differs by format: v1 (`recipe.yaml`) needs a recipe-local `conda_build_config.yaml` + rerender because `context.python_min` does NOT propagate to `.ci_support` (verified empirically — `conda-smithy rerender` left it at 3.10; a local rattler-build that bypasses `.ci_support` honors context and masks the bug), while v0 (`meta.yaml`) uses `{% set python_min %}` which shadows the `.ci_support` variant directly (no CBC, no rerender). This is the existing-feedstock counterpart to the Python Version Policy's "declare in `context:`" guidance (which is for fresh staged-recipes submissions). **G32** — triaging autotick PRs: a flake-vs-real-fix signature catalog (transient/pre-build infra → `@conda-forge-admin, please restart ci`: `dispatch task is gone`/`runtime dropped the dispatch task`, `_Py_HashRandomization_Init: failed to get random numbers`, `IncompleteRead`/`Connection broken`, 503/`error sending request`; deterministic real fixes → edit: ImportError-on-stdlib-name, pip_check version mismatch, `BackendUnavailable`, `does not exist`/`no candidates`, linter float-parse) **plus the maintainer-edit push mechanic** — a `gh pr checkout` clone's `origin` is the *upstream* feedstock, not the bot fork, so a plain `git push` lands a stray branch on the canonical repo; push the fix to `https://github.com/regro-cf-autotick-bot/<feedstock>.git HEAD:<pr-head-branch>`. **G33** — local rattler-build of a v1 feedstock recipe shouldn't pass `.ci_support` as a variant config: its strict `channel_sources: [conda-forge]` excludes the just-built package from its own test solve (misleading `excluded due to strict channel priority` / `no candidates were found`); use the pinning CBC + default channel + auto-added output-dir instead. Includes the `conda search` not-found-listing misread trap — `  - <dep>==<X>` is a `PackagesNotFoundError` line, not a match. **G34** — `pkg_resources.declare_namespace` packages (`fs`/Pyfilesystem2 the canonical case) break under setuptools 81+ with `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'pkg_resources'` raised from the *dependency's* `__init__`; cap `setuptools <81` in the consuming recipe's run deps (durable fix belongs in the provider feedstock). **Batch outcome**: 4 pure flakes restarted (cocoindex/html-to-markdown/dlt/selectolax), 6 real fixes built+tested-locally then pushed (llms-py python_min 3.11; copilotkit ag-ui-langgraph bump; okta-jwt-verifier retry2→retry; fs.googledrivefs setuptools<81; wagtail-nav-menus poetry-core→hatchling; wagtail-sharing python_min 3.12 + version-quote), 2 blocked on prerequisite dep feedstocks (microsoft-kiota-bundle, collate-sqllineage — deferred per user). **Cross-skill auto-memory delta**: added `feedback_test_locally_before_push.md` (build+test every feedstock fix locally before maintainer-edit push). **Files touched**: `SKILL.md` (G31–G34); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.29.0 → 8.30.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.30.0.

**v8.29.0** (Jun 17, 2026) — **New gotcha G30 from the lyric-py staged-recipes submission (PR #33764).** **MINOR bump** — additive: 1 gotcha; no code/test changes. conda-forge's `protobuf` package is the Python bindings and ships NO `protoc` binary — Rust recipes whose `build.rs` runs `tonic-build`/`prost-build` need **`libprotobuf`** (`bin/protoc`) in `requirements.build`, not `protobuf`. The trap hides locally: a `libprotobuf` in the dev pixi/conda env leaks `bin/protoc` onto the build PATH so the broken recipe builds green, while hermetic CI (only declared build deps on PATH) fails on every platform with `Could not find protoc`. G30 documents the fix (`protobuf`→`libprotobuf`; protoc is a build-platform tool → belongs in `build:`), the optional `export PROTOC="$BUILD_PREFIX/bin/protoc"` fallback (not via `script.env:`, which doesn't shell-expand), and a generalizable hermetic-verification technique — hide the stray host tool (often a relative symlink `protoc -> protoc-NN.N.N`) and rebuild — plus the relative-symlink `[ -e ]` trap. Case: lyric-py PR #33764 failed `linux_64`+`osx_64` with `Could not find protoc`; fixed `protobuf`→`libprotobuf`, verified by hiding `.pixi/envs/local-recipes/bin/protoc` (a symlink → `protoc-33.5.0`) and rebuilding all 4 py-variants green. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.29.0.

**v8.28.0** (Jun 17, 2026) — **DB-GPT v0.8.0 7-output multi-output build-and-ship closeout retro: 4 new gotchas (G26–G29).** **MINOR bump** — additive: 4 gotchas + skill-TODO notes; no code/test changes. Drove `docs/specs/db-gpt-conda-forge.md` end-to-end via bmad-quick-dev — 5 prerequisite recipes + the 7-output DB-GPT recipe, all to green local build + `prepare_submission_branch` (6 fork branches pushed, no PRs opened per user). The lyric stack exercised two notable patterns confirmed working: `lyric-py` (cocoindex-class Rust+PyO3 built by `cd`-ing into a Cargo-**workspace subdir** `bindings/python/lyric-py`, protoc via `tonic-build`, `pyo3 generate-import-lib` handling the Windows import-lib, **NOT abi3** → per-Python build with plain `python` run-dep that conda's `python_abi` run-export pins automatically) and the 3 lyric-* workers (itkwasm vendor-the-blob: noarch:python wrapping a pre-built `.wasm`, LICENSE vendored in-recipe, a `.wasm`-presence script test). **G26** — loosening upstream `==` pins to `>=` needs a build-time source-pyproject `sed` (`name==N`→`name>=N`) when `pip_check: true`, because the wheel METADATA bakes in the `==` and pip_check enforces it (mirror image of G24); the spec's FR-2/S10 assumed loosening the conda run-deps alone sufficed — it didn't. **G27** — a top-level `import` in a split package can eagerly pull a sibling's submodule whose deps are only declared under an extra (`dbgpt_client`→`dbgpt_ext.rag`→`dbgpt.rag.knowledge`→`bs4`); probe the import closure in the surviving `test_env` and add only what it needs (here: exactly `beautifulsoup4`). **G28** — an external dep's broken `dist-info` version (conda-forge `pdfminer.six` reports `0.0.0` while its conda version is correctly `20251230`) false-fails `pip_check` for any exact-pinning dependent (`pdfplumber` pins `pdfminer.six==20251230`); no in-recipe fix → disable `pip_check` on the single affected output, documented, keeping it on the other six. **G29** — multi-output checkers are top-level-only: `optimize_recipe` TEST-001 false-positives and `check_dependencies` returns empty/empty (a silent false-negative) on `recipe:`+`outputs:` recipes — trust conda-smithy+rattler lint for structure and verify deps via a flattened throwaway recipe. G25 (extras-flatten) held: the 68-dep `dbgpt-app` union + `httpx[socks]`→`socksio` + dropped `qianfan` all verified, and the only `pip_check` miss across 78 deps was the external G28 false positive. Also re-confirmed operationally: `get_build_summary` false-negative ("unknown/crashed" on success — trust the artifact + cleaned work dir) and the zombie-watcher trap (`kill -0` reports a defunct build as alive; break on `ps` STAT `Z`). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.28.0.

**v8.27.0** (Jun 17, 2026) — **DB-GPT multi-output spec audit retro: new gotcha G25 (conda has no "extras" — flatten every `pkg[extra]` upstream dep into `run:`, and resolve each extra to its actual conda package, which may be renamed)**. **MINOR bump** — additive: 1 new gotcha; no breaking changes, no schema or CLI changes. **What landed.** **G25 — Conda has no "extras" mechanism.** Two interlocking facts. (1) PEP 508 extras (`pkg[extra]`) are pip-only — installing `pkg[extra]` pulls `pkg` plus the deps under `pkg`'s `[project.optional-dependencies].extra`; conda has no equivalent, so every `pkg[extra]` in an upstream dep list must be flattened into `requirements.run`. In a multi-output recipe, `${{ pin_subpackage('sibling', exact=True) }}` does NOT pull the sibling's extras — the consuming output must carry them itself. (2) An extra's marker name ≠ the conda package it resolves to — `httpx[socks]` pulls `socksio` (per httpx's pyproject), NOT a package called `httpx-socks` (a different PyPI project that isn't on conda-forge). `pip_check: true` is the enforcement mechanism: it reads the installed wheel's `Requires-Dist: <dep>; extra == "..."` lines and fails when an activated extra's deps are absent — loudly in the building feedstock, or only in a downstream's CI (the builder's own pip_check covers just the package being built, per G24). Fix: for each `pkg[extra]`, read upstream's `[project.optional-dependencies]`, union base + activated extras, map each to its conda name (G10 four-spelling; watch the extra→renamed-package trap), list the union in `run:`, and drop extras no output activates. Detection helpers (grep the extras-bracket across pyproject files; `curl pypi.org/pypi/<dep>/json` to read the `extra ==` markers) are included in the gotcha. Proposed optimizer check `DEP-006` tracked as a TODO (not shipped). **Live case study — DB-GPT v0.8.0 multi-output spec audit** (`docs/specs/db-gpt-conda-forge.md`). The `dbgpt-app` output depends on `dbgpt[client,cli,agent,simple_framework,framework,code,proxy_openai,proxy_tongyi,proxy_zhipuai]` + `dbgpt-ext[rag,storage_chromadb]` where `dbgpt`/`dbgpt-ext` are sibling outputs in the same recipe (built without extras). The draft spec's run-dep list missed ~50 of the flattened **68** external deps; pip_check would have failed at CI. Two extras-resolution traps caught: `httpx[socks]`→`socksio` (spec guessed the nonexistent `httpx-socks`), and `qianfan` listed as required when it lives only in the non-activated `proxy_qianfan` extra (dropped). **Counter-factual**: had G25 been in the skill at intake, the flatten + extra-resolution would have been a recipe-skeleton checklist walk instead of an audit finding; for any multi-output recipe over a uv/poetry workspace with cross-member extras (the DB-GPT / lyric / langchain-monorepo class), ~1 full CI iteration saved — a flattened-deps `pip_check` failure is among the slowest to diagnose because it can surface only downstream. **Files touched**: `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/SKILL.md` (G25 gotcha section); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.26.0 → 8.27.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). The DB-GPT spec corrections themselves landed in `docs/specs/db-gpt-conda-forge.md` (same-session audit pass, separate from the skill change). **No cross-skill auto-memory deltas** — finding is CFE-internal. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.27.0.

**v8.26.0** (Jun 17, 2026) — **graphifyy osx-arm64 fanout retro: 2 new gotchas + 1 sub-rule clarification (G23 cmd.exe `^`-escape trap; G24 conda-label-vs-dist-info version mismatch; "Sub-workflow: Updating an existing recipe" 4th bullet on upstream-declared upper bounds being load-bearing under `pip_check`)**. **MINOR bump** — additive: 2 new gotchas + 1 cross-cutting clarification in sub-workflow guidance; no breaking changes; no schema or CLI changes. **What landed.** **G23 — Inline `sed` + `powershell` in `build.script` hits cmd.exe escape hell.** Symptom: a recipe needs to rewrite something in upstream's source tree at build time (typically pyproject.toml version, a hardcoded path); author writes `sed -i ...` on Unix + `powershell -Command "(Get-Content X) -replace ..."` on Windows. Unix passes; Windows fails — the regex either silently produces the wrong result OR rattler-build exits 255. Cmd ate the `^` from `[^"]` in the regex character class (cmd treats `^` as escape char outside double-quoted strings; the 4-layer YAML→cmd→PS→regex quoting chain strips it before powershell sees it). Fix: add `sed` to `requirements.build` (`m2-sed` on Windows) and use a single inline `sed -i 's/^version = .*/version = "${{ version }}"/' pyproject.toml` line that works on every platform. Anti-pattern to avoid: `powershell -Command "...regex with ^..."` — too many escaping layers. Escape hatch when sed isn't enough (multi-line, TOML structure): check in a small Python helper file under `recipe/` and invoke via `${{ PYTHON }} ${RECIPE_DIR}/helper.py` (Unix) + `"%PYTHON%" "%RECIPE_DIR%\helper.py"` (Win) with `$PKG_VERSION` for the version. **G24 — Conda label ≠ wheel `dist-info` version when upstream's `pyproject.toml` hardcodes a placeholder.** Symptom: a feedstock's own tests pass (`pip_check` only checks the package being built, not its dependents); a downstream feedstock pinning the package with an upper bound (e.g. `<pkg> >=0.7,<0.9`) fails CI with `<downstream> requires <pkg><0.9,>=0.7, but you have <pkg> 0.0.1` — even though `mamba list` shows the right version per conda metadata. Cause: `pip check` reads each installed package's wheel-bundled `dist-info/METADATA` `Version:` line, not conda repodata. When upstream's `pyproject.toml [project].version` is a placeholder that was never bumped to match the tag scheme (e.g. `alex-pinkus/tree-sitter-swift` hardcoded `version = "0.0.1"` across all 0.7.x tags), the conda label is correct but the wheel dist-info is poisoned. Fix: rewrite `pyproject.toml`'s `version` field at build time via G23's canonical pattern (`sed -i` with `m2-sed`). Idempotent — if upstream ever fixes their pyproject, the sed runs against the correct value and is a no-op. Also file the upstream issue. Detection helper (single python one-liner) included in the gotcha for proactive surveys. Scope: most common in tree-sitter language grammars (auto-generated parser.c + version-neglected Python binding); also applicable to language-server-protocol bindings, generated wrappers, and monorepo subpackages where only the parent is version-tracked. **Sub-workflow refinement — "Special-case categorizations" table extended with a 4th bullet: upstream-declared upper bounds on `run:` deps are LOAD-BEARING when `pip_check: true` is in the test block.** The existing DEP-002 guidance already noted "upstream-explicit upper bounds are widely accepted by reviewers"; the new sub-rule makes the enforcement mechanism explicit. If the recipe declares only `tree-sitter-julia >=0.23`, conda solver picks `0.25.0` (newest compatible), pip check then reads graphifyy's bundled wheel constraint `tree-sitter-julia<0.25` and FAILS the test loudly. The silent failure is worse — a maintainer who disables `pip_check` to "fix" it ships an install where pip-level deps disagree, and users hit ABI / API breaks at runtime. **Decision rule**: drop upper bounds ONLY when they were speculative (over-cautious generator-added); MIRROR them from upstream's `pyproject.toml [project.dependencies]` when present. `bot.run_deps_from_wheel: true` keeps them synced on autotick bumps with near-zero maintenance cost. **Live case study — graphifyy osx-arm64 fanout** (Jun 16-17, 2026; conda-forge/graphifyy-feedstock#8 + 22 platform-expansion PRs + 8 canonical-conda-forge.yml-sweep PRs + conda-forge/tree-sitter-swift-feedstock#5 for the dist-info fix). Scope: make graphifyy installable on osx-arm64 by shipping platform expansion across 22 tree-sitter-* dep feedstocks. Three iterations on graphifyy PR #8 itself: (1) shipped with lower-bound-only run-deps + 17-entry `run_constrained` extras → pip_check failed at CI on `tree-sitter-julia 0.25.0` violating upstream's `<0.25`; (2) restored upper bounds across all 26 tree-sitter-* run-deps → pip_check passed locally but failed at CI on `tree-sitter-swift 0.0.1` violating upstream's `>=0.7` (the dist-info mismatch surfaced from latent — `tree-sitter-swift` had shipped on conda-forge with wrong dist-info for the entire 0.7.x lifetime); (3) opened separate fix on tree-sitter-swift-feedstock#5 with G23/G24 pattern (`sed`+helper + dynamic tag), waited for repodata propagation, re-ran graphifyy PR #8 CI → SUCCESS → merged. **Empirical result**: 22 platform-expansion PRs merged in ~14h (Wave A through C) + 8 canonical-conda-forge.yml-retrofit PRs (S-F6) + tree-sitter-swift dist-info fix + graphifyy v0.8.40 with 17-entry run_constrained extras all shipped end-to-end. **Counter-factual**: had G23 + G24 + the upper-bounds sub-rule been in the skill at intake, iterations (1)+(2) on graphifyy PR #8 would have been collapsed (still would have needed iteration (3) for tree-sitter-swift, but the discovery would have been at recipe-edit time, not CI-debug time). Per future analogous fanout: ~1-2 iteration cycles saved on the downstream PR + zero CI-burn on the dist-info-blind first push. **Files touched**: `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/SKILL.md` (G23 + G24 gotcha sections; sub-workflow categorizations table 4th bullet); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.25.0 → 8.26.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry); `docs/specs/graphifyy-osx-arm64-fanout.md` (Wave F § S-E1 retro section). **No cross-skill auto-memory deltas** — all findings are CFE-internal. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.26.0.

**v8.25.0** (Jun 15, 2026) — **cocoindex PR #11 closeout: abi3 matrix-collapse pattern documented end-to-end (2 new gotchas G21/G22, new `reference/abi3-matrix-collapse.md`, cross-links from `python-min-policy.md` rule #7, gh OAuth `workflow`-scope note in `feedstock-maintenance.md`, fat-LTO-Windows-myth bust in `ci-troubleshooting.md`)**. **MINOR bump** — additive: 2 new gotchas + 1 new reference doc + 4 cross-cutting edits; no breaking changes; no schema or CLI changes. **What landed.** **G21 — conda-smithy mis-aligns the zip-keyed `is_python_min` flag when `python_min` is overridden upward.** Symptom: a Rust+PyO3 recipe with `pyo3 abi3-py311` + recipe-local `conda_build_config.yaml: python_min: "3.11"` + canonical tree-sitter-pattern `skip: is_abi3 and not is_python_min` — rerender succeeds, regenerated `.ci_support/*.yaml` shows `python_min: '3.11'` AND `is_python_min: [true]` AND `python: [3.10.* *_cpython]` simultaneously. The build runs against py3.10 and fails with `cocoindex requires Python >=3.11`. Cause: smithy's `variant_algebra.variant_add` unions pinning's python axis with the recipe-local CBC python_min but doesn't shift the zip-key's `true` position to match. Fix: use the rustworkx-pattern skip rule `not (match(python, python_min ~ ".*") and is_abi3)` which filters on the variant's `python_min` value directly via jinja string-concat (`~`) + `match()` glob, sidestepping the zip-key entirely. **G22 — Recipe-local CBC `python:` override using `*_cpython` suffix crashes smithy on py3.13+.** Symptom: `ValueError: '3.13.* *_cpython' is not in list` in `variant_algebra._version_order` during conda-forge-rerendering-service execution. Cause: conda-forge-pinning's python axis uses different suffix tags per Python version (`*_cpython` for 3.10–3.12; `*_cp313` for 3.13; `*_cp314` for 3.14; plus `*_cp313t`/`*_cp314t` for freethreading). The `_version_order` helper builds an ordering list from those exact strings and rejects entries that don't match. Fix: don't override `python:` axis at all — override only `python_min` and use the G21 fix's skip rule. **`reference/abi3-matrix-collapse.md`** (NEW) — full pattern documentation: two skip-rule variants (A = `is_abi3 and not is_python_min` for abi3 min = pinning min; B = `not (match(python, python_min ~ ".*") and is_abi3)` for abi3 min > pinning min) with feedstock citations for each (tree-sitter family vs rustworkx + cocoindex), `python.version_independent: ${{ is_abi3 }}` companion mechanics, `python-abi3` host dep, cross-Python `[python_min.*, "*"]` test pattern, abi3audit step with binary-path lookup table per build backend (maturin default / maturin `module-name` / setuptools-rust / Py_LIMITED_API), common-failures table (6 entries). **Cross-cuts**: `python-min-policy.md` adds rule #7 (override python_min upward for abi3); `feedstock-maintenance.md` "When to Rerender vs. Edit" adds "Merging Rerender PRs — gh CLI Needs `workflow` OAuth Scope" subsection (4-step diagnosis: `gh auth status` → refresh OR new PAT → `GH_TOKEN` env-var-vs-keyring precedence trap → PR-draft-state check); `ci-troubleshooting.md` Windows section adds "Fat-LTO on Windows for large Rust+PyO3 packages" subsection refuting the 6h-timeout folklore (empirical: cocoindex 1.0.10 win_64 leg 9 min 45 s with fat LTO + STRIP + 600+ crates including tree-sitter × 70 grammars). **Live case study — cocoindex PR #11** (https://github.com/conda-forge/cocoindex-feedstock/pull/11). Scope: attempt fat LTO + STRIP on Rust+PyO3 feedstock. Three iterations needed: (1) `is_abi3 and not is_python_min` + 4-entry CBC `python:` override with `*_cpython` suffix everywhere → smithy rerender crashed with G22 ValueError; (2) simplified to CBC `python_min: "3.11"` only — smithy collapsed matrix correctly but mis-aligned `python: [3.10.*]` → builds failed with `requires Python >=3.11`; (3) switched to `not (match(python, python_min ~ ".*") and is_abi3)` — single py3.11 variant per platform, abi3audit clean (0 ABI version mismatches), 8/8 CI legs green. **Empirical result**: 4 builds/platform → 1 build/platform; linux_64 wall ~12 min → ~3 min; osx_arm64 wall ~14 min → ~4 min; win_64 fat-LTO 9 min 45 s (was previously gated by the "do not enable fat LTO" recipe comment); `.conda` size 6.72 MiB × 1 instead of × 4. **Counter-factual**: had G21 + G22 + `abi3-matrix-collapse.md` been in the skill at intake, the matrix-collapse application on cocoindex would have been a 1-iteration recipe edit; this effort took 3 push/rerender cycles end-to-end. Per future Rust+PyO3 abi3 feedstock: ~2 push-iteration cycles saved (~30-60 min of operator wall-time + ~30-60 min of CI wall-time per iteration). **Token-hygiene note** also landed in `feedstock-maintenance.md` — `gho_...` tokens exposed in any session transcript should be rotated at github.com/settings/tokens. **Files touched**: `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/SKILL.md` (G21 + G22 gotcha sections); `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/reference/abi3-matrix-collapse.md` (NEW, ~150 lines); `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/reference/python-min-policy.md` (rule #7 + References cross-link); `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/guides/feedstock-maintenance.md` ("Merging Rerender PRs" subsection); `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/guides/ci-troubleshooting.md` ("Fat-LTO on Windows" subsection); `recipes/cocoindex/recipe.yaml` (final canonical state — matches PR #11 head 9d164ac); `recipes/cocoindex/conda_build_config.yaml` (NEW minimal `python_min: "3.11"`); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.24.0 → 8.25.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.25.0.

**v8.24.0** (Jun 14, 2026) — **python-confluent-kafka v0→v1 migration closeout: new gotcha G20 (silently-ignored `{{ X }}` substitutions in v1 recipes), Migration Discipline subsection in SKILL.md + 5-point expansion in `guides/migration.md`**. **MINOR bump** — additive: 1 new gotcha (G20) and 1 new SKILL.md Migration Protocol subsection + 1 new `guides/migration.md` section ("Migration Discipline"). No breaking changes; no schema or CLI changes. **What landed.** **G20 — v0 jinja `{{ X }}` syntax in v1 recipe.yaml is silently rendered as literal text.** Third entry in the v0→v1 silent-substitution class alongside G2 (about-fields) and G3 (`py < N` + `# [unix]`/`# [win]` selectors). `validate_recipe`, `rattler-build lint`, and `conda-smithy lint` all pass because bare `{{ … }}` is well-formed YAML; the failure surfaces at build/install time as `command not found: {{` (script context), `cannot parse spec '>={{ version }}'` (requirements context), or as a wrongly-applied patch (selector context). Detection: `grep -nE '(^|[^$])\{\{[^}]+\}\}' recipes/<name>/recipe.yaml` — any hit on a v1 recipe is a silent-failure candidate. Documented optimizer follow-up `JIN-001` is tracked as skill TODO (not yet shipped). **Migration Discipline** — five points captured at the SKILL.md level (one-liners with pointer) and the `guides/migration.md` level (full expansion with empirical case for each): (1) `package.name:` MUST match the conda-forge feedstock identity, not the local folder name (e.g. `recipes/confluent-kafka-python/` migrating a feedstock that ships as `python-confluent-kafka` MUST emit `package.name: python-confluent-kafka`); verify via `lookup_feedstock(pkg_name=<canonical-name>)` before pushing. (2) Bump `build.number` on same-version v0→v1 swap (typically 0→1) — conda solver needs distinct hashes between legacy `_0` and migration `_1` artifacts of the same `<name>-<version>`. (3) Stash `meta.yaml` aside during local validation (`mv meta.yaml meta.yaml.bak`), don't pre-delete — keeps STD-002 silent and the v0 reference available; drop on the fork branch (where v0 is genuinely retired), restore in the local mirror until PR merges. (4) `conda_build_tool: rattler-build` MUST ship paired with `conda_install_tool: pixi` in the same `conda-forge.yml` — the canonical 2026 declaration; both go in the same PR that drops `meta.yaml`; **always** request `@conda-forge-admin, please rerender` on the PR (CI scripts need regenerating to invoke rattler-build instead of conda-build). (5) `pip_check: true` on first-time enablement may surface "new" runtime deps — older v0 recipes that ran `test.imports:` only never caught upstream's PEP-508 transitive deps; expect to discover them on migration and ship unconditionally in `run:` rather than gating into v1 selectors for single deps. **Live case study — python-confluent-kafka PR #127** (https://github.com/conda-forge/python-confluent-kafka-feedstock/pull/127). Scope: v0→v1 migration of an existing feedstock at the same upstream version (2.14.2; the autotick bot's last bump was the day before). Workflow: (a) audited the hand-rolled `recipes/confluent-kafka-python/recipe.yaml` against the SKILL.md gotchas + canonical patterns; (b) caught the three G20 bugs (`{{ PYTHON }}`, `librdkafka >={{ version }}` ×2, `# [win]` patch selector) by manual inspection before the build ran; (c) collapsed the v0 list-form `build.script:` entries into v1 `if: unix / then: | ... else: | ...` blocks per G1 (env vars don't carry across script-list entries); (d) preserved the upstream Windows patch + pypy skip after verifying against upstream `setup.py @ v2.14.2` and the linked GitHub issue; (e) ran local rattler-build → `pip_check: true` surfaced upstream's `typing-extensions ; python_version < "3.11"` runtime dep; added `typing_extensions` unconditionally to `run:`; (f) green build across py310/311/312/313; (g) mirrored to fork checkout, dropped `meta.yaml`, added `conda_build_tool: rattler-build` + `conda_install_tool: pixi` to `conda-forge.yml`, pushed branch + opened PR + requested rerender; (h) PR CI went 39/39 green (linux_64 ×6 / linux_aarch64 ×6 / linux_ppc64le ×6 / osx_64 ×6 / osx_arm64 ×6 / win_64 ×6 + linter + aggregator) on the first run, no iterations needed. **Counter-factual**: had G20 + Migration Discipline been in the skill at intake, the migration audit would have been a checklist walk instead of a 5-minute manual eyeball; net time saved per future v0→v1 migration ≈ 5 minutes of audit + 1-2 avoided CI iterations (~20-40 min on the slowest emulated platform) when the bare-`{{ }}` substitutions are caught pre-build. **Files touched**: `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/SKILL.md` (G20 gotcha + Migration Discipline subsection in Migration Protocol); `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/guides/migration.md` (new "Migration Discipline" section, 5 points × ~30 lines each); `recipes/confluent-kafka-python/recipe.yaml` (v1 canonical shape, build.number: 1, +typing_extensions); `recipes/confluent-kafka-python/conda-forge.yml` (new local mirror; conda_build_tool: rattler-build + conda_install_tool: pixi); fork branch `migrate-recipe-to-v1` on `rxm7706/python-confluent-kafka-feedstock` (recipe.yaml replaces meta.yaml + conda-forge.yml extension); PR #127 opened against `conda-forge/python-confluent-kafka-feedstock`; `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.23.0 → 8.24.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). **v8.23.0** (Jun 14, 2026) — **Cocoindex PR #9 platform-expansion closeout: two new Rust+PyO3-on-Windows gotchas (G18, G19), reference doc 5× rewrite, gen-yml-reference auto-doc generator, new feedstock-platform-expansion guide + parameterized spec**. **MINOR bump** — additive across SKILL.md (2 new gotchas), `reference/conda-forge-yml-reference.md` (116 → 627 lines: 4-key interaction matrix + 4 canonical shapes + Azure resource tuning + `bot.inspection` 7-value enum + `noarch_platforms` justification rule), 2 new auto-generated `reference/*-full.md` docs from upstream JSON Schemas, new `guides/feedstock-platform-expansion.md`, new parameterized `docs/specs/feedstock-platform-expansion.md`. **What landed.** **G18 — `workflow_settings.store_build_artifacts: true` (unscoped) crashes Windows Azure builds via 7z + INetCache ACLs.** `Run Windows build` succeeds and produces the `.conda`; the next `Prepare conda build artifacts` task fails because 7z archives `D:\bld\bld\rattler-build_<pkg>_*\.work.pending-rm-*\AppData\Local\Microsoft\Windows\INetCache\Content.IE5` which has restricted Windows ACLs. Fix: scope to non-Windows via conditional list form (`platform: [linux_64, linux_aarch64, osx_64, osx_arm64]`). Upstream durable fix (out of feedstock scope, deferred): add `-xr!*INetCache*` to `conda-forge/conda-forge-ci-setup`'s `.scripts/create_conda_build_artifacts.bat`. Empirically `gh search code "store_build_artifacts" path:conda-forge.yml` returns ZERO hits — the conda-forge ecosystem default is "don't archive on any platform"; setting it at all is unusual. **G19 — Windows `pip install` fails `Error reading output: ... stream did not contain valid UTF-8`.** rattler-build captures pip stdout and UTF-8-decodes it; Windows console codepage (cp1252) breaks the decode when cargo/maturin/pip emit non-ASCII (license names with accents, em-dashes in descriptions). Fix: `PYTHONUTF8: "1"` in `build.script.env`. G19 also lands the FULL canonical Rust env block as the standard pattern: `CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_STRIP: symbols` (conda-forge default for ALL Rust builds per v8.9.1 retro — 30-50% binary size reduction) + commented `#CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_LTO: fat` with "time out issues" institutional knowledge note. **Discipline rule** (codified in G19): "the canonical env block is the default, not opt-in" — when fixing PYTHONUTF8 alone, ship STRIP and the commented LTO comment together; the single-line PYTHONUTF8 patch is a "Surgical Changes" misreading. xorq-datafusion (the user's other Rust+PyO3 feedstock) is the live reference recipe for this shape. **Reference doc rewrite.** `reference/conda-forge-yml-reference.md` grew from 116 lines to 627 lines. New "Four-key matrix" subsection explains how `provider` × `build_platform` × `noarch_platforms` × `test` interact (each-without-the-others-misconfigures-a-leg). Four canonical YAML shapes: (1) compiled-minimal-expansion (cocoindex post-this-spec), (2) compiled-multi-arch with cross-build hosts (pixi-feedstock), (3) noarch-multi-arch with emulated tests (apache-superset), (4) comprehensive Azure-tuned with docstring-style inline comments on every key. New "Azure resource tuning" subsection covers `azure.force`/`free_disk_space`/`max_parallel`/`settings_*` (promoted from a single Less-common table row). New "`bot.inspection` 7-value enum table" (`hint`/`hint-all`/`hint-source`/`hint-grayskull`/`update-source`/`update-grayskull`/`update-all`); `update-grayskull` documented as modern default. New `conda_install_tool`/`conda_build_tool`/`conda_build.pkg_format`/`error_overlinking`/`conda_forge_output_validation`/`check_solvable`/`run_deps_from_wheel` reference entries. Strong **"`noarch_platforms` only when platform-conditional runtime behavior"** rule landed with vizro-ai-class counter-example: a pure-Python visualization helper does NOT need `[linux_64, win_64, osx_64, osx_arm64, linux_ppc64le, linux_aarch64]` — Windows-leg flakes from antivirus/file-lock without changing the shipped noarch artifact. Stop-and-justify gate added before Shape 3 to prevent reflex copy-paste. Old "Not exhaustive" disclaimer replaced with explicit four-source roadmap (curated subset / exhaustive auto-generated / canonical upstream / concrete templates). Deprecation notice: `azure.store_build_artifacts` → `workflow_settings.store_build_artifacts` (per schema text "Deprecated. Use workflow_settings.store_build_artifacts instead"); schema accepts bool OR list of conditional `{provider/os/platform, value}` objects. **gen-yml-reference auto-doc generator.** New `scripts/gen_yml_reference.py` (280 lines canonical impl) + thin wrapper at `.claude/scripts/conda-forge-expert/gen_yml_reference.py` + `pixi run -e local-recipes gen-yml-reference` task + SCRIPTS list entry in `tests/meta/test_all_scripts_runnable.py`. Fetches upstream JSON Schemas (`conda-forge/conda-smithy/main/conda_smithy/data/conda-forge.json` + `prefix-dev/recipe-format/main/schema.json`), walks `$defs`/`anyOf`/`oneOf`/`allOf`/`$ref` recursively, emits per-key tables with type/default/description/enum into `reference/conda-forge-yml-reference-full.md` (864 lines, 45 top-level keys + all `$defs`) and `reference/recipe-yaml-reference-full.md` (686 lines). Idempotent; supports air-gapped mode via `--schema-file target=path`. Curated docs cross-link to auto-generated full docs. **New `guides/feedstock-platform-expansion.md`** (338 lines) — timeless workflow guide for the dual-goal "refresh local-recipes mirror + expand build matrix on existing feedstock" workflow. Three waves: (A) sync fork + diff-before-apply local mirror to latest upstream + native build verify, (B) clone feedstock + edit conda-forge.yml + smithy rerender + cross-target diagnostic builds, (C) commit + push + DRAFT PR + operator-confirm gates (S10 + S12 mandatory) + closeout retro. **v8.22.2** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Live-verification of v8.22.0 wrapper split on a real `bootstrap-data --profile admin` run, plus closeout retro**. **PATCH bump** — documentation only; no code or test changes. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the v8.22.0 effort closes out with a live end-to-end verification run + retro. **Live-verification result** (2026-06-13, warm-cache admin profile, ~17 min wall-clock end-to-end): Bootstrap summary printed **11 ✓ lines** with no `✗` or `⚠`, exit code 0. The 4 v8.22.0 sub-step lines rendered exactly as designed — `✓ cf-atlas-core` (331.3 s; B → B.5 → B.6 → C → C.5 → D → O → P → Q → R → S → E → E.5 → G → G' → H → J → L → M in canonical PHASES order), `✓ cf-atlas-F` (300.3 s via s3-parquet — cold parquet read on this run; warm-cache runs hit the ~30 s target), `✓ cf-atlas-K` (1.3 s — TTL-skipped because the previous run's GraphQL batch covered everything within the TTL window), `✓ cf-atlas-N` (1.6 s — 4 maintainer feedstocks refreshed, within the 3,600 s ceiling). The aggregate `✓ cf-atlas-build` row rendered alongside the 4 sub-step rows, matching the v8.22.0 design ("the bootstrap summary still prints a single `cf-atlas-build` row alongside the 4 sub-step rows so existing log-scrapers don't break"). **§ 10 (o) ordering invariant empirically validated**: Phase J produced 297,274 cf-graph edges from Phase E's `cf-graph.tar.gz` cache — would have been 0 if J had run before E. Confirms the v8.22.0 implementer's choice to iterate canonical PHASES order minus the skip set inside `core` (rather than user-supplied order) preserves the E → J prerequisite chain on a real channel-wide run. **Bonus dedup-on-redundant-call validated**: `bootstrap_data.py`'s outer Phase N step (the legacy `gh-phase-n` invocation) detected that the v8.22.0 split had already run Phase N inside `cf-atlas-N` and emitted `ⓘ Phase N already ran inside the cf_atlas build step (PHASE_N_ENABLED was in env via --profile, or v8.22.0 split). Skipping the redundant Phase N invocation.` — the dedup guard introduced in the v8.22.0 sub-agent's `_step_cf_atlas_split` orchestrator handles the env-propagation interaction correctly. **Phase F note**: this run measured Phase F at 300 s via s3-parquet (cold parquet on this admin profile's first run since the v8.18.1+ rolling-cache reset). The v8.22.0 CHANGELOG TL;DR estimated "~83 min serial via API or seconds via s3-parquet" — the ~5 min cold-parquet number falls comfortably inside the 7,200 s sub-step budget but is worth noting for future Phase F sub-step timeout tuning (the 7,200 s default has ~24× slack on cold-parquet days, ~240× on warm days). Not actioned in v8.22.2 (tuning down would erode the safety margin for a legitimately slow Phase F day; the existing budget is correctly conservative). **Retro outcome**: **no skill changes; verified existing guidance held for: v8.22.0 wrapper structural fix**. The two § 10 sub-rules landed by v8.22.1 ((n) wrapper-timeout false-negatives + (o) phase-ordering invariants) both held on the live run — (n) by construction (4 sub-step ✓ lines printed instead of one monolithic ✓), (o) by Phase J's 297k-edge result. No new findings; the v8.22.0 → v8.22.1 → v8.22.2 sequence is the v8.16.5 P2 carryover fully closed. **Counter-factual**: had this live-verification not run, the v8.22.0 ship would remain "verified by 30 unit tests" only — the unit tests cover the orchestrator's argv emission, timeout propagation, soft/hard failure semantics, and `--skip` / `--only` flag handling, but not the live-runner integration where bootstrap_data + conda_forge_atlas + pixi + cf-graph all interact. The live run closed that gap. **Discipline note (lessons for future wrapper-class refactors)**: a live end-to-end run on the target persona profile is the cheapest possible step-04-equivalent for orchestration-only refactors that skip the BMAD adversarial-review path per § 10 (i). v8.22.0 was directly shipped without adversarial review (correctly — no schema, no multi-table aggregation, no new provenance label); the gap was that "no adversarial review" meant the implementer's integration claim was test-suite-only until v8.22.2. **Discipline rule**: for orchestration-only refactors that ship without adversarial review, run a live end-to-end on at least one persona profile before declaring the effort done (the v8.22.0 → v8.22.2 sequence is the template — direct ship for the change, live-verify for the closeout). This is now § 10 (p) candidate guidance — promote to a formal sub-rule next time a wrapper-class refactor surfaces. **Files touched**: `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.22.1 → 8.22.2). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.22.2.

**v8.22.1** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Retro deltas from the v8.22.0 wrapper structural fix closeout**. **PATCH bump** — documentation only; no code or test changes. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the v8.22.0 closeout retro surfaced two durable engineering disciplines that landed as new sub-rules in `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10. **(n) Wrapper-timeout false-negatives are a structural defect, not a tuning problem.** v8.16.6 raised the `bootstrap-data` cf-atlas wrapper timeout from 7,200 s → 14,400 s to mitigate a wrapper-level false-negative: `bootstrap-data --profile admin` printed `✗ cf-atlas-build` while the Python subprocess kept running and finished cleanly. Raising the timeout only widens the slack window before the false-negative recurs — it doesn't fix the underlying defect that one operator-facing ✓/✗ aggregates ~21 phases under one wrapper, hiding which phase actually slipped past the wall clock when individual phase durations span 100× (Phase F's s3-parquet ~30 s vs. Phase K's sustained-rate ~75 min). v8.22.0 fixed it structurally by splitting the wrapper into 4 sub-steps each with its own timeout + independent ✓/✗ reporting. **Discipline rule**: when a wrapper around N phases produces a single boolean exit code while individual phase durations vary by 100×, the wrapper's "did it succeed" semantics are degenerate. Raise the timeout once to stop the symptom (v8.16.6-class mitigation buys time), then split the wrapper (v8.22.0-class structural fix). Always keep a legacy escape hatch (`BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_TIMEOUT=14400` restores the v8.16.6 single-subprocess behavior) for operators with log-scrapers or monitors keyed on the old single-row summary shape — the escape hatch is cheap to maintain (one env-var check + one fallback branch) and saves the cross-org coordination cost of a breaking change to summary output. **(o) Phase-ordering invariants survive sub-step splits only if you preserve canonical ordering inside each sub-step.** v8.22.0's 4-sub-step split (`core` / `F` / `K` / `N`) had to preserve the canonical PHASES execution order INSIDE the `core` sub-step: B → B.5 → B.6 → C → C.5 → D → O → P → Q → R → S → E → E.5 → G → G' → H → J → L → M. Phase J (which reads `cf-graph.tar.gz` populated by Phase E) MUST run after Phase E within the same sub-step, or it silently produces zero rows. Two new operator flags shipped with v8.22.0 (`--skip PHASES`, `--only PHASES`) expose phase selection to the operator; the implementation preserves operator-specified order under `--only` (the operator is explicit), but iterates canonical PHASES order minus the skip set under `--skip` so the safe default holds when the operator doesn't reorder. **Discipline rule**: in any phase-orchestration refactor that adds operator-facing phase-selection flags, the canonical PHASES list is the source of truth for ordering UNLESS the operator's flag explicitly opts out. A wrapper-split refactor doesn't introduce new schema or tables, but it can silently violate phase prerequisites by reordering — verify ordering invariants in tests that seed Phase-E-output and assert Phase J reads it, not just by inspection of the dispatcher list. The `test_cmd_build_only_preserves_listed_order` / `test_cmd_build_skip_excludes_phases` pair in `tests/unit/test_conda_forge_atlas_build.py` is the v8.22.0 template for this discipline. **What this retro does NOT land**: no auto-memory entry (both findings stayed in atlas-engineering scope — no cross-skill BMAD↔CFE rule); no v8.22.0 entry amendment (immutable-history per the v8.15.1 erratum discipline; v8.22.0 retains the original wording). **Counter-factual**: if (n) and (o) had been part of the skill at v8.16.5 retro intake, the wrapper false-negative would have been called out as a structural defect at first surfacing rather than mitigated via timeout-bump-then-defer (one fewer round-trip); the v8.22.0 implementer would have known to verify canonical PHASES order inside the core sub-step from spec intake rather than discovering it during step-04 review. Two step-04 findings × ~15 min triage saved on the next 2-3 wrapper-split-style efforts; ROI break-even on this retro entry's ~10 min of codification. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.22.1.

**v8.22.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Wrapper exit-code structural fix: `bootstrap-data` cf_atlas step split into 4 independently-reported sub-steps**. **MINOR bump** — consumer-visible behavior change in the bootstrap summary output (4 new ✓/✗ lines per cold run, new `⚠` soft-failure marker for the aggregate, new `BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_{CORE,F,K,N}_TIMEOUT` env vars) plus additive `--skip` / `--only` flags on `conda_forge_atlas.py build`. Lands the P2 carryover from the v8.16.5 session retro that v8.16.6 had only mitigated symptomatically. **What was broken.** `bootstrap-data --profile admin` ran a single `cf-atlas-build` subprocess invoking all ~21 phases serially under one 14,400 s wrapper timeout. When the wrapper deadline fired before the underlying Python subprocess returned, the bootstrap summary printed `✗ cf-atlas-build` while the subprocess kept running to clean exit — operators relying on the wrapper exit code saw a false-negative on a build that actually succeeded. v8.16.6 raised the timeout floor to 14,400 s (4 h) to widen the slack window, but the structural fix (per-phase wrapper invocations so each phase reports independently) stayed deferred. **The structural fix.** v8.22.0 splits `_step_cf_atlas` into a new `_step_cf_atlas_split` helper that runs the cf_atlas pipeline as **four independently-reported sub-steps**, each with its own timeout + ✓/✗ line: (1) **`cf-atlas-core`** — all phases EXCEPT F/K/N (B/B.5/B.6/C/C.5/D/O/P/Q/R/S/E/E.5/G/G'/H/J/L/M), default 1,800 s (`BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_CORE_TIMEOUT`), **HARD failure** — when core returns non-zero the helper short-circuits and the bootstrap aborts (F/K/N never run; aborting prevents compounding corruption on a half-built atlas); (2) **`cf-atlas-F`** — Phase F only (anaconda.org per-package downloads, ~83 min serial via API or seconds via s3-parquet), default 7,200 s (`BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_F_TIMEOUT`), **SOFT failure** — report and continue to K; (3) **`cf-atlas-K`** — Phase K only (VCS upstream-version fanout, ~60–75 min sustained-rate v8.20.0+ or ~30 min with `PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=1`), default 7,200 s (`BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_K_TIMEOUT`), **SOFT failure**; (4) **`cf-atlas-N`** — Phase N only (live GitHub CI/issues/PRs, ~14 min channel-wide), default 3,600 s (`BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_N_TIMEOUT`), **SOFT failure**, runs only when admin profile is active OR `--gh` is set. The four sub-steps shell out to `pixi run -e local-recipes build-cf-atlas -- --only PHASE_LIST` (or `--skip F,K,N` for core), routing through new mutually-exclusive `--skip` / `--only` flags landed on `conda_forge_atlas.py build` specifically to make the split atomic. **Aggregate `cf-atlas-build` line.** The bootstrap summary still prints a single `cf-atlas-build` row alongside the 4 sub-step rows so existing log-scrapers don't break; the aggregate reflects the worst sub-step outcome — `✓` when all four succeeded, **new `⚠` marker** when core ✓ but at least one of F/K/N returned non-zero, `✗` when core failed. The `⚠` aggregate is NOT counted toward the bootstrap exit code (operators told the bootstrap to continue past soft failures; the sub-step `✗` already surfaces what went wrong). **Phase ordering preserved.** Core phases run B → B.5 → B.6 → C → C.5 → D → O → P → Q → R → S → E → E.5 → G → G' → H → J → L → M in their canonical order — Phase E/J/L/M's dependency on the cf-graph cache (Phase E) lands inside the same sub-step, so the original prerequisite chain is intact. F/K/N each run in isolation under `--only`, but neither is a prerequisite for any other phase in the v8.21.0 pipeline, so isolating them is safe. **Legacy escape hatch — preserved.** Setting `BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_TIMEOUT` explicitly RESTORES the v8.16.6 single-subprocess invocation: one big subprocess, one ✓/✗ line, one timeout. Useful when an operator wants pre-v8.22.0 behavior or when the split surfaces an unexpected interaction. Operators who never set `BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_TIMEOUT` get the new behavior by default — that's the consumer-visible behavior change earning the MINOR rather than PATCH bump (existing surface didn't break, but the documented default shifted). The `_DEFAULT_TIMEOUTS["cf_atlas"]` constant stays at 14,400 s for backward-compatible env-override behavior. **Tests.** +20 new cases across two new files: `tests/unit/test_bootstrap_data.py` (15 cases — per-step timeout defaults, env-override propagation, sub-step orchestrator argv recording, F-failure-continues-to-K-and-N, core-failure-aborts-before-F-K-N, `--skip F,K,N` flag on core, `--only F` flag on F, Phase N skipped when gh disabled, `phase_n_maintainer` forwarded into env, `phase_h_source` inherited by every sub-step, sub-step timeouts read per-step env vars, legacy escape hatch routes to single invocation, split path used by default when no legacy env, `_run_cf_atlas_subprocess` emits `--only` / `--skip` flags, both-arrays-raises-ValueError) and `tests/unit/test_conda_forge_atlas_build.py` (15 cases — `_parse_phase_list` None/empty/uppercase/multi/whitespace/empty-token/unknown-raises/dotted-id, `cmd_build` skip excludes phases, `cmd_build` only runs subset, `cmd_build` only preserves listed order, skip-and-only mutex returns rc=2, no-flags runs every phase). Suite: 1,440 → **1,472 passing**, 0 failed, 0 errors. Pyright clean across `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` + `scripts/bootstrap_data.py`. **Files touched**: `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` (added `_parse_phase_list` helper + extended `cmd_build` with mutex-validated `--skip` / `--only` filtering + extended argparse with the two flags); `scripts/bootstrap_data.py` (added 4 new `_DEFAULT_TIMEOUTS` keys + docstring documentation block + added `_run_cf_atlas_subprocess` helper + added `_step_cf_atlas_split` orchestrator + refactored Step 4 to dispatch core/F/K/N sub-steps with legacy-env escape hatch + extended `results` type to `bool | None` to carry the new `⚠` aggregate sentinel + updated summary loop to render `⚠` + scoped exit-code computation to `ok is False` so soft failures don't fail the bootstrap); `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` (new "Wrapper false-negative — fixed structurally in v8.22.0" subsection inside the Profile Reference, with the 4-sub-step matrix + routing + legacy-escape-hatch documentation); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.21.0 → 8.22.0); `tests/unit/test_bootstrap_data.py` (NEW — 15 cases); `tests/unit/test_conda_forge_atlas_build.py` (NEW — 15 cases); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). **What v8.22.0 explicitly is NOT.** No schema migration (the wrapper split is orchestration-only; `cf_atlas.db` shape unchanged at v28). [legacy monolithic]` banner instead. **Why MINOR not PATCH.** The default `bootstrap-data --profile admin` run now prints **5 lines** in the summary where v8.21.0 printed **1** (`cf-atlas-core / -F / -K / -N` sub-step rows plus the aggregate `cf-atlas-build`). **v8.21.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **12-item cleanup bundle from the deferred-work backlog (Phase F+ Waves 2 & 3 + Phase K cron-runner)**. **MINOR bump** — additive code + tests across `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py`, three breakdown CLIs, `_parquet_cache.py`, and the engineering reference. The one consumer-visible behavior change that earns the MINOR rather than PATCH bump is **DW-W3-2**: recipes whose v0 `{% set python_min = "..." %}` declaration is wrapped in a non-trivial `{% if … %}/{% endif %}` block (typical CUDA-conditional shape) now extract as `None` instead of the conditional value, so `pyver_breakdown --policy-check` flips some rows from `bump-safe` to `unknown` (the actionable correction — the override only applies under one variant, so the whole feedstock shouldn't be flagged bump-safe based on it). **Test gaps closed (3 items).** **DW-test-1** lands two new migration-crash-simulation tests in `test_schema_v27_migration.py::test_v26_migration_recovers_from_partial_kill` and `test_schema_v28_migration.py::test_v27_migration_recovers_from_partial_kill`. Both use a `_CrashingConnection(sqlite3.Connection)` subclass (cleaner than monkeypatching `conn.execute`, which is read-only on the stdlib Connection object — the subclass override is the supported extension point) that raises after an Nth ALTER lands; re-running `init_schema` on the same DB without the crashing wrapper proves the migration ladder + sentinel writes are genuinely idempotent. **DW-K-2** adds three fractional-bucket regression tests in `test_phase_k_scheduler.py::TestRateLimitedScheduler`: `test_fractional_bucket_replenishment` drains to 0, sleeps 0.5 s real-time, then asserts the next acquire sleeps ~0.5 s more (covers the `0 < bucket < 1` partial-refill state); `test_sub_millisecond_acquires` fires 100 acquires at rps=1000 and asserts ≥50 ms wall-clock (after the 10-token initial burst, 90 paced acquires × 1 ms each — guards the sub-ms underflow path); `test_long_sleep_refill_clamp` monkeypatches `conda_forge_atlas.time.monotonic` to fake a 60-s clock jump, then verifies the bucket clamps to `bucket_capacity=10` (not 60 tokens) — the next 10 acquires don't sleep, the 11th does. **DW-K-5** strengthens `test_default_mode_uses_scheduler` by seeding 3 eligible GitLab rows (vs. 1 previously) so the dispatcher's REST scheduler path is exercised end-to-end; the test now asserts `len(call_times) == 3` (exact match — regression-guards a future patch removing `_phase_k_fetch_one` invocations from the loop) AND keeps the scheduler-class spacing-floor assertion (`1/rps - 50 ms slack`) as a separate sub-block. **Regex improvements (3 items).** **DW-W2-1** tightens the `pkg_python` filter in `_phase_f_via_s3` from `^(2\.7|3\.[0-9]{1,2})$` to `^(2\.7|3\.([0-9]|1[0-9]|20))$` so dirty parquet values like `'3.81'` now drop (previously matched `3.[0-9]{1,2}` and were kept — closes the v8.18.0 docstring drift the implementer flagged as known-limitation). Updated `test_python_regex_filter_drops_dirty_values` fixture adds a `'3.81'` row + asserts it's dropped; cross-contamination check extended. Re-tighten when Python 3.21 ships. **DW-W3-1** extends `_PYTHON_MIN_V1_RE` to optionally consume a YAML type tag (`!!str` / any `!!<word>`) between the colon and the value: `^\s*python_min:\s*(?:!!\w+\s+)?['\"]?(\d+\.\d+)['\"]?`. Rare in the 5,001-sample survey but valid YAML; the regression test `test_v1_yaml_tag_str_extraction` extracts `"3.11"` from `python_min: !!str "3.11"`. **DW-W3-2** adds Jinja conditional-detection around the v0 `{% set python_min %}` match. After a match succeeds, the helper scans backwards from the match position for the nearest `{% if <condition> %}`, walks forward with depth-tracking to find the matching `{% endif %}`, and — if the match is wrapped AND the condition is non-trivial (anything other than `true` / `True` / `1` / empty) — returns `None` instead of the matched value. Two new tests cover both paths: `test_v0_jinja_conditional_returns_none` (CUDA-conditional shape returns None) and `test_v0_jinja_set_outside_if_returns_value` (bare unconditional set still extracts). **Defensive coding (3 items).** **DW-W2-2** applies PEP 503 canonicalization (`re.sub(r'[-_.]+', '-', name.lower())`) to the parquet `pkg_name` column AFTER `read_filtered` returns but BEFORE the Wave 2 group-bys + `eligible_names` lookup; same normalization fires on the Wave 3 `chan_table`. Mirrors the `_phase_p_clickhouse` precedent (cited inline). Closes the lookup-miss where parquet's `'Pillow'` (capital P) wouldn't align with the lowercase-canonical `eligible_names={'pillow'}` — Wave 2 columns + breakdown tables would silently stay NULL. New test `test_pep503_normalization_matches_mixed_case_parquet` seeds the exact scenario + asserts `total_downloads=500` populated. **DW-W3-4** lands three bundled small fixes: (a) **connection close discipline** in `channel_split.py`, `platform_breakdown.py`, `pyver_breakdown.py` — each now wraps `_open_db()` in `with contextlib.closing(...)` so a future MCP-server in-process dispatch wouldn't leak connections (subprocess mode was fine; the wrapper is forward-looking); (b) **parquet scale guard** in `_parquet_cache.read_filtered` — when `len(months) > 12 AND pkg_names is None AND data_source is None`, emit a stderr warning that the call materializes the entire all-channel parquet (~150 MB+) so an accidental refactor surfaces immediately; (c) **type-annotation honesty** — verified `_extract_declared_python_min` signature is `str | None` (was fixed in v8.20.0 retro); no other Phase E helpers carry the same docstring/signature drift. **DW-K-1** adds a `PHASE_K_LIMIT` short-circuit on the 403-backfill expansion: when `PHASE_K_LIMIT > 0` (debug knob), the backfill SELECT is skipped entirely and a stderr advisory prints (`Phase K: PHASE_K_LIMIT set; skipping 403 backfill expansion (set PHASE_K_LIMIT=0 to enable)`). Sentinel still DELETEd on success per the existing one-shot contract — the test `test_phase_k_limit_skips_backfill_expansion` seeds a fresh-403 row + `PHASE_K_LIMIT=10`, asserts the row is NOT visited AND that the sentinel was consumed. Prevents a `PHASE_K_LIMIT=10` debug run from accidentally dragging thousands of zombie 403 rows back into eligibility on a fresh-upgraded DB. **Docs / operator advisories (3 items).** **DW-K-3** adds a one-line stderr advisory when `PHASE_K_CONCURRENCY` is set without `PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=1` — the default sustained-rate mode runs serially through the scheduler and ignores concurrency, so operators expecting throughput control are no longer silently surprised: `Phase K: PHASE_K_CONCURRENCY=N ignored in sustained-rate mode; use PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=1 or PHASE_K_REQUESTS_PER_SECOND=N to control throughput`. **DW-K-4** adds a "Codeberg note (v8.21.0)" paragraph to `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 1 right after the token-bucket scheduler example: documents that the 3 RPS default is uncited for Codeberg (auto-memory `project_phase_k_secondary_rate_limit.md` covers GitHub only); volume is small (~16 rows in a typical channel-wide run) and Codeberg's documented limits are higher than GitHub's, so 3 RPS appears safe; revisit if Codeberg-hosted feedstocks grow above ~100 OR a Codeberg HTTP 403 surfaces in `upstream_versions.last_error`. **DW-K-6** adds an explicit "**NOT thread-safe; use only from a single thread**" line to the `_RateLimitedScheduler` class docstring with the wrap-in-`threading.Lock` escape hatch — the previous module comment said "no `threading.Lock` because the default path is single-worker" but the class docstring itself didn't carry the constraint. **What v8.21.0 explicitly is NOT.** v8.20.1's § 10 (l) strict-`== "1"` boolean parse discipline applied by construction (no new `bool(os.environ.get(...))` introduced — DW-K-1 and DW-K-3 used explicit `is not None` / `> 0` checks); v8.20.1's § 10 (m) I/O matrix consistency wasn't a risk because this isn't a BMAD-driven effort with an I/O matrix — direct ship per the user's "no BMAD ceremony" directive. No schema bump (the migration files weren't touched), no new env var that gates a behavior path (the new advisories don't gate; they observe), no new persona-default flip. **Tests**: +10 (2 migration crash-sim, 3 fractional-bucket regression, 1 strengthened default-mode dispatch, 1 PHASE_K_LIMIT bypass, 1 YAML-tag extraction, 1 Jinja-conditional-None, 1 Jinja-unconditional-value, 1 PEP 503 normalization — and `test_python_regex_filter_drops_dirty_values` got an extra row + assertion for `'3.81'` dropped, which counts as a strengthen rather than a new case). Suite: 1,430 → **1,440 passing**, 0 failed, 0 errors. **v8.20.1** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Retro deltas from the v8.20.0 Phase K closeout**. **PATCH bump** — documentation only; no code or test changes. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the v8.20.0 bmad-quick-dev closeout retro surfaced two durable engineering disciplines + one clarification, landing as edits to `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10. **(l) Environment-variable boolean parses use strict `== "1"`, not `bool(os.environ.get(...))`.** The first v8.20.0 sub-agent wrote `aggressive_mode = bool(os.environ.get("PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE"))`. `bool()` of any non-empty string is True — so `PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=0`, `=false`, `=no`, even `= ` (trailing space) would silently re-arm the 8-worker burst pattern that the rest of the ship was designed to escape. Blind hunter caught it; patch was `== "1"` strict equality on the literal `"1"`. **Discipline rule**: any phase env-var that gates "opt-in to behavior X" uses **strict `== "1"`** not `bool(...)`. Document the convention in env-var docstrings ("set =1 to opt in; anything else is treated as unset"). Apply uniformly across all `PHASE_*_AGGRESSIVE`, `PHASE_*_DEBUG_*`, `PHASE_*_ENABLED`, `PHASE_*_DISABLED` flag variables. Numeric/string-value env vars naturally use `int()`/`float()` and aren't affected — but the v8.20.0 H4/EC-#7 patch added the sibling rule for numeric envs: **always validate finite-and-positive on `float()` parses** — wrap in try/except + `math.isfinite()` + fallback with stderr advisory; don't let an env-var typo (`nan`, `inf`, empty) crash a phase. **(m) Spec I/O matrix consistency between "Expected Output" and "Error Handling" columns.** v8.20.0's Phase K spec I/O matrix row 3 said both "DELETE sentinel before fanout starts" (Expected Output) AND "sentinel survives Phase K crash mid-run; idempotent recovery" (Error Handling). These are contradictory: if DELETE fires pre-fanout, mid-crash leaves the sentinel already gone, recovery via sentinel re-application is impossible. The implementer picked the literal Expected-Output reading; the edge case hunter caught the contradiction post-implementation; the patch moved the DELETE to two post-fanout success paths (main + empty-work early-return) so mid-crashes correctly preserve the sentinel. **Discipline rule**: when authoring an I/O matrix row whose Error-Handling column describes a sentinel/marker-based recovery, the Expected-Output column MUST describe sentinel persistence consistent with the recovery contract. Don't write "DELETE before X" alongside "survives mid-X crash" — pick the recovery you want and write both columns to match. If the two columns describe legitimately different control paths (success vs. failure), separate them into two matrix rows. **(j) scope clarification.** v8.19.1's rule (j) was titled "population-distribution claims need empirical-verification discipline". v8.20.0's AC-1 timing band (9.5-12s vs. the actual 5.5-12s bucket-math floor) demonstrated the rule applies to **all quantitative claims** — cost, coverage, distribution, timing, performance, throughput. (j) hereby clarified to cover any quantitative claim that can be derived or measured. **What this retro does NOT land**: no auto-memory entry (both findings stayed in atlas-engineering scope — no cross-skill BMAD↔CFE rule); no v8.20.0 entry amendment (immutable-history per v8.15.1 erratum discipline; v8.20.0 retains the original wording). **Counter-factual**: if (l) + (m) had been part of the skill at v8.20.0 intake — H2 (`bool()` truthy) doesn't surface in step-04, EC-#4 (sentinel-DELETE contradiction) doesn't surface in step-04, AC-1 amendment isn't needed. 3 step-04 findings × ~15 min triage saved on the next 2-3 Wave-style efforts. ROI ~2× on the first equivalent effort; compounds across future waves. **Retro artifact** at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/retro-cfe-phase-k-cron-runner-2026-06-13.md` (gitignored — BMAD working-file convention). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.20.1.

**v8.20.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Phase K sustained-rate cron runner — secondary-rate-limit fix for the REST fanout**. **MINOR bump** — additive: new `_RateLimitedScheduler` class + three new `PHASE_K_*` env vars + one-shot `meta` sentinel pair; no schema bump (no DDL on `meta`); GraphQL batch path completely untouched. Closes `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/spec-phase-k-cron-runner.md` (intake `docs/specs/atlas-phase-k-cron-runner.md`). **Problem.** A 2026-05-12 admin run logged **15 % HTTP 403s on a 4,400-row Phase K fanout (659 failures)** while the primary 5,000/hr GitHub quota stayed at <1% — the failures were GitHub's secondary / burst limit tripped by the 8-worker `ThreadPoolExecutor` peaking at ~70 req/s. Primary-quota tuning + retries + longer backoffs were all ruled out (auto-memory `project_phase_k_secondary_rate_limit.md` summarizes the elimination chain). **Fix.** Module-level `_RateLimitedScheduler(rps, bucket_capacity=10)` token bucket in `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` (stdlib `time.monotonic()`; ~30 LOC; no `threading.Lock` because the default path is single-worker — multiple workers competing for one bucket at 3 RPS adds zero throughput); Phase K REST fanout now wraps each call in `scheduler.acquire()` at default `PHASE_K_REQUESTS_PER_SECOND=3.0` (a 3× safety margin under GitHub's empirically-observed ~10 req/s secondary-limit ceiling for per-IP/token combinations). **Operator escape hatch.** `PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=1` restores the previous 8-worker `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=PHASE_K_CONCURRENCY)` burst pattern AND emits a one-line stderr warning at Phase K entry (`PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=1 — using 8-worker burst pattern; expect HTTP 403 churn`) so operators reviewing CI captures can tell at a glance which path was used. **Operator confidence in the new default.** First-30 s of scheduler activity logs per-request timing to stderr (`phase-k: req N at t=Xs (target rate 3.0 req/s)`), then goes silent unless `PHASE_K_DEBUG_SCHEDULER=1` is set — gives upgraders immediate visual confirmation the scheduler is engaged without spamming long-running CI logs. **GraphQL stays untouched.** `_phase_k_github_graphql_batch` still runs at `PHASE_K_GRAPHQL_BATCH_SIZE=100` repos/request (sustained <1 req/s for the same volume) and is NOT routed through the scheduler — touching it adds risk without benefit. REST fallback for GitHub (`PHASE_K_GRAPHQL_DISABLED=1`) does go through the scheduler. **One-shot 403-backfill sentinel.** `init_schema` atomically writes BOTH `meta.phase_k_403_backfill_pending=1` (consumable signal) AND `meta.phase_k_first_run_post_v8_20_0=1` (install marker) wrapped in BEGIN IMMEDIATE/COMMIT on the first init call after upgrade — the install marker is checked first so subsequent init calls short-circuit, and the consumable sentinel fires exactly once. `phase_k_vcs_versions` reads the sentinel at row-eligibility-build time, expands the TTL-gated SELECT to include every `last_error LIKE '%403%'` row regardless of fetched_at, then DELETEs the sentinel before fanout starts so a mid-fanout crash falls back to the natural `last_error != NULL` TTL bypass on the next run (idempotent recovery). No schema bump — the `meta` table is `(key, value)` and accepts arbitrary keys without DDL. **Wall-clock trade-off.** Cold full-channel Phase K grows from ~30 min (8-worker burst) → ~60-75 min (sustained-rate at 3 RPS), all under the existing 14,400 s = 4 h `cf_atlas` wrapper cap with ~80 min of slack. Incremental TTL-skip runs (<100 new rows) are unaffected — burst pattern never triggered at that scale anyway. **Tests.** +7 cases in NEW `tests/unit/test_phase_k_scheduler.py`: `TestRateLimitedScheduler::{test_30_requests_at_3rps_takes_at_least_10s, test_bucket_starts_at_capacity_and_drains, test_env_var_override_honored, test_zero_rps_rejected}` covers the AC-1 ±10% timing band, the burst-then-drain math, the `PHASE_K_REQUESTS_PER_SECOND` env-var read path, and the `ValueError` on `rps<=0`; `TestPhaseKDispatch::{test_default_mode_uses_scheduler, test_aggressive_mode_uses_thread_pool, test_backfill_sentinel_bypasses_ttl}` exercises the dispatcher's branch on `PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE` (constructed `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=8)` verified by spy), the scheduler-active path (per-call spacing verified out-of-band), and the full sentinel install→consume→delete cycle with a seeded `upstream_versions.last_error='HTTP 403'` row whose `fetched_at` is within TTL (vanilla SELECT would skip it; backfill expansion pulls it back in; sentinel DELETEd after eligibility build; install marker survives). Suite: 1,423 → **1,430 passing**, 0 failed, 0 errors. Pyright clean on `conda_forge_atlas.py` + `bootstrap_data.py`. **Files touched.** `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` (new `_RateLimitedScheduler` module-level class + `init_schema` one-shot sentinel pair install wrapped in BEGIN IMMEDIATE/COMMIT + `phase_k_vcs_versions` docstring update with the 3 new env vars + aggressive-mode branch with stderr warning + 403-backfill eligibility expansion + sentinel DELETE-before-fanout + `_scheduled_fetch_one` inner helper that wraps `_phase_k_fetch_one` with `scheduler.acquire()` + first-30s timing logs + scheduler-driven GitLab/Codeberg REST loop + scheduler-driven GitHub-REST-fallback when `PHASE_K_GRAPHQL_DISABLED=1`); `scripts/bootstrap_data.py` (docstring gains a "Phase K sustained-rate scheduler" block documenting all 3 new env vars + `_DEFAULT_TIMEOUTS["cf_atlas"]` comment updated from `K~30` to `K~60-75 (sustained) | K~30 (PHASE_K_AGGRESSIVE=1)` with the rationale); `tests/unit/test_phase_k_scheduler.py` (NEW, 7 cases); `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` (Phase K section: 3 new env vars in Tunables + new Cold wall-clock subsection + ✅ Resolved bullet replacing the secondary-rate-limit open issue); `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` (§ 1 gains a v8.20.0-canonical token-bucket-scheduler example block + cross-reference to auto-memory `project_phase_k_secondary_rate_limit.md`); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.19.1 → 8.20.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). **What's NOT in this ship.** No cross-process / distributed rate limiting (NG1 in spec); no dynamic rate detection from response headers (GitHub doesn't expose secondary limits via headers — NG4); no GitHub App authentication swap (App tokens get the same secondary limit — NG5); no Phase L / Phase H / Phase N retry-strategy changes (different rate-limit profiles, separate ships if needed — NG2); no host-specific RPS variation (Recommendation: same 3.0 RPS for github/gitlab/codeberg — OQ-3). **Boundaries discipline** (per `atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10 (g)–(k)): no schema migration, no multi-table aggregation, no new provenance label, no population-distribution claim — so the v8.18.1 § 10 (i) load-bearing step-04 adversarial review is recommended (touches a phase dispatcher) but not blocking per the spec checklist. **Retro** lands at closeout per CLAUDE.md Rule 2 at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/retro-cfe-phase-k-cron-runner-2026-06-13.md`.
