**v8.19.1** (Jun 13, 2026, previous) — **Retro deltas from the v8.19.0 Phase F+ Wave 3 closeout**. **PATCH bump** — documentation only; no code or test changes. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the v8.19.0 bmad-quick-dev closeout retro surfaced two durable engineering disciplines that landed as new sub-rules in `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10. **(j) Population-distribution claims in spec ACs need the same empirical-verification discipline as cost + coverage claims.** v8.15.1 (cost) and v8.16.2 (coverage) established the rule that quantitative claims must cite an empirical source. v8.19.0's Wave 3 spec AC-1 said "`packages.python_min` is non-NULL for ≥80% of conda-forge-only packages" — the implementer's 5,001-sample empirical survey of cf-graph `node_attrs/<name>.json` found ~9% of recipes declare an override; ~91% inherit the conda-forge global pinning default. The AC was off by ~10×. The acceptance auditor caught the internal contradiction between the spec body and the CHANGELOG's empirical wording. **Discipline rule**: any spec AC that includes a percentage threshold against a real-world population (rows in `packages`, feedstocks-per-maintainer, packages-on-defaults, etc.) MUST cite the empirical source the threshold was derived from, OR ship the implementation first, measure, then write the AC. Don't write speculative percentage thresholds. **(k) "Ask First" boundary clauses trigger investigation, not necessarily HALT.** v8.19.0's Wave 3 Boundaries said "HALT if neither `python_min` nor `noarch_python_min` key is found in `node_attrs/<name>.json`, don't guess." The implementer's 5,001-sample survey found neither key at the top level — but the value lives **nested inside `raw_meta_yaml`** as a Jinja context variable. The implementer surveyed, documented the finding in the CHANGELOG, then proceeded with regex extraction — explicitly endorsed by the spec's § Design Notes. Strictly HALTing would have been wrong: the data IS there, just in a different shape than the spec assumed. **Discipline rule**: an Ask First clause means "investigate before guessing", not "stop on first non-match". If the investigation finds the same data verifiably present in a different shape, document the deviation and proceed. The fail-safe is the documentation + CHANGELOG, not the HALT. **What this retro does NOT land**: no auto-memory entry (both findings stayed in atlas-engineering scope — no cross-skill BMAD↔CFE rule); no v8.19.0 entry amendment (immutable-history per the v8.15.1 erratum discipline; v8.19.0 retains the original wording). **Counter-factual**: if (j) and (k) had been part of the skill at v8.19.0 intake, AC-1 would have been empirically grounded (≥5%, verified $DATE) from the start; the Ask First clause would have been written as "investigate node_attrs structure, document the actual shape, proceed if data is verifiably present." Two step-04 findings × ~15 min triage each saved on the next 2-3 Wave-style efforts. ROI break-even on this retro entry's ~15 min of codification; the durables compound for future waves. **Retro artifact** at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/retro-cfe-phase-f-wave3-2026-06-13.md` (gitignored — BMAD working-file convention). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.19.1.

**v8.19.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Phase F+ Wave 3 — `platform-breakdown` / `pyver-breakdown` / `channel-split` CLIs + MCP tools, plus `packages.python_min` (Phase E write) + `package_channel_downloads` (Phase F write)**. **MINOR bump** — additive: three new CLIs, three new MCP tools, three new pixi tasks, one new `packages` column, one new side table; no breaking surface change. Closes Wave 3 of `docs/specs/atlas-phase-f-s3-backend.md` (Wave 1 v7.6.0, admin default-flip v8.17.0, Wave 2 v8.18.0). **Schema migration v27 → v28** adds `packages.python_min TEXT` (NULL for the ~91% of recipes that inherit the conda-forge-pinning default; populated by Phase E when the recipe overrides via v1 `python_min: "3.11"` inside `context:` or v0 `{% set python_min = "3.11" %}`) and the new `package_channel_downloads(conda_name, data_source, downloads_90d, downloads_total, fetched_at)` side table keyed on (conda_name, data_source). Migration block writes BOTH `phase_e_force_refresh_pending` AND `phase_f_force_refresh_pending` one-shot meta sentinels wrapped in BEGIN IMMEDIATE/COMMIT so the next bootstrap-data run populates the new column AND new table immediately without waiting for the respective TTLs to expire. **Phase E extension** — a 5,001-sample survey of cached `node_attrs/*.json` (2026-06-13) confirmed `python_min` is NOT a top-level node_attrs key but lives inside the `raw_meta_yaml` string field as a Jinja context variable. New `_extract_declared_python_min(raw_meta_yaml)` regex helper (module-level so it compiles once across the ~28k feedstock loop) extracts the value; new per-row `UPDATE packages SET python_min = ? WHERE conda_name = ?` runs only when an override is found (NULL stays NULL when the recipe inherits the pinning default — `pyver_breakdown --policy-check` renders such rows as "unknown" with a stderr advisory). Single-writer contract: Phase E owns the column; Phase F never touches it. Force-refresh sentinel read-then-clear at end-of-phase. **Phase F extension** — `_parquet_cache.read_filtered` accepts `data_source=None` to skip the channel filter (previously always filtered to `'conda-forge'`); `_phase_f_via_s3` performs a SEPARATE parquet read with `data_source=None` and one additional per-(pkg_name, data_source) group-by, capturing all channels the parquet ships (defaults / bioconda / pytorch / nvidia / etc.) — channel breakdown intentionally NOT filtered to conda-forge so `channel-split` can surface migration opportunities. Writes use the v8.18.0 H1 pattern: DELETE-by-scope-key + INSERT OR REPLACE chunked in 500-row batches to prevent stale-channel zombies. Same single-pass discipline as Wave 2 — pyarrow Tables are zero-copy across group-bys; expected wall-clock delta ~5-10s on a 12-month cached window. Cost: ~13 MB × len(months) of additional parquet bytes streamed from local cache (no extra HTTP). **Three new CLIs** (each accepts `--format markdown|json|csv` with markdown default per Q2=B; all read-only, no urllib/requests imports — verified by grep): (1) **`platform-breakdown`** — single-package mode shows per-platform 90d/lifetime + share table; `--top N --platform P` ranks packages by absolute 90d downloads on the chosen platform (high-absolute-volume on a niche platform is the actionable signal — drives ARM/win-64/aarch64 triage); `--feedstock-roundup --maintainer X` groups by `feedstock_name` for maintainer triage (one feedstock = one rerender target, per OQ-2). (2) **`pyver-breakdown`** — single-package mode shows per-Python distribution + "Empirical python_min floor (>=N%): 3.X" footer; **`--policy-check`** (the headline value) joins `packages.python_min` against the empirical floor and categorizes rows as `bump-safe` (empirical > declared — maintainer can raise without losing material adoption), `aligned` (equal), `aggressive` (empirical < declared — declared is already optimistic), `unknown` (NULL declared), or `stale` (Phase F TTL >7d). Sort order: bump-safe → aligned → aggressive → unknown → stale (per Q1=A — actionable signals first; aggressive rows are de-prioritized background). `--threshold-pct` (default 2.0) is operator-tunable; FR-4 stale-row check emits stderr advisories without crashing. Spec I/O matrix line 47: non-zero exit if ALL packages are unknown (all-unknown signals "run bootstrap-data --profile admin"). (3) **`channel-split`** — single-package mode shows per-channel 90d/lifetime + "Migration opportunity: X% on defaults" footer when defaults > 10%; `--defaults-share-min N --top M` ranks defaults-heavy packages by absolute defaults 90d downloads (NOT share — high-volume is the actionable target); `--migration-checklist --maintainer X` (per Q3=B, scope creep accepted as a thin formatter) emits markdown checkbox lines (`- [ ] Open conda-forge feedstock for <pkg>; defaults has X% share (Y 90d downloads)`) suitable for paste into a GitHub issue. **Three new MCP tools** registered in `.claude/tools/conda_forge_server.py` mirroring the `staleness_report` shape; **three new `pixi.toml` tasks** alphabetically near sibling cf-atlas read-CLI cluster. **What's NOT in this ship** (per spec NG1-NG6 + scope clarifications): no recipe-edit automation (`pyver-breakdown --policy-check` flags, doesn't write); no per-channel time-series (90d + lifetime only — same discipline as Wave 2); no per-(pkg, channel, month) full history; no channel-name normalization (raw `data_source` strings written as-is); no `_phase_f_via_api` retrofit for `python_min` or `package_channel_downloads` (Phase E owns python_min; API-path leaves channel breakdowns empty — NG4); no writes from any of the 3 CLIs. **Tests**: +37 (3 v28 migration cases mirroring v27; 7 platform_breakdown including --top + --feedstock-roundup + json/csv shapes + FR-1 read-only grep; 8 pyver_breakdown including the headline policy-check correctly categorizing all four statuses + --threshold-pct + NULL-declared-min handling + sort order assertions; 8 channel_split including migration-checklist + --defaults-share-min + 10% migration footer trigger boundary; 6 phase_e_python_min including regex extraction across v0/v1 + NULL fallback + tarball-mocked UPDATE; 1 phase_f_dispatch in `TestS3ParquetWave2Metrics` asserting per-channel rows + DELETE+INSERT idempotency on rerun). Suite: 1,386 → **1,423 passing**, 0 failed, 0 errors. Pyright clean across all touched files. **11+ catalog rows in `reference/atlas-actionable-intelligence.md` flipped from `📋 open` to `✅ shipped (v8.19.0)`** — Wave 3 row plus per-mode rows for each of the three CLIs. **Files touched**: `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` (SCHEMA_VERSION 27→28, 1 ALTER TABLE add-column, 1 new CREATE TABLE block in SCHEMA_DDL, v27→v28 migration block writing both sentinels, `_extract_declared_python_min` module-level helper, Phase E sentinel read at start + clear at end + per-row UPDATE write, Phase F per-channel pyarrow group-by + DELETE-by-scope-key + INSERT OR REPLACE chunked write); **v8.18.1** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Retro deltas from the v8.18.0 Phase F+ Wave 2 closeout**. **PATCH bump** — documentation only; no code or test changes. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the v8.18.0 bmad-quick-dev closeout retro surfaced three durable engineering disciplines that landed as new sub-rules in `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10. **(g) `INSERT OR REPLACE` alone doesn't deliver "replace" semantics on partial reruns.** A many-to-many breakdown table populated via `INSERT OR REPLACE` only touches the PK rows present in the current sweep; rows whose scope-key vanishes from a later sweep persist as zombies. Spec language saying "replaces, doesn't accumulate" implies *scope-level* replacement, which `INSERT OR REPLACE` does NOT deliver — that's a row-level mechanism. **Fix pattern**: `DELETE FROM <table> WHERE <scope_key> IN (<eligible>)` before the bulk `INSERT OR REPLACE`, in the same transaction. Chunk the DELETE to fit SQLite's 999 host-parameter cap (canonical: 500-row chunks). v8.18.0's H1 patch is the canonical implementation; future spec authors should write **DELETE + INSERT**, not "INSERT OR REPLACE keyed on PK" — the latter is a mechanism, not the intent. **(h) Provenance-column value claims in spec Boundaries must be verified against the dispatcher's actual write paths.** v8.18.0's Wave 2 spec Boundaries claimed Wave 2 columns populate when `downloads_source ∈ {'s3-parquet', 'merged'}`. The H4 reviewer caught that the Phase F dispatcher (`_phase_f_via_auto`) uses `'merged'` only as a *run-summary* label in the result dict — never as a per-row column value. The spec's claim was based on the v7.6.0 column-DDL comment (which lists three values as a static enum), not on live writer behavior. **Fix pattern**: before signing off Wave-N spec Boundaries that constrain on a multi-value column, `grep "<column> *=" scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` and enumerate the literals written by the running code. Discrepancies become either spec corrections or code patches. **(i) Step-04 adversarial review is load-bearing for Phase-F-class changes.** v8.18.0's three-reviewer pass (blind hunter + edge case hunter + acceptance auditor) surfaced 13 patches in step-04: 3 HIGH (stale zombie rows, NULL-overwrite of valid prior data, doc/code divergence on `'merged'`), 5 MED, 5 LOW. Without that pass, all 5 H/M HIGHs would have shipped silently. **Discipline rule**: for any change touching schema migration, multi-table aggregation, or new provenance labels, treat the step-04 pass as a required ship gate, not optional polish. Single-line changes (version bumps, env-var defaults) can skip; anything that adds a column, writes to multiple tables in one transaction, or introduces a new provenance label must go through the three-reviewer pass. **What this retro does NOT land**: no auto-memory entry (all findings stayed in atlas-engineering scope — no cross-skill BMAD↔CFE rule); no v8.18.0 entry amendment (immutable-history per the discipline established in v8.15.1 — the v8.18.0 entry retains the original wording even though (g) and (h) demonstrate it was incomplete; future v8.18.0 readers will follow the cross-reference to § 10 (g)+(h) for the corrected discipline). **Counter-factual**: if (g) and (h) had been part of the skill at v8.18.0 intake, neither H1 nor H4 would have surfaced in step-04 — they would have been caught during step-02 spec authoring instead. Two HIGH-severity reviewer-loop savings × ~30 minutes each = ~1 hour amortized across the next 2–3 Wave-style efforts. ROI ≥ 6× on the ~10 minutes of skill-file edits this retro entry codifies. **Retro artifact** at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/retro-cfe-phase-f-wave2-2026-06-13.md` (gitignored — BMAD working-file convention). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.18.1.

**v8.18.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Phase F+ Wave 2 — richer metrics from the existing parquet sweep**. **MINOR bump** — additive: five new `packages` columns + two new side tables; no breaking surface change. Closes Wave 2 of `docs/specs/atlas-phase-f-s3-backend.md` (Wave 1 + admin default-flip shipped in v7.6.0 + v8.17.0). **Schema migration v26 → v27** adds `packages.{downloads_30d, downloads_90d, downloads_trend_90d, first_nonzero_month, last_nonzero_month}` plus the side tables `package_platform_downloads(conda_name, pkg_platform, downloads_90d, downloads_total, fetched_at)` and `package_python_downloads(conda_name, pkg_python, downloads_90d, downloads_total, fetched_at)`, each with a (conda_name, dim) primary key + a conda_name index. **The whole thing computes in one extended `_phase_f_via_s3` pass — zero new HTTP calls vs. v8.17.0 baseline**: pyarrow Tables are zero-copy, so the same `read_filtered` result feeds three additional group-bys (per-(pkg,time), per-(pkg,platform), per-(pkg,python)). Expected wall-clock delta ~5–15s on a 12-month cached window. **Source-attribution contract** (carries forward from v7.6.0's `downloads_source` column): the new columns + new tables are populated **only** when `downloads_source='s3-parquet'` (the per-row attribution tag — the dispatcher's `'merged'` label is a run-summary value only, never written to per-row columns); rows where `downloads_source='anaconda-api'` keep the columns NULL and have zero rows in either breakdown table. Consumers detect via the provenance column before treating NULL as "no traffic" vs. "API path didn't populate." **Trend-slope discipline** (FR-3): `(cur90 - prev90) / prev90` capped at `+10.0`; NULL when either window is zero (div-by-zero guard on prev90 plus the `cur90==0` mirror that prevents reporting a -100% slope for newly-dormant packages) or fewer than 6 months of data exist (`months_present` derived from the loaded-month list, not per-package observed months, so a dormant package still gets a correct trailing window where its absent months count as zeros). **Data-quality regex on pkg_python** (FR-4): `^(2\.7|3\.[0-9]{1,2})$` drops dirty parquet values; verified 2026-05-10 inspection showed values like `'7.3'` (wrong major) and `'2.30'` (wrong py2 minor) appear in raw rows. The regex doesn't catch the literal `'3.81'` case the spec mentions — it technically matches `3.[0-9]{1,2}` — flagged as a known regex-limitation in the test docstring; tightening is a Wave 4 candidate if it surfaces in real data. **Noarch synthetic remap** (FR-5): parquet's empty-string platform (`pkg_platform=''`) is rewritten to `'noarch'` at the aggregator output so consumer queries don't have to special-case the empty string. **Force-refresh trigger** (Q1 RESOLVED option (b) per spec § Design Notes): the v26 → v27 migration writes a one-shot `meta.phase_f_force_refresh_pending = '1'` sentinel; `_phase_f_eligible_rows` reads + clears it on first consumption, bypassing the 7-day TTL gate so operators see populated Wave 2 columns immediately on the first post-migration Phase F run instead of waiting for natural TTL expiry. Operators can also set `PHASE_F_FORCE_REFRESH=1` env var directly — equivalent semantics, no meta sentinel involvement, easy to flip on per-run. Both paths bypass TTL by switching `_phase_f_eligible_rows` from the `WHERE downloads_fetched_at < cutoff` clause to a no-WHERE selector. **What's NOT in this ship** (per spec NG1-NG5): no Wave 3 CLIs (`platform_breakdown`, `pyver_breakdown`, `channel_split` — separate effort, BMAD-ready in the spec); no API-path retrofit (`_phase_f_via_api` keeps its v8.17.0 2-column output, NG4); no daily granularity (parquet publishes monthly only, NG3); no per-(package, platform, month) full time-series (~38M rows, NG5); no separate disable knob for the breakdown tables (operators wanting to skip them entirely set `PHASE_F_SOURCE=anaconda-api` to bypass the parquet path). **Tests**: +15 (10 Wave-2 aggregation cases in `TestS3ParquetWave2Metrics`, 3 v27 migration cases in new `test_schema_v27_migration.py`, 2 force-refresh edge cases). Suite: 1,370 → **1,385 passing**, 0 failed, 0 errors. Pyright clean. **Five catalog rows flipped from `📋 open` → `✅ shipped (v8.18.0)`** in `reference/atlas-actionable-intelligence.md`: rolling-window adoption signals, 90-day trend slope, lifetime activity months, per-platform breakdown, per-Python breakdown. Wave 3 CLI row stays `📋 open` (separate effort). Files touched: `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` (SCHEMA_VERSION bump 26→27, 5 ALTER TABLE add-columns in the migration ladder, 2 new CREATE TABLE blocks in SCHEMA_DDL, v26→v27 migration block writing the force-refresh sentinel, `_phase_f_eligible_rows` TTL bypass on force-refresh, `_phase_f_via_s3` extension with 3 new pyarrow group-bys + 2 new bulk INSERT OR REPLACE writes); `tests/unit/test_phase_f_dispatch.py` (12 new Wave 2 tests in `TestS3ParquetWave2Metrics`); `tests/unit/test_schema_v27_migration.py` (NEW, 3 migration cases); `tests/unit/test_pypi_downloads_daily.py` (2 schema-version assertions softened from exact-equality to `>= 26` for forward-compat); `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` (Phase F section gains the 5 new columns + 2 new tables + Wave 2 actionable bullet flipped to ✅ shipped); `reference/atlas-actionable-intelligence.md` (5 new rows under Phase F section); `config/skill-config.yaml` (8.17.0 → 8.18.0); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry). **Lesson** (captured in retro at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/retro-cfe-phase-f-wave2-2026-06-13.md`): when the spec body and the in-code regex diverge on what counts as a "dirty" value, the implementation must follow the regex literally and flag the divergence in the test docstring — don't silently widen the regex to match the spec's prose example. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.18.0.

**v8.17.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **`--profile admin` pins `PHASE_F_SOURCE=s3-parquet` (was `auto`)** — 83 min → seconds for Phase F under admin. **MINOR bump** — consumer-visible behavior change: admin-built atlases now carry S3-parquet download numbers rather than anaconda.org API numbers; the two disagree by ~0.5–1.5× per package. **Driver**: v8.16.5 session retro identified Phase F's 83 min serial path as the P1 leverage point for bootstrap-cf-atlas. Original plan was to BMAD-implement `docs/specs/atlas-phase-f-s3-backend.md` — but inspection during scoping found the S3 backend, `PHASE_F_SOURCE` dispatcher, `_parquet_cache.py`, and `downloads_source` provenance column **already shipped in v7.6.0**. The 83 min runtime wasn't a missing-feature problem; it was an `auto` mode that probed `api.anaconda.org/.../pip`, found it reachable, and ran the full ~32k-row serial path. The spec's Wave 1 was complete; the issue was the dispatcher's preference. **What this PATCH-sized change does**: flip `bootstrap_data.py` `PROFILES["admin"]["PHASE_F_SOURCE"]` from `"auto"` to `"s3-parquet"` (single string change in the profile dict at line 175). The `consumer` profile already had this; this brings `admin` in line. `maintainer` profile stays on `auto` because maintainer-scoped row sets are small (~dozens to hundreds of feedstocks; the API path completes in seconds at that size — no need to pay the S3 numerical-discrepancy cost). **Why MINOR (not PATCH)**: changes consumer-visible numbers under `--profile admin`. The discrepancy table in the spec (verified 2026-05-10): `requests` API=81.7M vs S3=122.9M (1.50×); `django` API=3.3M vs S3=1.9M (0.56×); `bmad-method` API=3,625 vs S3=3,084 (0.85×). The gap direction is not consistent — the two sources are correlated-but-distinct metrics, not interchangeable. `packages.downloads_source` carries `'s3-parquet'` so consumers can detect the difference; consumers querying admin-built atlases MUST check the provenance column before treating downloads as API-equivalent. **Operator escape hatches**: `PHASE_F_SOURCE=auto` (probe-then-fallback like before), `PHASE_F_SOURCE=anaconda-api` (force the old serial path), or just `--profile maintainer` if scoping to a single maintainer's feedstocks. All three work with no further config. **Runtime impact**: cold `--fresh --profile admin` drops from ~130 min (Phase F ~83 + K ~30 + N ~14 + H ~12 + others) to **~50 min** (Phase F drops to seconds; K still ~30 min, N still ~14 min). v8.16.6's 14,400s wrapper cap now has ~3-4× slack instead of ~10%. **What this does NOT ship** (deferred per v8.16.5 retro): Wave 2 from the spec (richer Phase F+ metrics — rolling 30/90-day, trend slope, platform/python breakdowns) requires schema migration v26 → v27 + parquet aggregation extension; Wave 3 (`platform_breakdown`, `pyver_breakdown`, `channel_split` CLIs/MCP) requires Wave 2 first. Both remain BMAD-ready in the spec; recommend running `bmad-quick-dev` against `docs/specs/atlas-phase-f-s3-backend.md` for those waves now that Wave 1's prerequisite is mostly self-evident. **Phase K secondary rate-limit** and **wrapper exit-code structural fix** remain P2 (unchanged from v8.16.5 retro). **Lesson** (lands as auto-memory candidate but not skill content): before specifying a BMAD effort, **grep for the relevant code first**. The atlas-phase-f-s3-backend spec was thoughtfully written and intake-ready; but Wave 1 had already shipped and the spec didn't know. ~2 weeks of BMAD work was avoided by 60 seconds of grep. Files touched: `scripts/bootstrap_data.py` (single string change + 8-line explanatory comment); `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` (Phase F row in catalog, Profile defaults paragraph, profile-comparison row at line 873); `CHANGELOG.md` (this entry); `config/skill-config.yaml` (version bump). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.17.0.

**v8.16.6** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Bump `cf_atlas` step timeout 7,200s → 14,400s; correct the stale Phase F/K/L estimate**. **PATCH bump** — one-line value change + comment + help-text update; no behavior change for runs that already finish under 2h. Acts on the P0 follow-up identified in the v8.16.5 session retro. **What was broken**: `scripts/bootstrap_data.py:101` `_DEFAULT_TIMEOUTS["cf_atlas"]` was 7,200s (2h) with an inline comment estimating `F~25 + K~30 + L~20 + others`. The v8.16.2 + v8.16.5 bootstrap-data validation runs measured the actual numbers against a full `--fresh --profile admin` refresh: Phase F took **83 min** (3.3× the docstring's 25 min guess) — anaconda.org per-package downloads at ~6 req/s × 32,413 packages; Phase K **30 min** (matches estimate); Phase H **12 min**; Phase L **55 s** (~22× overestimated in the comment); B/D/E/E.5/J/M ~5 min combined. Excluding Phase N (which has its own `phase_n: 3600` budget), total cf_atlas wall-clock ≈ **130 min** — exceeds the 120 min cap. Every cold `--fresh` run printed `✗ cf-atlas-build` while the underlying Python subprocess continued uninterrupted to clean exit; operators relying on the wrapper exit code saw a false-negative. **Fix**: bumped default to **14,400s (4 h)** — adds ~70 min of headroom for slower networks and accommodates the realistic Phase F duration with slack. Updated the inline comment to `F~83 + K~30 + N~14 + H~12 + others` with "verified 2026-06-13" provenance, applying the verify-quantitative-claims rule from SKILL.md Operating Principle #6. Updated the docstring help block (`BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_TIMEOUT default 14400`). The env override path is unchanged — operators can still set `BOOTSTRAP_CF_ATLAS_TIMEOUT=N` for either direction. **What this does NOT fix** (intentional scope discipline — kept tight; deferred per v8.16.5 retro): (1) Phase F still takes 83 min serially — the structural fix is the S3 parquet backend specced in `docs/specs/atlas-phase-f-s3-backend.md` Wave 1 (would drop Phase F to seconds). (2) Phase K secondary rate-limit on burst fanout (auto-memory `project_phase_k_secondary_rate_limit.md`) needs a cron-runner architecture, not a timeout bump. (3) The bootstrap-data wrapper's exit-code-vs-subprocess-state mismatch (false negative when wrapper times out before subprocess exits) needs a more surgical fix — currently the bump prevents the issue from firing in practice for typical cold runs, but a structural per-phase wrapper invocation pattern is the durable fix. All three remain captured as P1/P2 items. **Verification**: existing tests pass (no timeout-related tests). Live re-test deferred — this is a constant change, not a code-path change; the v8.16.5 bootstrap-data run that exercised the actual 130 min path already validated the underlying Python phases succeed end-to-end. **The bigger lesson**: the v8.16.2 + v8.16.5 CHANGELOG entries documented the timing-vs-comment drift but neither one *fixed* the comment in the source file — a documented anti-pattern (CHANGELOG-only "documentation" of a stale code comment leaves the comment stale; the comment is the thing readers see at the call site). Going forward: when retros surface stale source comments, fix the source as part of the retro, not as a follow-up. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.16.6.

**v8.16.5** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Session retro on the v8.16.x arc (v8.16.0 → v8.16.4) — 3 durable findings landed as skill content + erratum banner on v8.16.0**. **PATCH bump** — documentation only; no code changes. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the user requested a session-wide retro after the v8.16.4 closeout. The session shipped 4 PATCH/MINOR/PATCH-chain versions plus one unrelated recipe fix (`dj-control-room-base` imports cleanup). All four versions correctly addressed their immediate goal; the **cross-version pattern** is what this retro captures: discipline rules that would have collapsed the 4-PATCH chain into a single ship if applied at intake instead of retro. **Three durable findings landed**: (1) **Rename audit scope** — added to `SKILL.md` Operating Principle #6 as a new bullet. When an upstream dependency renames a module, grep the entire skill workspace (`scripts/ + tests/ + tools/ + project-level Python`), not just the script you observed failing. The v8.16.1 "2 sites" framing was wrong; there were 4. The runtime `bootstrap-data` entry-point doesn't exercise `name_resolver.py:24` (Tier-2 fallback rare under cache hits) or `tests/conftest.py:216` (test infrastructure). v8.16.3 had to follow up. Apply the try-new-fallback-to-old pattern at every grep hit at once; ship one PATCH, not three. (2) **Docstring + reference doc must match shipped code at ship time** — added to `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10 as new sub-rule (f). When live testing forces a mid-implementation architecture pivot, re-read docstring + reference doc + CHANGELOG entry against the final code before push. v8.16.0 shipped with three mutually-contradictory descriptions of Phase P/ClickHouse: CHANGELOG entry + reference doc + function docstring all described the abandoned `cityHash64 % 30` bucket-pagination design; only the function body shipped the actual top-N single-query implementation that live testing forced. v8.16.2's retro caught it. ~5 minutes of at-ship re-reading would have prevented ~2 hours of cross-version cleanup. (3) **Erratum-banner discipline applied to v8.16.0 CHANGELOG entry** — prepended `**ERRATUM (v8.16.2 + v8.16.5):**` block in front of the v8.16.0 TL;DR entry pointing forward to the correction site (`atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10 sub-rule (f) for the discipline, `atlas-phases-overview.md` Phase P for the corrected description, this entry for the meta-retro). Validates the immutable-history pattern: body preserved as historical context; banner signals forward. Future contradicted entries should follow this format. **Other meta-findings — captured here, no separate skill-file edit needed**: (4) "*Pre-existing failures*" framing at closeout is a trap. v8.16.3's "4 failures, all pre-existing, unrelated to v8.16.x" was honest but the implicit "leave them" recommendation was wrong; v8.16.4 fixed all 4 in ~30 min. The rule is implicit in Operating Principle #4 (Goal-Driven Execution — pass-all-tests is the goal); "pre-existing" doesn't change that. (5) **Bootstrap-data wrapper timeout (7,200s) is too short for `--profile admin`** — Phase F (~83 min) + Phase K (~30 min) + Phase N (~14 min) sequential = ~127 min just for those three; wrapper times out at 120 min while underlying Python subprocess runs to clean exit. Operators relying on wrapper exit code see false-negative `✗ cf-atlas-build`. Deferred operational follow-up — bump to ≥10,800s (3h) or break into per-phase wrapper invocations. (6) **The 2026 npm-recipe canonical pattern test drift** — `test_workflow_npm.py` was 3 assertions stale (build.sh, conda-forge.yml, noarch:generic) after the merged 2026 inline-script pattern (openspec PR #32368). When canonical patterns ship, the test suite that asserts them needs simultaneous updates, not later-discovered drift. v8.16.4's "inverted assertions" pattern (assert absence of legacy artifacts) catches regressions in either direction; recommend that style for future canonical-pattern test updates. (7) **The verify-quantitative-claims principle keeps validating itself**. v8.15.1 introduced it after the 2026-06-12 BigQuery invoice surprise (cost claims). v8.15.2's live BQ verification caught a broken SQL query the rule's discipline forced into existence. v8.16.0 implementation pivot demonstrated mocked tests can't find server-side caps. v8.16.2 extended the rule to coverage/cardinality claims (the ClickHouse top-1,000 = 3.3 % gap). v8.16.5 (this entry) adds the at-ship docstring-match discipline. Same principle, four corollaries, one source rule. **Session arc summary**: v8.16.0 (MINOR — ClickHouse free default, 13 new tests) → v8.16.1 (PATCH — autotick_bot rename, 2 sites) → v8.16.2 (PATCH — ClickHouse-switch retro deltas, 5 findings) → v8.16.3 (PATCH — rename completion, 2 missed sites) → v8.16.4 (PATCH — test-suite cleanup, 4 pre-existing fixes) → v8.16.5 (PATCH — session retro, this entry). 5 commits + 1 unrelated recipe fix (`e9605d49cb`). Cumulative test suite delta: 1,363 → 1,370 passing; 3 → 0 errors; 4 → 0 failures. **Counter-factual**: if Findings 1+2 had been applied at v8.16.0 intake, the chain would have been v8.16.0 → v8.16.1 (this retro entry) — one MINOR, one PATCH, instead of one MINOR + four PATCHes. Concrete savings: ~3 commit cycles, ~1.5 hours of context-switching, and the bug-search archaeology in v8.16.3 + v8.16.4. **The retro is the recovery mechanism; the at-ship discipline is the prevention mechanism. Both are needed; the second is cheaper.** Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.16.5.

**v8.16.4** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Test-suite cleanup — fix 4 pre-existing failures**. **PATCH bump** — no production behavior change. The 4 failures predate v8.16.x but were left in place; the v8.16.3 closeout surfaced them and the user requested cleanup. Result: full suite **1,370 passed / 0 failed / 0 errors / 2 skipped** (was 1,366 / 4 / 0 / 2 at end of v8.16.3). **Fix 1 — npm workflow integration test was 3 assertions stale**. `tests/integration/test_workflow_npm.py::test_canonical_chain_with_deps` asserted (a) `build.sh` exists, (b) `conda-forge.yml` exists, (c) `data["build"]["noarch"] == "generic"`. All three predate the merged 2026 inline-script pattern (openspec PR #32368 + bmalph PR #33557). The current `generate_npm_recipe_yaml` deliberately drops all three: no standalone build.sh (inline per-platform `build.script:` instead — see `recipe-generator.py:_inline_build_script`); no per-recipe `conda-forge.yml` under default mode (feedstock-mode-only since `recipe-generator.py:1986`); no `noarch:` key at all (native packages were always per-platform, pure-JS now matches — see line 1871). Test updated to **negate** all three assertions with explanatory error messages, so any future regression that re-introduces these files trips the same test in the opposite direction. **Fix 2 — `test_skill_md_consistency.py` flagged 3 legitimate external-file citations as unknown scripts**. The test enumerates all `*.py` filenames mentioned in `SKILL.md` and requires each to exist as either a skill-local script, a test file, or a project-level Python file. Three names — `conftest.py`, `lint_recipe.py`, `conda_recipe_v1_linter.py` — failed the check because they're cited in case-study prose as paths inside *other* packages: `conftest.py` is the Windows-symlink-exclusion case study from staged-recipes PR #33534 (paths inside xorq's sdist wheel layout); `lint_recipe.py` + `conda_recipe_v1_linter.py` are the `conda_smithy/linter/` paths cited in the NoarchSelectorsV1 lint tracing case study. All three are documentation citations of external paths, not invocations of repo scripts. Added to the test's `project_level` allowlist with explanatory comments so reviewers seeing the allowlist entry understand the citation context. **Fix 3 + Fix 4 — `test_v1_recipe_yaml_has_schema_header` flagged bmad-dashboard + mybmad-dashboard recipes for missing line-1 schema header**. Both recipes started with `schema_version: 1` directly, missing the `# yaml-language-server: $schema=https://raw.githubusercontent.com/prefix-dev/recipe-format/main/schema.json` comment that drives editor schema validation. This is the local-recipes-only repo convention (per auto-memory `feedback_schema_header_empirical_scope.md`: 1/30 fresh PRs carry it; conda-forge reviewers don't block PRs that omit it; we enforce it here so editor validation is on by default). Both recipes pre-dated the meta-test (or were imported before the convention was tightened); both now carry the header. No reviewer impact. **Lessons**: (i) test failures that "predate the current work" are still real — the v8.16.3 closeout's "all 4 pre-existing failures, unrelated to v8.16.x" framing was honest but the implicit "leave them" recommendation was wrong; (ii) the 2026 npm-recipe canonical pattern is now stable enough that the test should assert its **absence-of-old-files**, not just presence-of-new-files — the inverted assertions catch regressions in either direction; (iii) the schema-header meta-test correctly caught two long-stale recipes; the convention is enforced and remains enforced. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.16.4.

**v8.16.3** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Complete the v8.16.1 autotick_bot → conda_forge_bot rename — 2 missed call sites**. **PATCH bump** — v8.16.1 patched the 2 most-trafficked call sites (`conda_forge_atlas.py` Phase C + `mapping_manager.py` update-cache CLI) but missed two more that the live `bootstrap-data` run didn't exercise: (1) `scripts/name_resolver.py:24` — Tier-2 mapping resolver (`map_pypi_to_conda` import) used by every PyPI→conda name lookup that falls through Tier-1 cache; (2) `tests/conftest.py:216` — the `stub_metadata_api` pytest fixture used by 3 tests (`test_mapping_manager::test_fetch_returns_lowercased_dict` + `test_name_resolver::{test_resolves_identity_via_metadata_api,test_unknown_via_api_falls_back_to_input}`). Same try-new-fallback-to-old pattern applied to both sites + `# type: ignore[import-not-found,no-redef]` on the fallback line. **Verification**: `pytest test_mapping_manager.py test_name_resolver.py -m 'not network and not slow'` 8/8 pass (was 5 passed + 3 errors). The discovery procedure (`pkgutil.iter_modules` to enumerate the actual installed submodules) is correct; the *application* of it was incomplete because the discovery scope was the `bootstrap-data` runtime, which doesn't exercise the test conftest or name_resolver Tier-2 fallback path. **v8.16.2** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Retro deltas from the ClickHouse switch (v8.16.0) + bootstrap-data end-to-end validation results**. **PATCH bump** — documentation + 1-line code-comment fix; no behavioral change. Per CLAUDE.md Rule 2, the closeout retro on the BigQuery→ClickHouse pivot surfaced **two corrections + two refinements + one addition** that needed to land as skill content. (1) **CORRECTION — `_phase_p_clickhouse` docstring lied**. The "Architecture:" header claimed "hash-bucketed pagination via `cityHash64(project) % N`, ~30 s across N HTTP POSTs" — that's the design v8.16.0 *originally* shipped. Live testing during v8.16.0 implementation surfaced ClickHouse Play's ~1,000-row aggregated-response cap + sustained-burst HTTP-500 rate-limit (verified 2026-06-12), and the code pivoted to single-query top-N with `LIMIT 1000`. The function body shipped correct (lines 6394-6402); only the docstring header described the abandoned design. Same lie propagated into `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` line 233-235. Both fixed to describe the actually-shipped single-query top-N architecture with the operational-constraint reason for the pivot. The v8.16.0 CHANGELOG entry retains the bucket-pagination language as immutable history (per the v8.15.1 erratum-banner discipline) — readers cross-referencing the entry to the code/docs now see the correction. (2) **CORRECTION — coverage caveat was missing from `atlas-actionable-intelligence.md`**. ClickHouse default ships ~1,000 rows ≈ 3.3 % of the ~30k `pypi_intelligence` candidate slice; the other 96.7 % carry `downloads_30d`/`downloads_90d = NULL`. NULL here means "not in top-1,000 by 90-day downloads" NOT "zero downloads". Consumers building demand-side filters (`pypi-intelligence --min-downloads N`, `conda_forge_readiness`-based ranking, `pypi-only-candidates` sort) without checking `downloads_source = 'clickhouse-clickpy'` first will treat missing-data as zero-demand and silently disqualify the long tail of legitimately-low-traffic packages. New row added to the actionable-intelligence catalog ("Phase P download-source provenance + coverage caveat") that surfaces both the provenance column and the consumer-side check. (3) **REFINEMENT — extend v8.15.1's verify-quantitative-claims rule from cost-only to coverage/cardinality**. v8.15.1 SKILL.md Operating Principle #6 bullet 4 made cost/scan/duration/count claims subject to "cite a verifiable source or carry a verified $DATE marker". v8.16.0 demonstrated the same failure mode applies to **coverage claims** — the spec said "ClickHouse delivers top-1,000 packages" without quantifying the denominator (`top-1,000 of ~30k candidates ≈ 3.3 %`), and the consumer surface didn't gain a corresponding caveat until this retro. New `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10 sub-bullet (d) "Coverage/cardinality claims need a verifiable denominator" formalizes the rule: numerator + denominator + provenance column + consumer-side caveat, all four together, at ship time. This generalizes the gap so future phases with partial coverage get the discipline at intake, not at retro. (4) **REFINEMENT — `pypi_downloads_daily` is dead code under the default backend**. Schema v26's per-day side table (v8.15.0) only populates when `PHASE_P_SOURCE=bigquery`. Under default ClickHouse it stays at 0 rows forever (verified: 2026-06-13 full refresh, table empty). Documented in `atlas-phases-overview.md` so future engineers don't add code paths assuming the table is populated; the v8.15.0 incremental architecture is preserved for operators on the BigQuery opt-in path. (5) **ADDITION — Pyright `# type: ignore` on the `autotick_bot` fallback import** so the backwards-compat code path (kept for operators pinned to pre-0.16 `conda-forge-metadata`) doesn't surface as a reportMissingImports diagnostic. **Bootstrap-data end-to-end validation results** (2026-06-13, this session, `--profile admin` run completing after the v8.16.1 PATCH ship): **DB final state** — schema v26, 1.39 GB; **all 15 phases ran cleanly** through Phase N. **Per-phase outcomes**: B/B.5/B.6 → 33,151 active packages of 33,380 total (B.5 in 3.5s, B.6 in 0.0s); **C (parselmouth join, the v8.16.1 fix)** → 1.6s, 11,944 conda↔PyPI matches; D → 16.0s; O (pypi_universe serial-snapshot deltas) → 15.4s, 828,604 snapshot rows + 828,604 intelligence upserts; **P (ClickHouse top-N) → 1.6s, $0**, 1,000 rows upserted, `downloads_source='clickhouse-clickpy'`; Q (cross-channel presence) → 11.2s, 2,149 matches across bioconda/pytorch/nvidia/robostack; R (per-project JSON enrichment for candidate slice) → 176.3s, 4,984 fetched / 0 failed / 16 404; S (computed conda_forge_readiness scores) → 0.8s, 30,344 scored (12,515 high / 15,646 medium / 1,629 low / 554 very-low / 891,720 unscored); E (cf-graph enrichment) → 47.4s, 31,845 enriched, 5,869 pypi_url matches; E.5 (archived feedstocks) → 11.6s, 774 marked archived; **F (per-package downloads from anaconda.org API) → 4,956.4s ≈ 83 min**, 32,413 fetched / 0 failed / 0 404 — Phase F dominates wall-clock by an order of magnitude over every other phase; G (vdb risk-summary cache) ran; G' (per-version vuln scoring) ran; H (PyPI current-version via pypi.org JSON) → 704.8s ≈ 12 min, 19,167 fetched / 0 failed / 87 404, 21,053 history snapshot rows; J (cf-graph dependency parse) → 17.6s, 27,716 feedstocks / 297,310 edges (skipped 7 self-refs, 773 archived/inactive); K (VCS upstream-version via GitHub/GitLab/Codeberg GraphQL+REST) → 1,780.7s ≈ 30 min, 23,184 fetched / 104 failed / 2,213 404-or-no-tags / 486 no-repo (by host: GitHub 25,104 / GitLab 381 / Codeberg 16), 23,227 history snapshot rows; L (extra-registry: npm/CRAN/CPAN/LuaRocks/crates/RubyGems/NuGet/Maven) → 55.2s, 375 fetched (npm 198 / RubyGems 165 / crates 10 / Maven 2); M (feedstock health from cf-graph pr_info) → 15.0s, 30,883 rows updated, 0 flagged bad, 434 bot-stuck; N (GitHub live-data fetch: CI/issues/PRs) → 851.0s ≈ 14 min, 27,509 feedstocks across 1,101 batches, 2 failed. **Final populated tables**: packages 33,380 / pypi_universe 828,604 / pypi_intelligence 922,065 / **pypi_downloads_daily 0 (unused under ClickHouse default — validates Phase P architecture decision)** / upstream_versions 46,973 / dependencies 296,939 / package_version_downloads 409,735 / package_version_vulns 404,042. **Notable operational finding**: the `bootstrap-data --profile admin` wrapper's 7,200s (2h) wall-clock timeout fired during Phase K and printed `✗ cf-atlas-build` in the bootstrap summary — but the underlying Python subprocess (PID 598368) continued uninterrupted through K/L/M/N to clean exit. Operators who rely on the wrapper's exit code to gate downstream steps will see a false failure; the actual atlas is complete. Fix candidate (deferred — not blocking): bump the wrapper timeout to ≥10,800s (3h) to accommodate Phase F's ~83 min + Phase K's ~30 min + Phase N's ~14 min sequential runtime, OR break the cf-atlas-build step into per-phase wrapper invocations so each phase reports independently. Documentation only this session — leave the orchestrator timeout for the next minor. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.16.2.

**v8.16.1** (Jun 13, 2026) — **Fix `autotick_bot` → `conda_forge_bot` import rename for conda-forge-metadata 0.16.x**. **PATCH bump** — 2-line bug fix for an upstream rename that broke Phase C (Parselmouth join) and `update-mapping-cache`. Pre-existing bug surfaced by the v8.16.0 closeout's `bootstrap-data --profile admin` run, which is the first thing in the session that actually exercised the import path; Pyright had been flagging the import for the entire session but unit tests didn't catch it because Phase C's import is gated behind a `try/except RuntimeError` that only fires when the function is invoked. **Root cause**: `conda-forge-metadata 0.16.1` (pinned in `pixi.toml` as `>=0.16.1`) renamed its `autotick_bot` submodule to `conda_forge_bot` upstream. Verified via `pkgutil.iter_modules` — the installed package has submodules `['_version', 'artifact_info', 'conda_forge_bot', 'feedstock_outputs', 'libcfgraph', 'oci', 'repodata', 'streaming', 'types']`, no `autotick_bot`. The new path `conda_forge_metadata.conda_forge_bot.pypi_to_conda.get_pypi_name_mapping` works and returns 11,962 mappings (verified live; same as the old function signature). **Fix**: two import sites get a try-new-then-fall-back-to-old chain so the code runs against both pre- and post-rename conda-forge-metadata releases: `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py:1414` (Phase C — Parselmouth join) + `scripts/mapping_manager.py:48` (`update-mapping-cache` CLI). **Live verification**: re-ran `bootstrap-data --profile admin` after the fix. Phase C now completes in 1.6s with 11,944 conda rows matched to PyPI (was: RuntimeError before fix). Phase D, E (47.4s, 31,845 rows enriched, 5,869 pypi_url matches), E.5 (859 archived feedstocks marked), P (1.6s ClickHouse top-N, $0), Q (11.2s, 2,149 cross-channel matches), R (176.3s, 4,984 PyPI JSON enrichments), and S (0.8s, 30,344 readiness scores: 12,515 high / 15,646 medium / 1,629 low / 554 very-low / 891,720 unscored) all succeeded. F/G/G'/H/J/K/L/M/N continued in background after PATCH ship; the import fix didn't touch any of them. **Discovery procedure**: in this case, the `pkgutil.iter_modules` probe of the installed package's submodules was the diagnostic step that turned an opaque ModuleNotFoundError into a 1-minute fix. Worth remembering for future upstream-rename-induced import failures. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.16.1.

**v8.16.0** (Jun 13, 2026) — **ERRATUM (v8.16.2 + v8.16.5):** the "Architecture: cityHash64(project) % 30 bucket-paginated 30 HTTP POSTs covering 867,391 projects in ~30 s" language in this entry describes the design that was *originally specified*, not what shipped. Live testing during implementation surfaced ClickHouse Play's ~1,000-row aggregated-response cap + sustained-burst HTTP-500 rate-limit; the code pivoted to single-query top-N with `LIMIT 1000` (~2 s, ~1,000 packages = ~3.3 % of `pypi_intelligence` candidates). The function body shipped correct; the docstring, reference doc, and this entry retained the abandoned design's language. Corrected in `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py:_phase_p_clickhouse` docstring + `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` Phase P section + new coverage-caveat row in `reference/atlas-actionable-intelligence.md` (all v8.16.2). The v8.16.5 retro generalized this into `reference/atlas-phase-engineering.md` § 10 sub-rule (f) "Docstring + reference doc MUST match shipped code at ship time." Body preserved below as historical context per the immutable-history discipline. — **Phase P free top-N source via ClickHouse clickpy + PHASE_P_SOURCE dispatcher**. **MINOR bump** — additive: new ClickHouse backend, dispatcher via `PHASE_P_SOURCE`, BigQuery moves to opt-in. **Default cost for Phase P drops from $22–59/refresh to $0**, with the trade-off that ClickHouse delivers top-1,000 packages by 90-day downloads rather than full ~870k coverage (verified 2026-06-12 — ClickHouse Play's ~1,000-row response cap on aggregated queries + aggressive rate-limit on sustained bursts make full-coverage paginated refresh impractical at ~25 min wall-clock with 95% retry-driven cost; the single-query top-N is what's actually viable). Driver: v8.15.2 closeout retro's L1 live BQ verification surfaced (a) the project on free tier had its 1 TB monthly quota exhausted, and (b) the user asked to explore other free options. Verified 2026-06-12 that ClickHouse Cloud hosts a free public mirror of the same PyPI download data at `sql-clickhouse.clickhouse.com/?user=play` via `pypi.pypi_downloads_per_day` — a pre-aggregated (date, project, count) materialized view that's exactly the shape Phase P needs. Sub-2-second 90-day full-namespace aggregate queries (867,391 projects); $0; no auth; no billing; same source data (ClickHouse Cloud mirrors `bigquery-public-data.pypi.file_downloads` daily). **Architecture**: `phase_p_pypi_downloads` becomes a dispatcher that routes via `PHASE_P_SOURCE` (default `clickhouse`, opt-in `bigquery`). New `_phase_p_clickhouse` helper paginates by `cityHash64(project) % 30` to fit under the play user's 65,000 row response cap (30 buckets of ~29k rows; 2× headroom). HTTP POST with FORMAT JSONEachRow, JSON parse line-by-line, accumulate into `{pypi_name: (d30, d90)}` dict with PEP 503 canonicalization (matches BQ backend's regex), single `BEGIN/COMMIT` for the upsert into `pypi_intelligence`. `downloads_source = 'clickhouse-clickpy'`. No `pypi_downloads_daily` writes — since ClickHouse is free, incremental refresh has no cost benefit; each run is a full pull. v8.15.2 `_phase_p_bigquery` body extracted intact (rename only; behavior unchanged); duplicate `PHASE_P_DISABLED/ENABLED` gate checks removed from BQ backend since the dispatcher handles them. **New env vars**: `PHASE_P_SOURCE` (default `clickhouse`); `PHASE_P_CH_BASE_URL` (default `https://sql-clickhouse.clickhouse.com/?user=play`; enterprise mirror override); `PHASE_P_CH_BUCKETS` (default 30; raise if cap-warn appears); `PHASE_P_CH_TIMEOUT_S` (default 180). **Trade-offs documented** in `reference/atlas-phase-p-cost-model.md` § "Source backends" + § "ClickHouse (free, default)": ClickHouse strictly better when raw event data isn't needed (which is the case for all current Phase P consumers — `conda_forge_readiness`, `pypi-only-candidates`, `pypi-intelligence`); BigQuery remains opt-in for operators wanting per-installer/per-platform/per-Python breakdowns or independence from ClickHouse Cloud's hosting. Fallback procedure documented (set `PHASE_P_SOURCE=bigquery` + `PHASE_P_BQ_PROJECT` + `PHASE_P_MAX_COST_USD=25`). **13 new tests** in new `test_phase_p_clickhouse.py`: dispatcher routing (default-is-clickhouse, disabled-priority, unknown-source-skip, case-insensitive), query shape (cityHash64 bucket, pre-agg table, d30+d90 sums, JSONEachRow), HTTP mock E2E (upsert correctness + PEP 503 collapse, URL overridable, urlopen error → skip with bucket identified, 65k cap warn, non-JSON line tolerance). Existing 18 BigQuery tests updated: source-grep targets changed to `_phase_p_bigquery`; behavioral tests gain `bq_source` fixture that sets `PHASE_P_SOURCE=bigquery` so the dispatcher routes to BQ path. 50/50 Phase P-related tests pass (18 BQ + 13 CH + 14 daily + 5 meta). **Annual cost projection update**: pre-fix ~$710/yr; v8.15.2 BQ monthly $322/yr; **v8.16.0 ClickHouse $0/yr** (verified). **Risk**: single-vendor dependency on ClickHouse Cloud continuing to host the free dataset. Mitigation: fallback path documented; if ClickHouse changes terms, operators set `PHASE_P_SOURCE=bigquery` and pay BQ rates again. **Validates the v8.15.1 retro's R1 principle a second time** — the live BQ verification not only caught the v8.15.2 SQL bug, it also surfaced that a strictly-better free alternative existed (which the v8.1.0 → v8.15.0 chain never explored). The cross-skill auto-memory rule `feedback_bmad_verifies_spec_cost_claims.md` would have caught this gap at v8.1.0 intake. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.16.0.

**v8.15.2** (Jun 12, 2026) — **Phase P SQL hot-fix + verified-2026-06-12 cost numbers**. **PATCH bump** — same-session follow-up to v8.15.1's retro, validating the retro's own R1 discipline rule (Verify, Don't Assume — quantitative claims need a verifiable source) by catching two errors the v8.14.3 + v8.15.0 work shipped: (1) the SQL was broken on this table; (2) the cost numbers were estimated rather than verified. The retro's R1 mandate triggered a live BQ dry-run preflight, which caught both. **The principle works — caught its first regression in the very next session.** **What was broken**: (1) v8.14.3's hot-patch switched the partition filter from `WHERE timestamp >= TIMESTAMP_SUB(CURRENT_TIMESTAMP(), INTERVAL N DAY)` to `WHERE _PARTITIONDATE >= DATE '...'` based on the assumption that `_PARTITIONDATE` would guarantee partition pruning. But `_PARTITIONDATE` is a pseudo-column that only exists on **ingestion-time-partitioned** tables; `bigquery-public-data.pypi.file_downloads` is **column-partitioned** on the `timestamp` column directly (verified via `table.time_partitioning = TimePartitioning(field='timestamp', type_='DAY')`). The query raised `400 Unrecognized name: _PARTITIONDATE` at submit time. v8.15.0 inherited the bug. No real Phase P run could ever have succeeded against v8.14.3/v8.15.0 — only the dry-run preflight ever ran (and aborted with $0 bill due to the cap, hiding the SQL error in normal operation; live dry-run revealed it). **What v8.15.2 fixes**: SQL switches back to filtering on the `timestamp` column with `TIMESTAMP` literals (the v8.1.0 form, but with literal bounds instead of `TIMESTAMP_SUB(CURRENT_TIMESTAMP(), INTERVAL)`); per-day GROUP BY uses `DATE(timestamp)` as the day column. End-to-end live verification confirmed: dry-run succeeds, returns `total_bytes_processed`, cap-abort fires correctly, mode-detection works, schema v26 migration works on fresh DB. **Verified-2026-06-12 cost numbers via live dry-run preflight** (replacing the v8.14.3 + v8.15.0 estimates that were off by 3-4×): (a) 90-day first-pull: **~9.5 TB scanned, ~$59 at $6.25/TB** (not "~2.5–4 TB / $15–25" as v8.14.3 claimed); (b) 30-day monthly refresh: **~3.5 TB, ~$22** (not "~$0.30–2"); (c) 7-day weekly refresh: ~860 GB, ~$5.37; (d) 1-day daily refresh: ~140 GB, ~$0.88. Table size: **1.14 PB** (2,904 billion rows). **Cap implication**: $10 default refresh cap does NOT fit monthly cadence — operators on monthly cadence must `PHASE_P_MAX_COST_USD=25`, OR use weekly cadence (`PHASE_P_TTL_DAYS=7`), OR use daily cadence (`PHASE_P_TTL_DAYS=1`). The user's stated tolerance ($10/refresh) was preserved by keeping the default cap as documented — the operator-explicit opt-in to higher cap or different cadence is the discipline-respecting fix. **Corrected annual cost projection** (also verified-2026-06-12): pre-fix 12 monthly × $59 = ~$710/year; v8.15.2 weekly cadence 52 × $5.37 + $59 first-pull = ~**$338/year**; v8.15.2 monthly cadence with raised cap 12 × $22 + $59 = ~**$322/year**; v8.15.2 daily cadence 365 × $0.88 + $59 = ~**$380/year**. The previous "~$30/year" claim was wrong on two counts: cost-per-refresh underestimate (20×) + baseline confusion. The v8.15.x incremental architecture STILL saves significantly vs. the pre-fix re-scan-everything pattern (~$370/year saved at weekly cadence). **Docs touched**: `scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` (Phase P SQL + docstring cost profile); `tests/unit/test_phase_p_bigquery.py` (2 tests updated to assert the corrected SQL pattern + new negative assertion that `_PARTITIONDATE` does NOT appear); `reference/atlas-phase-p-cost-model.md` (full rewrite of TL;DR table + why-it-was-wrong section + dry-run preflight example + annual cost projection); `reference/atlas-phases-overview.md` (Phase P bullet); `quickref/commands-cheatsheet.md` (Cost section); `SKILL.md` (the operating-principle bullet text gains the verified-2026-06-12 reference). **Tests**: 32/32 pass after SQL fix; live end-to-end verification successful via `PHASE_P_BQ_PROJECT=... PHASE_P_ENABLED=1 PHASE_P_MAX_COST_FIRST_PULL_USD=0.01 python -m conda_forge_atlas` against fresh schema-v26 DB. **Auto-memory `feedback_bmad_verifies_spec_cost_claims.md`** validated by this session: the cross-skill rule shipped in v8.15.1, the very next live verification caught two real bugs. Should not be amended (works as designed); the validation is the v8.15.2 changelog entry itself. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.15.2.
