**v8.11.1** (Jun 2, 2026) — Legacy-path cleanup + `recipe_editor.py` line-fold fix. Caps the npm-generator correction arc that ran v8.10.0 → v8.10.1 → v8.11.0 → v8.11.1 over 5 days (May 26 → Jun 2). **PATCH bump** — internal cleanup; default-path behaviour unchanged.

The full arc in one paragraph: v8.10.0 (2026-05-26, MINOR) dropped `context.name` from Python v1 recipes, switching `package.name` and `source.url` to fully-literal forms with only `${{ version }}` interpolated, matching current grayskull. v8.10.1 (2026-06-02, PATCH) fixed three coupled npm bugs from PR #33358 reviewer feedback: `source.url` now uses `${{ version }}` templating (autotick correctness), `build.sh` uses `${PKG_VERSION}`, and the tee command quotes `${PREFIX}` (SC2086). v8.11.0 (2026-06-02, MINOR) **flipped the npm generator default** from `noarch: generic` + standalone `build.sh` + tee Windows shim to **per-platform inline build** with `build.script: + if: unix / then / else` branches matching openspec PR #32368 + bmalph PR #33557 attempt-2. The pre-v8.11.0 noarch:generic pattern was structurally broken on current staged-recipes CI (rattler-build symlink-portability check + missing build.bat on Windows leg). bmalph #33557 attempt 2 verified the new pattern: linux_64 3m17s / osx_64 6m14s / win_64 3m20s green. v8.11.1 deleted the legacy `--no-inline-build` escape hatch + dead code (5 helpers, 4 CLI flags, 2 tests) — keeping a known-broken path for back-compat was a maintenance liability with zero real users. v8.11.1 also fixed `edit_recipe`'s line-fold cosmetic bug (`yaml.width = 4096`).

Per-release detail below. Auto-memory `canonical_npm_recipe_pattern.md` is the live reference for the v8.11.0+ npm recipe shape; auto-memory `feedback_pypi_conda_mapping_unreliable.md` is the live reference for the four-form name-divergence check codified in v8.11.2's G10 and broadened in v8.11.4.

**v8.11.8** (Jun 9, 2026) — Recipe-authoring gotcha **G15** + Build Failure Protocol diagnostic chain + three diff-before-apply categorization refinements, all from the `conda-forge/ag-ui-langgraph-feedstock` PR #22 fix retro. **PATCH bump** — additive: one new SKILL.md gotcha + one BFP sub-section + three sub-workflow bullets + CHANGELOG entry; no generator, template, or optimizer code change. (1) **New gotcha G15 — "Rebuilding the same recipe re-hashes the `.conda` artifact but leaves `repodata.json` stale"** documents the trap that surfaces during cross-package local fix workflows. rattler-build embeds the build timestamp into the `.conda` zip's central directory; a second build of the same recipe sources on the same machine produces an artifact with identical contents but different bytes (timestamp differs) → different sha256. The normal write path updates `repodata.json` atomically, but the failure mode appears when the index update doesn't fire on the second run (the internal index cache thinks the prior hash is current). Downstream builds then resolve via repodata → expect hash A → read the file → get hash B → `hash mismatch when extracting file://...` error. Fix: `rm build_artifacts/<config>/noarch/<pkg>-<ver>-<build>.conda` then re-invoke `rattler-build build` — a fresh build writes artifact AND updates `repodata.json` atomically. Case study: `ag-ui-langgraph 0.0.41` fix session — bumped `ag-ui-a2ui-toolkit` 0.0.2 → 0.0.3, built it (first build wrote artifact + indexed), then re-ran the same build command to capture the test-passed log in a grep-friendly form. The second build wrote new artifact bytes but repodata still pointed at the first build's hash. The `ag-ui-langgraph 0.0.41` build then failed at the test phase with `hash mismatch when extracting file:///.../ag-ui-a2ui-toolkit-0.0.3-pyhc364b38_0.conda: expected 85ea90d5..., got 766570d75...`. `rm` + rebuild ag-ui-a2ui-toolkit refreshed repodata; downstream build resolved 0.0.3 cleanly and tests passed. G15 also notes that `pixi run rattler-index` is **not** a bound task in this skill's pixi env — invoking it through pixi just dumps the task list rather than running `rattler-index fs <channel-path>`; the rebuild path is the practical re-index. (2) **New Build Failure Protocol § "Diagnostic chain for feedstock CI test failures"** codifies the 5-step diagnosis that resolves most ImportError-class test-phase failures on existing feedstocks: (a) `gh run view <run-id> --log-failed | tail -200` for the exact ImportError; (b) `WebFetch(pypi.org/pypi/<name>/json)` to cross-check upstream `[project.dependencies]` lower bounds; (c) `lookup_feedstock(pkg_name=<offending-dep>)` to check if conda-forge is behind; (d) confirm CI's test Python version from the resolution table (newest-cpython resolution silently bypasses `python_min` verification); (e) bump the recipe's lower bound to match upstream's minimum. Most cases resolve at step (b) — the failure pattern is virtually always "upstream advanced a transitive lower bound; recipe didn't follow." Case study: PR #22 failed with `ImportError: cannot import name 'A2UIGuidelines' from 'ag_ui_a2ui_toolkit'`; upstream `pyproject.toml` had `ag-ui-a2ui-toolkit>=0.0.3` (A2UIGuidelines added in 0.0.3); recipe pinned `>=0.0.2`. One-line fix. (3) **Three new special-case categorizations in the v8.11.7 diff-before-apply sub-workflow**: (3a) "Test `requirements.run:` missing a `python` pin → ALWAYS a correction to apply" — the optimizer's `SEL-002` doesn't flag the missing pin on script-tests (only python-test-blocks); without `python ${{ python_min }}.*` the solver resolves to the newest cpython and `python_min` verification is silently skipped. Symptom in CI: resolution table shows `python 3.14.5 ... cp314` for a recipe with `python_min: 3.10`. (3b) "Upstream's explicit `requires-python = "<X,>=Y"` upper bound → a correction to apply when migrating from speculative `<4.0`" — tightening to upstream's declared maximum (`<3.15` for `requires-python = "<3.15,>=3.10"`) matches the wheel build matrix. `DEP-002` flags it but should be acknowledged as a trade-off: upstream-explicit upper bounds are accepted by reviewers; `DEP-002`'s "move to run_constrained" suggestion is for speculative upper bounds, not upstream-declared ones. (3c) "Run-dep lower-bound bumps where upstream's `pyproject.toml` advanced → check the dep's feedstock state first" — when the new version isn't on conda-forge yet, the fix becomes 2-step (bump the prerequisite feedstock first, then the consumer); local verification needs both built so v8.2.0's local-channel auto-inject can resolve. Cross-links G15 for the rebuild-hash trap that surfaces during these 2-step workflows. (4) **CHANGELOG-only observation — optimizer SEL-002 misfires on script-based tests**. SEL-002 checks for `python_version: ${{ python_min }}.*` in `tests[].python:` blocks but doesn't recognize the equivalent pinning when the recipe uses a script-test with `tests[].requirements.run: [python ${{ python_min }}.*]`. False positive for any noarch:python recipe that uses script-tests instead of python-tests. The ag-ui-langgraph recipe correctly pins the test python via `requirements.run:` (after correction #2) but SEL-002 still fires. Optimizer fix flagged for a future maintainer pass — `_check_sel_002` needs to also accept the `python ${{ python_min }}.*` form in script-test `requirements.run:`. (5) **CHANGELOG-only observation — `pixi run rattler-index` task missing from the skill's pixi env**. Tried as the cleanest re-index path for G15; pixi printed the task list instead. The `rattler-index` binary exists in the env (`pixi run -e local-recipes rattler-index fs <path>` would work as a direct invocation) but the bare `pixi run -e local-recipes rattler-index` doesn't resolve. Could be added as a thin task in `pixi.toml` for ergonomic re-indexing, but the rebuild path in G15 is more reliable (atomic with the recipe's actual state). (6) **Verified existing guidance held during the ag-ui-langgraph retro**: (6a) **v8.11.7 diff-before-apply sub-workflow worked end-to-end on its first real use after the weasyprint debut** — the move-aside + fresh-generate + enrich + diff + 3-bucket categorization sequence read cleanly; the user approved the proposed 3/0/5 categorization (3 corrections / 0 stylistic / 5 rejected regressions plus the meta.yaml deletion) in one prompt. Grayskull would have dropped `entry_points: dev = ag_ui_langgraph.dojo:main` + `run_constraints: fastapi >=0.115.12` + the `license: MIT` field (grayskull emitted empty `license:`); the 3-bucket walk caught all three regressions. (6b) **Migration Protocol § Churn Rule** correctly identified the stale v0 `meta.yaml` left alongside the v1 `recipe.yaml` as STD-002; deletion + rebuild passed cleanly. (6c) **v8.2.0 local-channel auto-inject** worked as documented — the ag-ui-langgraph build automatically resolved `ag-ui-a2ui-toolkit 0.0.3` from `build_artifacts/linux64/noarch/` without manual `--channel` flags (once G15's repodata-stale trap was resolved). (6d) **`get_build_summary` false-negative caveat** (step 8 SKILL.md note from v5.7.0) — initial native-mode trigger returned `status: "unknown"` with `"build may have crashed"`. The artifact-mtime check confirmed no 0.0.41 artifact existed (so it actually was a failure this time, not a false negative), which routed correctly to the direct-rattler-build re-run that captured the hash-mismatch error. The caveat handled both the false-negative (weasyprint v8.11.7 case) and the real-negative (this case) correctly. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.8.

**v8.11.7** (Jun 9, 2026) — Diff-before-apply sub-workflow + step-9 feedstock-vs-staged-recipes branching from the `conda-forge/weasyprint-feedstock` v67.0 → v69.0 local update retro. **PATCH bump** — additive: two SKILL.md sections + CHANGELOG entry; no generator, template, or optimizer code change. (1) **New sub-workflow section "Sub-workflow: Updating an existing recipe (diff-before-apply)"** added under Primary Workflow. Documents the move-aside + fresh-generate + `enrich_from_feedstock` + diff + 3-bucket categorization (Corrections to apply / Regressions to reject / Stylistic no-change) + present-to-user + restore-and-selective-apply pattern. The weasyprint session exercised every step: grayskull-fresh v69.0 generation dropped `pango >=1.44.0` + `glib` from `requirements.run:` (both system C-libs not visible to PyPI metadata) plus the documented workaround comment for `conda-forge/weasyprint-feedstock#23`, plus the `pip check` script test. Naive overwrite would have shipped a broken recipe. The presented diff caught all three regressions, the 6 grayskull-emitted corrections (canonical v8.10.0 `package.name`/`source.url` literal forms, PyPI-authoritative `about.summary`/`homepage`/`documentation` from `project_urls`, dropped speculative `python <4.0` upper bound), and one stylistic-no-change (`description:` formatting). User approved the 6/4/1 categorization in one prompt; restore + 2 surgical Edit calls landed cleanly; rebuild produced `weasyprint-69.0-pyhcf101f3_0.conda` (262 KiB) with `✔ all tests passed!` including `weasyprint --help` exercising the C-FFI bindings (validating that `pango` + `glib` weren't dropped). (2) **New step 9 sub-bullet "Feedstock updates branch off here"** clarifies that `submit_pr` targets `conda-forge/staged-recipes` and is correct only for **new** package submissions; for updates to an **existing** feedstock (version bumps, dep fixes, CI fixes), the PR target is `conda-forge/<name>-feedstock` directly. `lookup_feedstock(pkg_name=<name>)` returning `exists=True` is the signal — when it does, skip steps 8b + 9 and instead clone the feedstock, copy `recipes/<name>/recipe.yaml` over `recipe/recipe.yaml`, bump `build.number` (or reset to 0 on version bump), and open a PR against the feedstock. Steps 1–8 apply identically to both paths. Previously the autonomous-loop wording was staged-recipes-centric, leaving the feedstock-update workflow under-documented. (3) **Known grayskull-path emit drifts documented in the new sub-workflow** so the diff-categorization phase knows what to expect — (3a) **long `source.url` line-folded across two lines** by ruamel.yaml's default `width=80` (looks like `weasyprint-${{ version \n    }}.tar.gz`); cosmetic only, recipe still builds. The v8.11.1 line-fold fix landed in `edit_recipe` (the load-modify-dump cycle) but NOT in the grayskull subprocess emit path. The sub-workflow tells the user to restore the clean single-line form. Generator-internal fix flagged for a future maintainer pass (would need `yaml.width = 4096` in the post-grayskull normalization step). (3b) **`python_min: "3.10"` over-emit at default floor** — reconfirmed in v8.11.7 (originally flagged in v8.11.2 CHANGELOG; persists in v8.11.6's generator). The weasyprint fresh-generate also emitted it. Sub-workflow tells the user to drop it unless overriding the floor; future maintainer pass should fix `_resolve_python_min()` / `generate_recipe_yaml()` to honor the v8.8.0 design. (4) **CHANGELOG-only observation — `behind_upstream` (cf_atlas Phase D pypi-serial snapshot) returned stale v68.1 vs live PyPI v69.0**. Caught only because the user questioned the recommended version ("why 68.1 when latest is 69.0"). The atlas's pypi-serial data is a snapshot frozen at the last Phase D run; the user's local atlas was ~weeks stale. The skill's "Before recommending from memory" rule under `# auto memory` covers memory staleness but doesn't extend to atlas-recommended versions. Refinement: when `behind_upstream` is used to drive a version-bump recommendation (vs. survey-style queries like "what's behind?"), cross-check against live `WebFetch(https://pypi.org/pypi/<name>/json)` before authoring the bump — particularly for major-version lag where the cost of bumping to the wrong target version is high (rerun deps check, rerun gates). Not a SKILL.md edit in this patch; flagged for a future "Before recommending from atlas" sub-section if the pattern recurs. (5) **CHANGELOG-only observation — `update_recipe` MCP wrapper silent-failure mode**. Dry-run succeeded with the correct plan (`{actions: [update context.version, update build.number, calculate_hash source.0], success: true}`), but the real run with `dry_run=False` returned `{"success": false, "error": "recipe_editor.py failed.", "details": ""}` — no diagnostic content. Manual fallback worked: `curl + sha256sum + edit_recipe(actions=[...])` landed the bump in one call. The `recipe_editor.py failed.` message with empty `details` is a known-broken error-reporting path in the autotick MCP wrapper; the underlying script likely succeeded at the planning stage but errored during file writeback, and stderr/stdout were swallowed. Workaround: when `update_recipe` returns this message, fall back to the manual three-step (download sdist → compute sha256 → `edit_recipe` with explicit version + sha256 actions). Flagged for a future maintainer pass to surface the underlying error message in the wrapper's `details` field. (6) **Verified existing guidance held during the weasyprint retro**: (6a) **step 8 `get_build_summary` false-negative caveat** — the first build of v69.0 reported `status: "unknown"` with `"build may have crashed"` while the artifact existed at `build_artifacts/linux64/noarch/weasyprint-69.0-pyhcf101f3_0.conda` with mtime newer than build start. The SKILL.md step 8 instruction to "check `build_artifacts/<config>/<subdir>/` for `<name>-<version>-*.conda` files" worked exactly as documented. (6b) **canonical v8.10.0 patterns** (drop `context.name`, literal `package.name`, literal `source.url` path segments) were the grayskull-fresh emit's source-of-truth advantage on the diff (vs. the live feedstock's pre-v8.10.0 `${{ name[0] }}` / `${{ name }}` chain). The diff-before-apply pattern is how those canonical updates can land on a stable feedstock without churning every other section. (6c) **G10 four-form name-divergence check** correctly identified `weasyprint` as already on conda-forge under the bare name on the first call (`lookup_feedstock` returned `exists=True` immediately). (6d) **enrich_from_feedstock** correctly merged the existing feedstock's hand-curated maintainers + recipe-maintainers-emeritus list (idempotent — running it against an empty fresh recipe added the 3 maintainers cleanly). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.7.

**v8.11.6** (Jun 8, 2026) — Recipe-authoring gotcha **G14** from the `conda-forge/wagtail-ab-testing-feedstock` PR #8 fix. **PATCH bump** — additive: one new SKILL.md gotcha + CHANGELOG entry; no generator, template, or optimizer code change. (1) **New gotcha G14 — "Autotick bot v0 version bumps can fail the conda-forge-linter `package.version` float-parse rule"** documents a class of v0-meta.yaml-only failures triggered by `regro-cf-autotick-bot` PRs. The bot correctly edits the jinja `{% set version = "X.Y" %}` line but doesn't touch the YAML template `version: {{ version }}`, which renders to bare `X.Y` and is then YAML-typed as float instead of string. The lint catches this proactively. Two fixes: (a) minimal — quote at the YAML level (`version: "{{ version }}"`); (b) long-term — migrate v0 → v1, where `${{ version }}` substitution preserves the string type by construction and the lint can't fire. The bug affects already-merged feedstocks whose lint was tightened post-submission; the next autotick bump exposes it. Case study: PR #8 on `conda-forge/wagtail-ab-testing-feedstock` (autotick `0.13 → 0.14`). Local fix went straight to v1 — wrote `recipe/recipe.yaml`, updated `conda-forge.yml` with `conda_build_tool: rattler-build` + the python-cityhash-aligned bot settings (`bot.check_solvable`, `bot.run_deps_from_wheel`, `conda_install_tool: pixi`), deleted `recipe/meta.yaml` after a clean v1 rattler-build run produced `wagtail-ab-testing-0.14-pyhcf101f3_0.conda` (148 KiB). Held locally pending user decision on push strategy (bundle v1 migration + version bump in one PR vs. minimal version-quote fix to unblock bot's PR #8). (2) **Refinement to existing guidance (no SKILL.md edit yet)** — `build.skip: not linux` at the top-level of a v1 multi-output recipe applies to all outputs, and staged-recipes CI honors the directive (non-Linux build legs report SUCCESS-with-skip rather than FAILURE). Verified empirically on staged-recipes PR #33454 pixitainer with two `noarch: generic` outputs both carrying `__linux` runtime constraints. Worth a sub-section in G12 or a new G15 in a future retro if the pattern recurs. (3) **CHANGELOG-only observation — `migrate_to_v1` MCP wrapper bug**. The wrapper passes the supplied `recipe_path` directly as feedrattler's `feedstock_name` positional argument; feedrattler then tries to `gh org.get_repo(<absolute-path>)` and gets a 404. Workaround for now is direct `pixi run feedrattler <name> --local-clone-dir <path>`, or manual v1 conversion when the recipe is small. The MCP wrapper at `.claude/tools/conda_forge_server.py` (or wherever `migrate_to_v1` is bound) needs to extract the bare feedstock name from the path before invoking feedrattler. Flagged for a future maintainer pass; not fixed in this patch (touches a different part of the codebase than the gotcha addition). (4) **Verified existing guidance held**: G10 four-form name-divergence check correctly identified `wagtail-ab-testing` as already on conda-forge under the bare name (saved a redundant submission attempt — same pattern as `langfuse` / `django-lasuite` / `dockerflow` earlier). Migration Protocol § Churn Rule worked end-to-end (validate v1 → build success → delete meta.yaml). The pixitainer `build.skip: not linux` fix exercised the staged-recipes-CI-honors-skip behavior cleanly (5/5 legs reported terminal SUCCESS). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.6.

**v8.11.5** (Jun 7, 2026) — Recipe-authoring gotcha **G13** + a one-line refinement to G1, both from the staged-recipes#33647 solvor + staged-recipes grafeo session. **PATCH bump** — additive: one new SKILL.md gotcha + cross-link addition to G1 + CHANGELOG entry; no generator, template, or optimizer code change. (1) **New gotcha G13 — "CWD persists across `script:` list entries — and `(cmd)` is not a subshell on Windows cmd.exe"** documents two interlocking facts that together produced a Windows-only build failure on solvor PR #33647 (buildId 1534140 win_64). Fact A: rattler-build's script-list entries share CWD across entries — G1 documents that env vars don't carry, but **CWD does**. Fact B: on Windows cmd.exe, `(cmd1 && cmd2)` is command grouping (purely syntactic) — there is no child process, so a `cd dir` inside the parens permanently changes the parent's CWD. The combination: a bash subshell pattern `- (cd subdir && tool ...)` that works fine on Linux/macOS leaks CWD into the next entry on Windows, which then breaks (in solvor's case, pip from `$SRC_DIR\rust\` couldn't find pyproject.toml). The fix is pushd/popd — works identically in bash and cmd.exe; no `if: unix / then / else:` block needed; forward slashes in paths work on both shells. G13 also documents the maturin/PyO3 case where this comes up in practice (`[tool.maturin].manifest-path` pointing at a subdirectory Cargo.toml, since `cargo-bundle-licenses` doesn't have a `--manifest-path` flag and operates on CWD), and includes a collapsed-single-entry fallback for cases needing shell-specific syntax beyond CWD. Case study: solvor PR #33647 (initial bash-subshell fix `(cd rust && cargo-bundle-licenses --format yaml --output ../THIRDPARTY.yml)` succeeded on local Linux + CI linux_64 + CI osx_64 but failed on CI win_64; cmd prompt visible in the log as `(base) %SRC_DIR%\rust>...` confirmed CWD leak; pushd/popd replacement on commit `efd84c9ee6` went all-green across linter + linux_64 + osx_64 + win_64. (2) **G1 refinement** — one-line caveat added that distinguishes env-vars/functions (don't carry across entries, per G1's original claim) from CWD (does carry, contradicting G1's earlier offhand mention of `cd` in the same "doesn't survive" list). G1 now cross-links to G13 for the CWD-isolation pattern. (3) **CHANGELOG-only observation — v8.9.0 maturin-detection regression on solvor + grafeo**. Both packages have `[build-system].build-backend = "maturin"` declared in their pyproject.toml's, but `generate_recipe_from_pypi` produced `noarch: python` recipes (the noarch path) instead of the maturin compiled-extension path. The v8.9.0 release notes state `_generate_maturin_recipe_yaml()` is dispatched from `info.build_backend == "maturin"` — that detection appears broken for at least these two cases. Both recipes required full manual rewrites (drop noarch:python, add C+stdlib+rust compilers + cargo-bundle-licenses to build, switch run to bare `python` per conda-smithy lint rule). Flagged for a future maintainer pass to investigate `recipe-generator.py` v8.9.0's `info.build_backend` extraction path; not fixed in this patch (would need to regenerate 3+ different maturin packages to validate any fix). (4) **CHANGELOG-only observation — `cargo-bundle-licenses` lacks `--manifest-path`**. Despite skill templates mentioning the flag, the actual `cargo-bundle-licenses` binary on conda-forge errors with `error: unexpected argument '--manifest-path' found`. The tool reads CWD instead. This is why G13's pushd-to-subdir pattern is needed for `[tool.maturin].manifest-path`-not-at-root cases. Skill template references to `--manifest-path` for cargo-bundle-licenses should be removed in a follow-up — the canonical pattern is the G13 pushd/popd form. (5) **Verified existing guidance held during the solvor + grafeo session**: G10 four-form name-divergence check correctly identified `solvor` as genuinely missing (all four spellings — `solvor`, `solvor-py`, `solvor-python`, `python-solvor` — returned zero hits on conda-forge); the prerequisite-recipe-chain workflow worked end-to-end (solvor recipe → local channel auto-injection → grafeo's run dep `solvor >=0.6.1` resolved from local build_artifacts/); canonical license-file pattern 2 (in-recipe LICENSE) worked for grafeo (whose sdist omits LICENSE but the upstream GitHub LICENSE matches and was already shipped in `recipes/grafeo/LICENSE`). Solvor PR #33647 final state: all-green across linter + linux_64 + osx_64 + win_64. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.5.

**v8.11.4** (Jun 7, 2026) — G10 broadened to a four-form PyPI→conda name-divergence check after a third confirmed pattern surfaced during a suitenumerique build-report audit. **PATCH bump** — additive: G10 rewrite (title, table, check list, case studies) + auto-memory update + CHANGELOG entry; no generator/template/optimizer code change. (1) **New divergence pattern documented** — PyPI `langfuse` maps to `conda-forge/langfuse-python-feedstock` (61 noarch builds at v4.7.1 matching PyPI v4.7.1; recipe `source.url: pypi.org/packages/source/l/langfuse/langfuse-${{ version }}.tar.gz` confirms identity). The `-python` suffix appears when upstream ships a multi-language SDK family (langfuse-js, langfuse-go, etc.) and conda-forge wants to name the Python distribution explicitly. Distinct from the `-py` suffix (G10's original `wasmtime → wasmtime-py` case), which appears when the underlying runtime is itself a separately-packageable native library. (2) **G10 retitled** from "PyPI Python bindings to non-Python language runtimes use the `-py` suffix on conda-forge" to "PyPI → conda-forge name divergence — verify across four spellings before declaring a dep missing" — the original title was too narrow (langfuse is a pure-Python SDK, not a Python binding to a non-Python runtime, yet still uses a suffix). New title + body emphasize the empirical reality: the choice of `-py` vs `-python` vs underscore-preserved vs bare is a per-feedstock decision with no algorithmic rule. (3) **Check list expanded from 3 to 4 name forms** — bare PyPI name → hyphen↔underscore swap → `-py` suffix → `-python` suffix. The new Case Study 2 documents the langfuse discovery during a suitenumerique build-report audit (the 2026-05-31 SUITENUMERIQUE_SUMMARY.md listed `langfuse` as a Wave-1b conda-forge-submission-ready recipe; re-check on user prompt found it already on conda-forge as `langfuse-python` v4.7.1; Wave-1b submission count dropped 13 → 12). (4) **Auto-memory `feedback_pypi_conda_mapping_unreliable.md` updated** in parallel — three patterns now documented (underscore preserved, `-py`, `-python`); how-to-apply check list expanded from 3 to 4 forms; MEMORY.md index entry refreshed. (5) **Open work flagged**: proposed `optimize_recipe` check **DEP-005** = "PyPI name in `requirements.run:` has a `-py` or `-python` feedstock on conda-forge" — would catch the rename gap before push. Deferred — would need an extended mapping lookup in `optimize_recipe`. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.4.

**v8.11.3** (Jun 7, 2026) — Recipe-authoring gotchas G11 + G12 + step 8b refinement from the staged-recipes#33534 xorq CI-fix retro. **PATCH bump** — additive: two new SKILL.md gotcha sections + one step 8b sub-bullet + CHANGELOG entry; no generator, template, or optimizer code change. (1) **New gotcha G11 — "PyPI sdist symlinks fail hatchling's wheel build on Windows"** documents the failure pattern that caused two consecutive Windows CI failures (Azure buildId 1533937 + 1533940) on the xorq 0.3.26 recipe. Upstream PyPI sdists can ship POSIX symlinks via tar's symlink record; Linux + macOS build agents extract them natively but Windows Azure runners lack `SeCreateSymbolicLinkPrivilege` by default, so tar's extraction falls back to writing a text stub containing the literal target path. Hatchling's `os.stat` on that stub fails with `WinError 123 / ERROR_INVALID_NAME`. The fix extends the recipe's downstream pyproject.toml patch with a `[tool.hatch.build.targets.wheel]` exclude entry for the offending symlinked path; the symlink target file remains in the wheel under its real path so test discovery still works. G11 documents the symptom (exact error message + path format), the underlying Windows symlink-extraction semantics, the targeted-vs-broad fix tradeoff (`**/conftest.py` globs strip too much), a preventive `tar tvz | grep '^l'` one-liner to flag the risk before pushing to CI, and the distinction from G6 (which fires at rattler-build's noarch-Windows-portability check *after* the wheel is built; G11 fires *during* hatchling's wheel build itself, before validation runs). Case study: xorq's single sdist symlink at `python/xorq/common/utils/tests/conftest.py` → `../../../backends/xorq_datafusion/tests/conftest.py`; fix added that one path to the exclude list; Azure buildId 1533952 win_64 GREEN. (2) **New gotcha G12 — "Platform-conditional `run:` deps in noarch:python recipes need `noarch_platforms` in `conda-forge.yml`"** documents conda-smithy's `lint_noarch_selectors` rule (R1-002) and its documented v1 escape hatch. The rule fires on `if: <platform> / then:` selectors in `requirements.run:` of noarch:python recipes — including correct rattler-build v1 syntax for gating platform-conditional runtime deps (which the conda solver evaluates at install time, not build time). The escape hatch: declare `noarch_platforms` with >=2 entries in a per-recipe `conda-forge.yml`. Researched via `Explore` subagent against `conda-smithy/linter/lint_recipe.py` line 302 (`if "lint_noarch_selectors" not in lints_to_skip`); v1 path in `conda_recipe_v1_linter.py` → `lint_usage_of_selectors_for_noarch()` with message class `NoarchSelectorsV1`. G12 documents the symptom (full lint message), the rule's intent (catching build-time selector mistakes; runtime selectors in `run:` are a false-positive trap), the canonical fix (with full example conda-forge.yml content + minimum 2-platform requirement), and the case where the rule is correctly rejecting your recipe (build-time selectors in `script:`, `build.skip:`, `host:`, `build:` — at which point you actually do need to drop `noarch: python`). Case study: xorq added `noarch_platforms: [linux_64, osx_64, win_64]` after G11's symlink patch made all three viable; final CI run (head `0be2b938e4`) went all-green. (3) **Step 8b sub-bullet refinement** — `prepare_submission_branch` hardcodes the commit message to "Add recipe for <name>", which is misleading for any commit other than the initial submission (CI fixes, reviewer feedback, version bumps). Documented the direct-git fallback for follow-up commits on an existing PR branch: `git -C <fork> checkout <pr-branch>` + copy updated files + descriptive commit + `git push origin <branch>`. The fork path is reported by `prepare_submission_branch(dry_run=True)` as the `fork_path` field. Also cross-linked the existing "Optional add-on: conda-forge.yml" sub-bullet to G12, noting that `noarch_platforms` is also required to silence `lint_noarch_selectors` (not just to extend the CI matrix). (4) **Verified existing guidance held during the xorq retro**: Migration Protocol § Churn Rule (delete stale meta.yaml alongside a successful v1 recipe.yaml build) worked exactly as documented — STD-002 fired locally, deletion + rebuild passed, artifact unchanged. `validate_recipe`'s separation of rattler-build lint vs conda-smithy lint correctly surfaced the v1 lint divergence (rattler-build accepted the selector; conda-smithy blocked it). Two proposed `optimize_recipe` checks flagged as open work: **DEP-004** = `requirements.run:` lists a dep with no conda-forge build on one or more platforms (would have caught the git-annex platform-coverage issue locally; needs atlas integration to know which platforms a dep is missing on); **NOARCH-001** = noarch:python recipe has `if: <platform>` selectors in `run:` but no `conda-forge.yml` with `noarch_platforms` >=2 entries (would have flagged the conda-smithy lint trap before push; needs `conda-forge.yml` parsing). Both deferred — would need new check implementations. PR #33534 final state: head `0be2b938e4`, all 6 checks GREEN (linter, conda-forge-linter, build linux_64, build osx osx_64, build win_64 win, umbrella), 3-commit fix sequence on top of the existing PR head. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.3.

**v8.11.2** (Jun 7, 2026) — Recipe-authoring gotcha G10 + generator-drift observation from the `simonw/micropython-wasm` packaging retro. **PATCH bump** — additive: one new SKILL.md section + one CHANGELOG observation; no generator or template code change. (1) **New gotcha G10 — "PyPI Python bindings to non-Python language runtimes use the `-py` suffix on conda-forge"** documents the divergence pattern that caused a false-alarm "wasmtime is missing from conda-forge" scoping mistake during initial scoping for `simonw/micropython-wasm`. Manual repodata search for the bare PyPI name `wasmtime` returned 0 hits across all 7 platforms checked; the real feedstock is `wasmtime-py` (39 builds × 5 platforms at v45.0.0; `conda-forge/wasmtime-py-feedstock` pushed 2026-05-26). The `-py` suffix is distinct from the underscore-preserved pattern (G7's `tree_sitter` case) — both are real conda-forge naming conventions for different scenarios. G10 lists the three name forms to check before declaring a dep missing (bare PyPI name → hyphen↔underscore swap → `-py` suffix) and notes that `check_dependencies` does the lookup correctly via the grayskull mapping cache while manual repodata searches do not. The optimizer does not flag the divergence today — recipes hand-emitted by grayskull with `requirements.run: [..., wasmtime]` will pass `optimize_recipe` and `validate_recipe` but fail `check_dependencies` against the real `wasmtime-py`. Closing the optimizer gap (a new `DEP-003` "PyPI name in run requirements has a known `-py`-suffix feedstock on conda-forge") is open work. Auto-memory `feedback_pypi_conda_mapping_unreliable.md` updated in parallel with the wasmtime case (cross-skill methodology; lives in auto-memory, not in the skill, because the check applies beyond recipe authoring). (2) **Observation — `generate_recipe_from_pypi` still emits `python_min: "3.10"` in `context:` even at the default conda-forge floor**, contradicting the v8.8.0 changelog claim that "python_min: in context is conditionally emitted only when the conda-forge floor (3.10) is exceeded — at the default it's now omitted, matching what 26/30 sampled PRs do". The generated `recipes/micropython-wasm/recipe.yaml` has `python_min: "3.10"` at line 5 unnecessarily; this is one line of cosmetic noise per generated recipe at the default floor. Recipe is still valid (the optimizer's SEL-002 only fires when `python_min` is missing entirely; it does not fire when `python_min` is present at the default). Flagged here for a future maintainer pass to determine whether the v8.8.0 fix didn't land for the grayskull subprocess path, was reverted, or has a regression in `_resolve_python_min()` / `generate_recipe_yaml()`; no generator fix in this patch (would need a multi-recipe regression run to validate without breaking the higher-floor path). (3) **Verified existing guidance held during the `micropython-wasm` build**: G7 sdist-driven import-name check (`tar tzf <sdist> | grep '__init__.py$'`) confirmed `micropython_wasm` as the correct import name on the first try (matches the trivial hyphen→underscore transform but G7 says verify anyway); canonical CFEP-25 test triad emitted correctly by the generator; license-file placement pattern 1 (upstream archive ships LICENSE) worked as documented in the canonical license-file critical-constraint section; all four pre-build gates (`validate_recipe` / `optimize_recipe` / `check_dependencies` / `scan_for_vulnerabilities`) returned 0 issues. The single-recipe `noarch: python` `micropython-wasm` recipe was generated, hand-edited (one `wasmtime` → `wasmtime-py` rename per G10), built (190 KB `.conda` with bundled 363 KB `micropython-wasi.wasm` blob), installed in a fresh `/tmp/test-micropython-wasm` prefix from the local channel, and tested end-to-end (MicroPython actually executed inside the WASM sandbox via conda-forge's `wasmtime-py 45.0.0`, computing `2**10 = 1024` and printing from inside the sandbox) without any other skill-internal drift. **v8.11.1** (Jun 2, 2026) — Legacy-path cleanup + `edit_recipe` line-fold fix. **PATCH bump** — internal cleanup; no behaviour change for the default path. Two follow-ups from v8.11.0's bmalph + yo CI runs. (1) `recipe_editor.py` line-fold fix — `ruamel.yaml`'s default `width=80` was folding long YAML strings (e.g. `pnpm-licenses generate-disclaimer --prod --output-file=third-party-licenses.txt`) into 2-line continuations during the load-modify-dump cycle of `edit_recipe`. Set `yaml.width = 4096` so single-line items stay single-line. Caught when the IDE selection of `recipes/yo/recipe.yaml` showed the fold after `edit_recipe` was used to swap the `MAINTAINER` placeholder. (2) Removed the legacy `--no-inline-build` escape hatch + its dead code. The legacy path (noarch:generic + standalone build.sh + tee Windows shim) was kept "for back-compat" in v8.11.0 but it's BROKEN on current staged-recipes CI — that's why bmalph and yo PRs failed before the v8.11.0 refactor. Keeping a known-broken path adds maintenance burden with no real users. Dropped: `_build_sh_template` function, `_template_npm_tarball_filename` helper, `inline_build` + `with_build_bat` + `no_bin_links` kwargs from `generate_npm_recipe_yaml`, `--inline-build` / `--no-inline-build` / `--with-build-bat` / `--no-bin-links` CLI flags, the `elif not inline_build:` branch in the conda-forge.yml emitter, the `if args.inline_build` extras-note line. Tests `test_npm_legacy_inline_build_false_emits_build_sh_and_cfy` + `test_npm_with_build_bat_opt_in` removed. `test_npm_url_and_filename_are_version_templated` renamed to `test_npm_source_url_is_version_templated`. `test_npm_inline_build` renamed to `test_npm_inline_build_default` and simplified. `test_npm_no_third_party_licenses_inline_build` renamed similarly. 44/44 tests pass (was 46; net -2 for the two deleted legacy tests). Generator output unchanged: regen of `recipes/bmalph` matches live byte-for-byte (modulo the `MAINTAINER` placeholder). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.1.

**v8.11.0** (Jun 2, 2026) — npm generator switches default to per-platform inline build (openspec PR #32368 + bmalph PR #33557 pattern). **MINOR bump** — behaviour change for all new npm recipes; legacy noarch:generic + standalone build.sh + tee Windows shim available via `--no-inline-build` (subsequently deleted in v8.11.1). Driven by bmalph PR #33557 CI failures that exposed two fundamental flaws in the v6+ "noarch:generic" canonical pattern: (1) rattler-build's symlink-portability check rejects the `bin/<cmd>` symlink that `npm install --global` creates on Unix because noarch:generic claims Windows compatibility where symlinks are non-portable; (2) staged-recipes CI builds noarch:generic on every platform, and without a `build.bat` the Windows leg runs nothing — no LICENSE staged → "No license files were copied" failure. The yo PR #33358 hit the same root cause (its `__unix`/`__win` virtual-package selectors are a different symptom of the same per-platform-vs-noarch tension). The merged openspec recipe (#32368) sidesteps both by dropping noarch:generic and using `build.script:` with `if: unix / then / else` branches — each platform's native `npm install --global` produces the right shape (Unix: symlinks-to-.js; Windows: native `.cmd` shims). Bmalph PR #33557's second attempt confirmed the pattern works cleanly on linux_64 + osx_64 + win_64 simultaneously (3m17s/6m14s/3m20s green CI). Six concrete changes in `scripts/recipe-generator.py`: (1) `_inline_build_script` rewritten to emit per-platform branches (`set -ex` + pnpm/npm sequence on Unix; `call <cmd>` + `if %ERRORLEVEL% neq 0 exit 1` after every step on Windows; tarball filename jinja-templated). (2) `generate_npm_recipe_yaml` default `inline_build=True` (was False); drops `noarch: generic` for ALL npm recipes when inline. (3) `requirements.host: nodejs` now emitted for inline-build recipes (matches openspec; needed for the test-env solver). (4) No standalone build.sh / build.bat / per-recipe conda-forge.yml in the default output. (5) `--inline-build` CLI flag rewired to `argparse.BooleanOptionalAction` with `default=True`. (6) Feedstock-mode conda-forge.yml drops `noarch_platforms` and `shellcheck.enabled`. 46/46 tests pass. Live verification: `recipe-generator.py npm bmalph` emits a recipe.yaml byte-for-byte identical to the CI-passing bmalph (modulo the `MAINTAINER` placeholder); no build.sh, no conda-forge.yml. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.11.0.

**v8.10.1** (Jun 2, 2026) — npm generator emits `${{ version }}` in `source.url` + `${PKG_VERSION}` in `build.sh` + quoted `${PREFIX}` in the tee command. **PATCH bump** — bug fixes; no template additions. Driven by user-reported feedback on `recipes/bmalph` (npm@2.11.0). Three coupled bugs in `scripts/recipe-generator.py`'s npm path: (1) `fetch_npm_info` set `source_url = tarball_url` literally — `v["dist"]["tarball"]` from the npm registry has the version baked in (`.../bmalph-2.11.0.tgz`). The autotick bot only mutates `context.version` and re-runs `calculate_hash` against the rendered URL; with a literal version in the URL, autotick would silently mint a recipe whose `context.version` advanced but whose source.url + sha256 still pointed at the previous tarball — a real functional bug. New helper `_template_npm_source_url(url, version)` rewrites the `-<version>.tgz` (or `v<version>.tar.gz` for `--source github`) suffix to `${{ version }}`. Falls back to literal URL for unrecognized shapes. (2) `_build_sh_template` + `_inline_build_script` emitted `${{SRC_DIR}}/{info.tarball_filename}` literally (e.g. `${SRC_DIR}/bmalph-2.11.0.tgz`). New helper `_template_npm_tarball_filename(filename, version)` rewrites the version suffix to `${PKG_VERSION}` (bash env var, injected by rattler-build into build scripts — not jinja). (3) SC2086 shellcheck issue exposed by [staged-recipes#33358](https://github.com/conda-forge/staged-recipes/pull/33358) reviewer feedback: `tee ${PREFIX}/bin/<name>.cmd << EOF` needs `${PREFIX}` quoted. Both `_build_sh_template` and `_inline_build_script` updated to emit `tee "${PREFIX}"/bin/...`. New test `test_npm_url_and_filename_are_version_templated`. 45/45 tests pass. Updated `recipes/bmalph/recipe.yaml` + `build.sh` to match (and rebuilt clean). Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.10.1. PyPI / CRAN / CPAN / LuaRocks paths not audited in this patch.

**v8.10.0** (May 26, 2026) — Drop `context.name` from Python v1 recipes; switch `package.name` and `source.url` to fully-literal form. **MINOR bump** — additive + corrective; matches what current grayskull emits and what conda-forge reviewers asked for on `recipes/xorq-datafusion` and `recipes/py-yaml12`. Three concrete changes in `scripts/recipe-generator.py`: (1) `_build_source_url_template()` rewritten to emit `https://pypi.org/packages/source/<first-letter>/<distribution-name>/<sdist-stem>-${{ version }}.tar.gz` — only `${{ version }}` interpolates; first letter, distribution name, and sdist filename stem are all literal. Drops the v8.9.1 `${{ name[0] }}` / `${{ name }}` / `${{ name | replace("-", "_") }}` chain entirely. (2) `generate_recipe_yaml()` (noarch path) drops `name:` from `context:`, switches `package.name:` from `${{ name | lower }}` to literal `info.name.lower()`. (3) `_generate_maturin_recipe_yaml()` does the same. (4) `generate_meta_yaml()` (v0 path) translates the v1 `${{ version }}` syntax in `info.source_url` down to v0 `{{ version }}` so meta.yaml renders correctly under conda-build jinja (closes a latent bug that surfaced once `info.source_url` carries v1 syntax). Three template updates: `templates/python/noarch-recipe.yaml`, `compiled-recipe.yaml`, `maturin-recipe.yaml` — all drop the `context.name` line, switch `package.name` to a `REPLACE_NAME` literal placeholder, and rewrite the URL to literal segments with `REPLACE_SDIST_STEM-${{ version }}`. SKILL.md updates: "PyPI `source.url` Must Use..." critical-constraint section rewritten to show the literal pattern as canonical; "Recipe Formats Quick Reference" v1 example block updated to match. Live verification: `recipe-generator.py pypi rich` emits `package.name: rich` + `source.url: .../r/rich/rich-${{ version }}.tar.gz` + no `context.name`; `recipe-generator.py pypi py-yaml12` emits `package.name: py-yaml12` + `.../p/py-yaml12/py_yaml12-${{ version }}.tar.gz`. 44/44 tests pass. Non-Python templates (Rust CLI, Go, R, etc.) and v0 meta.yaml templates intentionally untouched. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.10.0.

**v8.9.1** (May 25, 2026) — Two corrections on top of v8.9.0 (same-day PATCH). (1) Grayskull-style interpolated source URLs. `_build_source_url_template()` emits `https://pypi.org/packages/source/${{ name[0] }}/${{ name }}/<stem>-${{ version }}.tar.gz` where `<stem>` is `${{ name }}` / `${{ name | replace("-", "_") }}` / `${{ name | lower }}` / `${{ name | lower | replace("-", "_") }}` depending on how the sdist filename relates to the distribution name. v8.9.0 hardcoded literals — a regression from grayskull and from the previous py-yaml12 recipe. Also fixes a latent v8.9.0 bug: `fetch_pypi_info` was passing the templated URL (with `${{ ... }}` unrendered) to `_ensure_sdist_cached`, which broke maturin detection because the sdist download failed silently. Now tracks both concrete (for download) and templated (for recipe) URLs. **Subsequently superseded by v8.10.0** — the interpolated `${{ name[0] }}` / `${{ name }}` chain was undone five days later in favour of fully-literal URLs after live grayskull output + reviewer feedback diverged from the v8.9.1 codification. (2) CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_{STRIP, LTO} env vars in the maturin template. The conda-forge.org/.../rust page documents these as recommended for any Rust build, not just CLI binaries. v8.9.0 incorrectly excluded them based on empirical 27-PR adoption (3-7/27) — but the docs are **prescriptive**, not descriptive. The maturin template + `_generate_maturin_recipe_yaml` now emit `script.env` with both env vars; `cargo build` (invoked internally by maturin) inherits them and produces a stripped + LTO-optimized cdylib. Cargo-auditable was investigated and **skipped** — maturin uses `cargo build` not `cargo install`, so wiring it would require a `CARGO=cargo-auditable` wrapper not first-class supported by maturin. (3) py-yaml12 recipe updated to match the new generator output. Updated `config/skill-config.yaml` to 8.9.1.

**v8.9.0** (May 25, 2026) — Maturin/PyO3 generator routing + sdist-driven import-name extraction + abi3-gated `version_independent` + maturin template rewrite to the empirical phonors-pattern minimum. **MINOR bump**, additive + corrective. Driven by the `recipes/py-yaml12` build surfacing that `recipe-generator.py pypi <name>` produced an incorrect `noarch: python` recipe for a PyO3 package. Spec: `docs/specs/conda-forge-expert-v8.9.md`. Empirical sample: 52 Rust label PRs + 27 PyO3/maturin PRs (Mar 2020 – May 2026) + 30 pure-python PRs + 5 docs sources (added [conda-forge.org knowledge_base](https://conda-forge.org/docs/maintainer/knowledge_base/)).

### Key learnings landed in code

- **`cargo auditable install --locked --no-track --bins` is CLI Rust style** (93% of CLI sample; 0% in PyO3 sample). PyO3 packages should NOT include it.
- **Windows `CARGO_HOME` workaround is package-specific, not canonical** (0/25 CLI Rust + 1/27 PyO3 with documented git-checkout-depth justification). Maturin template no longer includes it.
- **CFEP-25 dual-version test matrix is a pure-python convention** (19/30 = 63% in pure-python; 1/27 = 4% in PyO3). The maturin template's `python_version` is opt-in commented, not default.
- **`version_independent: true` is conditional on Cargo.toml abi3 feature** (2/27 PyO3 use it, both with abi3 declared). Generator extracts the abi3 feature from sdist and emits `version_independent: true` only when present.
- **Import name lives in sdist's Cargo.toml + src/lib.rs `#[pymodule]`, not the PyPI distribution name** (G7 trap). py-yaml12 distribution → yaml12 import; microsoft-kiota-bundle → kiota_bundle; azure-identity-broker → azure.identity.broker.
- **Authoritative build backend lives in `pyproject.toml [build-system].requires`, not PyPI's `requires_dist`** (G2). Maturin's wheels-only delivery means `requires_dist` doesn't list maturin.

### Generator changes (`scripts/recipe-generator.py`)

1. **Sdist cache**: `_sdist_cache_path()` + `_ensure_sdist_cached()` — downloads sdist once per generator run under `/tmp/cfe-sdist-cache/`, air-gap safe (network failure → fall back to heuristics). Reuses `_http.auth_headers_for` for JFrog mirror auth.
2. **Import-name extraction**: `_extract_import_name_from_sdist()` — reads `Cargo.toml [lib] name` + cross-validates with `src/lib.rs #[pymodule] pub fn <X>()` for PyO3; falls back to shortest-`__init__.py` path for pure-Python. Closes G7.
3. **Abi3 detection**: `_extract_abi3_from_sdist()` — regex matches three Cargo.toml abi3 forms. Gates `version_independent: true` emission.
4. **Build-system extraction**: `_extract_build_system_requires_from_sdist()` — parses `pyproject.toml [build-system].requires` as the primary build-backend source.
5. **Entry-point extraction**: `_extract_entry_points_from_sdist()` — parses `[project.scripts]` (Wave D / S18 placeholder; not yet emitted into recipe — wired into `PackageInfo.entry_points` for future use).
6. **OS-marker classification**: `_classify_sys_platform_deps()` — maps `colorama ; sys_platform == 'win32'` to `{"win": ["colorama"]}`. Generator now emits `if: win / then:` selector blocks in the noarch path when markers are present (Wave D / S16; per knowledge_base virtual-package rule).
7. **Maturin route**: `generate_recipe_yaml()` checks `info.build_backend == "maturin"` first and delegates to **`_generate_maturin_recipe_yaml()`** — a compiled-extension recipe modelled on the phonors PR (modal 27-PR PyO3 pattern), with optional `version_independent: true` block, no `noarch: python`, Rust toolchain in build, maturin in host.

### Template changes

8. **`templates/python/maturin-recipe.yaml`** rewritten to phonors-pattern minimum (2-line script, no CFEP-25 matrix in tests, no Windows CARGO_HOME, no LTO/strip env; `version_independent` annotated as opt-in commented block). Header comment now carries empirical adoption percentages for each pattern.
9. **`templates/rust/cli-recipe.yaml`** — added the `provider: osx_arm64: azure` conda-forge.yml note next to the shell-completion block (per conda-forge.org Rust example page).

### Live verification

- `recipe-generator.py pypi py-yaml12` now emits a clean maturin recipe with import `yaml12` + `version_independent: true` (abi3 auto-detected from Cargo.toml) + 0 optimizer suggestions.
- `recipe-generator.py pypi rich` continues to emit a clean noarch recipe (no regression).
- `recipes/py-yaml12` builds 4 artifacts cleanly on Linux (py310/py311/py312/py313).

### What's NOT in v8.9.0 (deferred)

- `[project.scripts]` → `build.python.entry_points` recipe emission (Wave D / S18) — extraction helper is wired but the generator doesn't yet emit the block. Most CLI Python packages can hand-add it for now.
- `_can_noarch_python()` advisory validator (Wave D / S15) — implemented but not yet wired into the generator's main path. Available for future use.
- Sample-anchored doc header in noarch recipes (Wave D / S19) — already done for maturin path; not yet replicated to noarch.

**v8.8.0** (May 25, 2026) — Python recipe generator + template alignment with conda-forge canonical pure-python example. **MINOR bump**, additive + corrective. Deep-research pass: read [conda-forge.org/pure-python](https://conda-forge.org/docs/maintainer/example_recipes/pure-python/) + [rattler-build/python](https://rattler-build.prefix.dev/latest/tutorials/python/) + [rattler-build/rust](https://rattler-build.prefix.dev/latest/tutorials/rust/), validated against 30 fresh merged Python PRs + 27 Rust PRs from staged-recipes. Key meta-finding codified: conda-forge docs lead rattler-build tutorials by ~12 months on Rust patterns. Source-of-truth ranking from now on: **conda-forge docs > merged PRs > rattler-build tutorials**.

### Generator changes (`scripts/recipe-generator.py`)

1. **CFEP-25 dual-version test matrix** — `generate_recipe_yaml` now emits `python_version: [${{ python_min }}.*, "*"]` in `tests[].python`. Closes self-consistency gap where every generated recipe tripped TEST-002 in the same skill's own optimizer.

2. **Full `about:` block** — `description: |`, `repository`, `documentation` are now emitted when PyPI metadata exposes them. New `_extract_project_urls()` helper handles every spelling variation seen in the wild (`Repository`/`Source`/`Source Code`/`Code`, `Documentation`/`Docs`, `Homepage`/`Home`). PyPI's modern `project_urls` dict is preferred over legacy top-level `home_page`.

3. **Build-backend detection expanded** — `determine_build_backend()` now detects `pdm-backend` and `scikit-build-core` in addition to the existing hatchling / flit-core / poetry-core / maturin / setuptools fallback. `pdm-backend` was 1/30 in the Python PR sample (emerging); `scikit-build-core` is the modern default for C-extension projects.

4. **Conditional `python_min:` in context** — emit only when above the conda-forge floor (3.10). 26/30 sampled PRs omit it at the default since the May 2026 upstream sync moved the default into `conda-forge-pinning`.

5. **`python_min` floor clamp** — new `_resolve_python_min()` helper clamps the parsed `python_requires` to the conda-forge minimum 3.10. Pre-fix bug: rich's `python_requires>=3.9` produced an invalid recipe with `python_min: "3.9"`; now clamped to 3.10 (and per #4, omitted from context because at default).

6. **`generate_meta_yaml` mirror** — v0/meta.yaml generation now mirrors patterns #2, #4, #5 in jinja syntax (`{% set python_min %}` conditional, `description: |` block, `dev_url`/`doc_url` from project_urls).

### Template changes (`templates/python/*.yaml`)

7. **`noarch-recipe.yaml`** — drops `python_min: "3.10"` from `context:` (now relies on `conda-forge-pinning` default); replaced with explanatory comment.
8. **`noarch-recipe.yaml`** — `pdm-backend` and `scikit-build-core` added to the commented build-backend choices (with `scikit-build-core` annotated "for packages with compiled extensions").
9. **`compiled-recipe.yaml` + `maturin-recipe.yaml`** — audited; already correct (no `python_min` in context).

### SKILL.md edits

10. **Schema-header subsection (#9)** — softened to be empirically honest. 1/30 fresh merged PRs carry the comment; conda-forge reviewers do not block PRs that omit it. Documents that this is a **local-recipes repo convention** enforced by `tests/meta/test_recipe_yaml_schema_header.py` + the optimizer's `SCHEMA-001` check, specifically chosen so every recipe under `recipes/` benefits from editor schema validation.

11. **Rust Recipe Standards source-of-truth note (#10)** — explicit blockquote explaining that rattler-build's Rust tutorial shows plain `cargo install`; the `cargo auditable` + `--no-track` + `--bins` overlay is conda-forge style validated by 17/17 merged CLI Rust PRs.

### Adoption evidence (30 + 27 PR sample)

| Pattern | Conda-forge canonical | Generator pre-v8.8.0 | Generator post-v8.8.0 | PR adoption |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Schema header | not shown | ✓ | ✓ | 1/30 (local-only) |
| `schema_version: 1` | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | 14/30 |
| `noarch: python` | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | 28/30 |
| `pip install --no-build-isolation` | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | 24/30 |

### Live verification

`python recipe-generator.py pypi rich` (PyPI declares `python_requires>=3.9`) emits a clean recipe.yaml that:
- has the schema header on line 1, `schema_version: 1` on line 2;
- omits `python_min:` from `context:` (clamped to 3.10 = default);
- emits the CFEP-25 `python_version: [${{ python_min }}.*, "*"]` test matrix;
- emits `description: |` (falls back to summary when long_description is HTML/markdown);
- emits `documentation: https://rich.readthedocs.io/en/latest/` (auto-extracted from project_urls);
- correctly falls back to `setuptools` backend when no PEP 517 backend is declared.

### No recipe files in `recipes/` touched

This release is a generator + template + docs change. Existing recipes are unaffected; the next generated recipe is the first to benefit. No churn.

**v8.7.0** (May 25, 2026) — Rust recipe template refresh + universal schema-header enforcement. **MINOR bump**, additive only. Driven by a 21-PR sample of CLI Rust recipes merged to `conda-forge/staged-recipes` Apr–May 2026 plus the live [conda-forge.org/docs/maintainer/example_recipes/rust](https://conda-forge.org/docs/maintainer/example_recipes/rust/) page. Three Rust templates rewritten to the canonical 2026 pattern (`cargo auditable install --locked --no-track --bins`, unix/win `--root` split, `script.env`+`script.content` shape with `CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_STRIP: symbols` + `CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_LTO: fat`, both `cargo-bundle-licenses` + `cargo-auditable` in build deps); new `SCHEMA-001` optimizer check that flags any v1 recipe.yaml missing the `# yaml-language-server: $schema=...` header or `schema_version: 1` directive; two new SKILL.md Critical-Constraints subsections (schema-header invariant + Rust Recipe Standards). No behavior change for non-Rust recipes.

### Sample-driven evidence (21 merged PRs, Apr–May 2026)

Six PRs in first-pass sample + 15 in expanded sample. Adoption across the 17-PR CLI-Rust slice was 100% on every universal pattern; the 4 holdouts are pyo3/maturin Python extensions (cachebox, phonors, cocoindex — use pip install, not cargo install) and one Rust compiler (inko — nushell custom build script). Sample PRs reviewed: #33361 ljosbru · #33349 cachebox · #33343 goose · #33332 handlr-regex · #33311 cargo-leptos · #33286 phonors · #33276 html-to-markdown-cli · #33275 iwe · #33266 shh · #33248 cubic · #33247 rbw · #33231 cocoindex · #33225 hk · #33196 dora-rs · #33167 lune · #32971 simple-http-server · #32967 inko · #32931 agent-browser · #32919 mrtree-rs · #32914 phraze · #32911 comrak · #32907 cmakefmt · #32891 cargo-update.

### Changes

**1. `templates/rust/cli-recipe.yaml`** — full rewrite to canonical 2026 pattern:
- `cargo auditable install --locked --no-track --bins` (was: plain `cargo install --locked --root $PREFIX --path .`)
- Unix/Win install-root split (`${{ PREFIX }}` vs `%LIBRARY_PREFIX%`) — was missing
- `script.env`+`script.content` shape with `CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_STRIP: symbols` + `CARGO_PROFILE_RELEASE_LTO: fat` — was missing
- `cargo-auditable` added to build deps alongside existing `cargo-bundle-licenses`
- Tests use `package_contents` with `strict: true` and optional shell-completion `files:` block
- Shell-completion generation block included commented-out as opt-in (clap `completion --shell` or `COMPLETE=<shell>` env var styles both shown)
- Schema header included verbatim (the SCHEMA-001 invariant)

**2. `templates/rust/library-recipe.yaml`** — added the `script.env` for STRIP/LTO; kept the cdylib pattern (libraries use `cargo build --release` + manual artifact copy, not `cargo install`). Inline comments clarify the divergence from the CLI pattern.

**3. `templates/rust/cli-meta.yaml`** — meta.yaml v0 mirror of cli-recipe.yaml for legacy feedstocks. Uses `script_env:` list (v0's only env-injection mechanism — v0 lacks `script.env`+`content` separation). Auditable + no-track + bins + unix/win selectors via `# [unix]` / `# [win]` comments.

**4. New optimizer check `SCHEMA-001`** in `scripts/recipe_optimizer.py`:
- Flags any `recipe.yaml` (v1 file) that lacks the `# yaml-language-server: $schema=https://raw.githubusercontent.com/prefix-dev/recipe-format/main/schema.json` header.
- Also flags a v1 recipe.yaml missing `schema_version: 1`.
- Wired into `optimize_recipe()` in the critical-constraints batch alongside STD-001 + STD-002.
- v0 meta.yaml files are excluded (the prefix-dev schema is v1-only; meta.yaml uses Jinja2 + conda-build selectors).
- Confidence 1.0 — surfaces as an error, not a warning.

Generator coverage audit confirmed all 3 v1 generation paths in `recipe-generator.py` already emit both lines: PyPI/grayskull path (`generate_recipe_yaml`, f-string at line 255-256), rattler-generate path (`_run_rattler_generate`, `_ensure_yaml_language_server_header` at line 1350), and npm path (`generate_npm_recipe_yaml`, explicit at line 1079-1080). SCHEMA-001 closes the gap for user-edited / hand-migrated / template-copied recipes that bypass the generator.

**5. `SKILL.md`** — two new Critical-Constraints subsections:
- *"Every v1 Recipe Must Declare the Schema Header"* — documents the universal rule, points to SCHEMA-001 + the three generator paths.
- *"Rust Recipe Standards (CLI binaries — conda-forge 2026 canonical pattern)"* — enumerates the 5 universal patterns with their adoption rate (17/17), shows the canonical skeleton, and lists the 3 documented exceptions (pyo3/maturin extensions, cdylib libraries, custom-script projects).

Quarterly audit cron (`automation/quarterly-audit.prompt.md`) should flag any future drift in the upstream Rust example page so the templates stay aligned.

**v8.6.0** (May 24, 2026) — AppThreat Deep Signals: EPSS scores + CWE category rollup from external public catalogs, wired into Phase G + Phase G' overlay so cf_atlas operators can triage by exploitation-probability and severity-type instead of just by Critical/High count. **MINOR bump** — additive: 2 new fetcher CLIs (`fetch-epss`, `fetch-cwe-catalog`), 4 new `packages` columns surviving v25 cleanup (`vuln_max_epss_score`, `vuln_max_epss_percentile`, `vuln_cwe_top`, `vuln_cwe_categories_json`), 4 new CLI flags across existing scripts, persona-profile auto-runs. **Schema v23 → v24 → v25** (v24 provisioned for Waves B/C; v25 dropped the Wave-C-cancelled surface). 4 waves, 2 PRs already shipped to `origin/main` (commits `e4ba891cd2` Wave A, `e22c531ac2` Wave B); Wave C cancelled pre-implementation; Wave D = this commit.

Honest narrative — this release shipped two new signals + dropped two planned ones. The cancellations and the parent-spec corrections caught along the way are documented below rather than buried.

### Wave A (commit `e4ba891cd2`) — Schema v24 + EPSS pipeline foundation

- Schema bump v23 → v24 adds three side tables (`epss_scores`, `cwe_categories`, `package_hardening`) + 6 packages columns + 3 package_version_vulns columns. Migration is additive + idempotent; SCHEMA_DDL entries cover fresh DBs, ALTER ladder covers existing DBs. Caught one regression in `test_schema_migration_v19::test_rerun_is_noop` (SCHEMA_DDL was missing entries that the ALTER ladder added; fresh-DB-vs-post-migration column equality broke). Fixed by adding the new columns to both SCHEMA_DDL and the ladder.
- New `scripts/epss_fetcher.py` (~270 lines) + wrapper + `fetch-epss` pixi task. Pulls FIRST.org's daily CSV at `https://epss.empiricalsecurity.com/epss_scores-current.csv.gz`. **Parent-spec URL was stale** — said `cyentia.com`; verified actual canonical host is `empiricalsecurity.com` (Cyentia rebranded). Normalizes `percentile` from FIRST's 0.0-1.0 to stored 0.0-100.0 at upsert time to match CISA's published convention.
- New `_load_epss_scores(conn) -> dict[str, tuple[float, float]]` helper next to `_load_kev_cves`; graceful-degrade to `{}` on missing table.
- Live verification: 334,683 EPSS rows ingested in 5.1 s; 4,378 high-EPSS (≥0.7); top-10 are well-known actively-exploited CVEs (Citrix CVE-2023-23752, HTTP/2 Rapid Reset CVE-2023-44487, Jenkins CVE-2024-23897, Drupal CVE-2018-7600).
- 13 new unit tests covering `_normalize_percentile`, `_parse_snapshot_date`, `upsert_epss_rows` (insert/idempotent/update/malformed-skip), `_load_epss_scores` (missing/empty/populated), `main()` error-path.

### Wave B (commit `e22c531ac2`) — CWE catalog + Phase G/G' overlay wiring

- New `scripts/cwe_catalog_fetcher.py` (~270 lines) + wrapper + `fetch-cwe-catalog` pixi task. Pulls MITRE CWE Research Concepts view from `https://cwe.mitre.org/data/csv/1000.csv.zip`. **Parent-spec was wrong** about the file: said `2000.csv.zip` (Architectural Concepts); 1000 is the Research Concepts view this spec intends. 944 CWEs verified. CSV is BOM-tolerant via `utf-8-sig` decode (review finding); defensive CWE-ID prefix guard handles future double-prefix scenarios.
- New committed `data/cwe_categories_seed.json` maps 67 well-known CWEs to 7 cf_atlas categories (RCE / DoS / Info-Disclosure / Auth-Bypass / Memory-Safety / Traversal / Injection). Unmapped CWEs default to 'Other' at upsert.
- New `_load_cwe_categories(conn) -> dict[str, str]` helper + new `_aggregate_v8_6_0_overlays(affecting, epss_map, cwe_map)` pure function shared by Phase G + Phase G'. Tie-break for `cwe_top` is documented as first-encountered (matches Python `max` stability).
- Phase G + Phase G' overlay loops modified to load all three maps (KEV + EPSS + CWE) at run start and write 4 new columns per package (vuln_max_epss_score + percentile + cwe_top + cwe_categories_json). `_phase_g_sync_current_rollup` extension propagates the per-version columns to packages with **COALESCE-to-existing** pattern (review-finding fix — earlier draft clobbered Phase G's direct writes to NULL whenever Phase G' ran with stale epss_map).
- **Withdrawn-filter scope DROPPED** after verification: vdb's OSV source (`osv.py:91`) and GHSA source (`gha.py:184-185`) both skip withdrawn records at ingest. The proposed `vuln_total_active` / `vuln_withdrawn_count` columns shipped in Wave A's schema but stay NULL channel-wide — Wave D drops them in v25 cleanup. Documented at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/deferred-work.md` § parent-spec corrections.
- Live verification: 944 CWEs ingested in 1.03 s; 67 seeded + 877 → 'Other'. Channel-wide `PHASE_G_TTL_DAYS=0` Phase G rerun (32,144 rows in 37.8 s) surfaced 213 actionable packages with EPSS scores + 216 with CWE classifications. CWE distribution realistic for Python ecosystem: Info-Disclosure 133 / DoS 24 / RCE 21 / Other 18 / Injection 9 / Traversal 5 / Auth-Bypass 4 / Memory-Safety 2.
- 13 new tests for `cwe_catalog_fetcher` + 13 for the overlay-formula + rollup-sync extension.

### ~~Wave C — Phase T blint + Phase U EPSS overlay~~ — **CANCELLED 2026-05-23 (pre-implementation)**

Cancelled during `bmad-quick-dev` verification phase after low-signal-to-effort assessment:

- **Phase T (blint hardening)** — conda-forge's hermetic compile environment sets PIE / RELRO / stack-canary / NX via channel-wide global pinning. Per-package variance is minimal; even when a non-hardened binary surfaces, the actionable response is "file upstream issue and wait for a compiler-flag patch" — not a triage signal. Blint is genuinely useful for vendor-supplied binaries (Windows EXEs, distro packages); for conda-forge it would surface ~32k uniform answers at ~150 GB of download cost (admin top-N) or be limited to per-maintainer local-build snapshots. Verification also caught two parent-spec errors: PyPI package is `blint` not `owasp-blint` (404), and blint can't scan `.conda` archives directly (would need an extract preamble adding ~2× the LOC).
- **Phase U (EPSS overlay phase)** — redundant with Wave B's `_phase_g_sync_current_rollup` extension. The "pure-SQL backfill" wording in the parent spec conflated "rerun max-EPSS computation" with "re-fetch vdb data" — they're equivalent today because per-package CVE lists aren't stored. A genuine standalone Phase U would require a new `package_cves` table — separate spec, not v8.6.0.

Full cancellation rationale at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/deferred-work.md` § "Wave C cancellation". Schema columns provisioned in Wave A are dropped in this commit's v25 migration.

### Wave D (this commit) — Schema v25 cleanup + CLI flags + persona profiles + closeout

- **Schema v24 → v25 migration** — `DROP TABLE package_hardening` (+ 2 indexes); `DROP COLUMN packages.{vuln_total_active, vuln_withdrawn_count}`; `DROP COLUMN package_version_vulns.vuln_total_active`. SQLite ≥3.35 native `ALTER TABLE … DROP COLUMN` (verified: pixi env has 3.53.1). Migration is idempotent: guarded by `pragma_table_info` column-presence + `sqlite_master` table-presence checks. Live-tested against the production v24 atlas: dropped 3 columns + 1 table; EPSS + CWE columns preserved.
- **CLI flag additions**: `staleness-report --by-epss / --has-cwe <CAT>`; `my-feedstocks --epss --cwe` (appends per-row flags); `cve-watcher --epss-threshold <FLOAT>` (filters delta to packages with `vuln_max_epss_score >= threshold`); `detail-cf-atlas` auto-renders Max-EPSS + Top-CWE rows in the VDB Risk section when populated (no flag — always-on display when data present). **Dropped from the original spec per Wave C cancellation:** `--active-only` (no withdrawn data) + `--hardening` (no package_hardening data).
- **Persona profile auto-runs**: maintainer + admin profiles both set new env vars `BOOTSTRAP_FETCH_CISA_KEV` + `BOOTSTRAP_FETCH_EPSS` + `BOOTSTRAP_FETCH_CWE_CATALOG` to `1`. `bootstrap_data.main()` orchestration gains Steps 2a + 2b + 2c (between CVE DB and vdb refresh) gated on those env vars. Consumer profile skips all three (air-gap preserving). Dry-run verified against admin profile: all three steps land in the planned sequence.
- Honest CHANGELOG (this entry); skill-config 8.5.3 → 8.6.0; `reference/atlas-actionable-intelligence.md` catalog flips (2 rows: EPSS + CWE → ✅); SKILL.md atlas section reflects v25; CFE retro at `_bmad-output/projects/local-recipes/implementation-artifacts/retro-appthreat-deep-signals-2026-05-24.md`.

### Files touched (Wave D only — see commits `e4ba891cd2` + `e22c531ac2` for Waves A + B file lists)

- `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/scripts/conda_forge_atlas.py` — `SCHEMA_VERSION` 24 → 25; SCHEMA_DDL strip 3 column entries + `package_hardening` block + 2 indexes; ALTER ladder strip the 6+1 entries; new v24 → v25 cleanup block (idempotent DROP COLUMN / DROP TABLE / DROP INDEX)
- `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/scripts/staleness_report.py` — `query()` gains `by_epss=False, has_cwe=None`; argparse gains `--by-epss` + `--has-cwe` (8-category choice); SELECT pulls new columns
- `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/scripts/my_feedstocks.py` — `_SELECT_COLS` gains EPSS + CWE columns; `parse_args` gains `--epss` + `--cwe`; `render_portfolio` extended to print per-row EPSS / CWE flags
- `.claude/skills/conda-forge-expert/scripts/cve_watcher.py` — `query()` gains `epss_threshold=None`; argparse gains `--epss-threshold`; SQL gains an optional `vuln_max_epss_score >= ?` clause

The original v8.6.0 spec ruled out cdxgen / atom / dep-scan for the channel-wide phase pipeline. Verification at `CycloneDX/cdxgen lib/helpers/utils.js@9798-9920` (2026-05-23) showed cdxgen DOES support `pixi.lock` via `parsePixiLockFile` (emits proper `pkg:conda/<name>@<version>-<build>?os=<subdir>` purls) — the spec's earlier "no conda/pixi support" claim was wrong. Channel-wide use still ruled out (cf_atlas Phase B + J already supersede); per-workspace use filed as **DW17** — `scan_project --pixi-lock` mode, separate from v8.6.0.

**v8.5.3** (May 23, 2026) — Two independent atlas vulnerability-data fixes bundled, both surfaced by the 2026-05-23 channel-wide audit: DW13 (CISA KEV signal) and DW12 (rollup-staleness drift). **PATCH bump** — additive (new table + new helper + new pixi task) and a self-correcting SQL tail step; no API breaks, no behavior change for callers that don't touch the new `cisa_kev` table. **Schema v22 → v23.**

### DW13 — CISA Known Exploited Vulnerabilities catalog (Path C)

The original DW13 plan was to add the `aqua` source to `vdb-refresh` via `--cache-os`. A 33 GB download + crash later, the postmortem found that **appthreat-vulnerability-db's `aqua.py:30` hardcodes the `kevc` directory (CISA's KEV catalog inside the Aqua vuln-list) into `DEFAULT_IGNORE_SOURCE_PATTERNS`**. The include-override env vars (`VDB_INCLUDE_*`) only look up keys in `config.LINUX_DISTRO_VULN_LIST_PATHS`, which has no `kevc` entry — so there is no documented way to flip the default. Even a *successful* `--cache-os` run downloads ~33 GB of distro CVE data and **still** leaves `vuln_kev_affecting_current = 0` across the channel.

Path C bypasses vdb for KEV entirely. CISA publishes the catalog as a ~2 MB JSON feed at `https://www.cisa.gov/sites/default/files/feeds/known_exploited_vulnerabilities.json`; pulling it directly is 4-5 orders of magnitude smaller and immune to vdb's source-suppression default.

- New `cisa_kev` table (schema v23) — 13 columns + 3 indexes; cve_id PK so re-fetches are pure UPSERT. Free-text `knownRansomwareCampaignUse` mapped to tri-state `INTEGER` (`Known→1, Unknown→0, other→NULL` for future-proofing).
- New `scripts/cisa_kev_fetcher.py` (~250 lines) + `scripts/fetch_cisa_kev.py` wrapper + pixi task `fetch-cisa-kev` (three-place rule honored). Uses `_http.fetch_with_fallback` for retry semantics; idempotent INSERT OR REPLACE; `--dry-run` / `--json` / `--db` / `--timeout` flags.
- New `_load_kev_cves(conn)` helper in `conda_forge_atlas.py`. Phase G and Phase G' both call it once at run start and OR the result with vdb's per-CVE `kev` field: `sum(1 for v in affecting if v.get("kev") or v.get("id") in kev_cves)`. When the table is missing or empty, the formula degrades cleanly to vdb's native behavior (which is always 0 today — same as before the fix; no regression).
- Phase G + G' both print whether the overlay is active at run start (`KEV overlay active: 1,602 CISA-catalogued CVE IDs loaded`) or empty with a hint to run `fetch-cisa-kev`.
- `vdb-refresh` task reverted to `--cache` (was momentarily switched to `--cache-os` during the failed first attempt). Pixi task docstring now records the trap so future maintainers don't repeat the 33 GB experiment.

**Live verification:** `pixi run -e local-recipes fetch-cisa-kev` → **1,602 CVEs** loaded in **0.74 s** from CISA catalog version `2026.05.22` (released yesterday). 323 (~20%) flagged with known ransomware-campaign use.

### DW12 — `vuln_*_affecting_current` rollup-staleness drift

Caught by the same 2026-05-23 audit: the `packages.vuln_*_affecting_current` columns are written by Phase G against `latest_conda_version` at G-run time. When Phase B advances `latest_conda_version` on a subsequent run, the rollup goes stale until the next Phase G. The audit found 6 false positives (airflow, ibis-framework, jupyterlite-core, pytorch-cpu, starlette, strawberry-graphql) — atlas-stored counts flagged the feedstock as currently vulnerable but the live vdb scan saw the now-latest version was clean.

Fix landed two ways for defense in depth:

- **`_phase_g_sync_current_rollup` tail step** in `phase_g_prime_per_version_vulns` — pure-SQL UPDATE that re-derives the four rollup columns from `package_version_vulns` at the row's CURRENT `latest_conda_version`. O(N) idempotent; commits inside the same transaction as the per-version vuln writes so a partial run never leaves the rollup half-synced.
- **`v_current_version_vulns` SQL view** — query-time-correct alternative joining `package_version_vulns` to `packages.latest_conda_version` at SELECT time. New code should prefer the view; the rollup columns are retained for backward-compat and synced by the tail step so existing readers don't have to migrate.

### Reference + meta-DB hygiene

- `appthreat-vulnerability-db`'s `--cache-os` flag is a documented trap (looks correct, blows up to 33 GB, doesn't deliver KEV). The aqua.py ignore-list pattern (`kevc`, `oval`, `glad`, `mariner`, distros) is undocumented in vdb's README; the catalog of what `--cache-os` actually adds is `AquaSource — alpine-unfixed + everything in LINUX_DISTRO_VULN_LIST_PATHS not in IGNORE`. For conda-forge purposes, **none of those add useful signal** — they're OS-distro CVEs (RHEL/Debian/Ubuntu/Alpine) that don't map to conda-forge package coordinates. Keep `vdb-refresh` on `--cache` (OSV + GHSA only) for application CVEs and use `fetch-cisa-kev` for the KEV overlay.
- 33 GB of orphaned `data.vdb6` + `data.index.vdb6` from the crashed pull were deleted (`vdb.meta` was already stale-pointing at the pre-crash 893,580-record OSV+GHSA snapshot; the data files were inconsistent with their own metadata).
